[24 April 2025] Public comments on US AI Action Plan published:
The Office of Science and Technology Policy (OSTP) via the Networking and Information Technology Research and Development (NITRD) National Coordination Office (NCO) and the National Science Foundation, has published a total of 10,068 public responses that were received to the Request for Information on the development of an AI Action Plan. The comments touch on topics ranging from copyright to the environmental harms of AI data centres.

Copyright & IP
[23 April 2025] US President signs executive order to advance AI education:
US President Trump has signed an executive order establishing a comprehensive national initiative to advance AI education for American youth, aiming to ensure the United States maintains global leadership in AI. The order creates a White House Task Force on AI Education, chaired by the Director of the Office of Science and Technology Policy, and directs federal agencies—including the Departments of Education and Labor and the National Science Foundation—to prioritise AI literacy, teacher training, and workforce development. Key measures include promoting AI courses and certification opportunities for high school students, incentivising AI-related apprenticeships, encouraging public-private partnerships to expand K-12 AI resources, and launching a Presidential AI Challenge to highlight student and educator achievements. The directive emphasises early exposure to AI concepts, professional development for educators, and lifelong learning opportunities, all designed to prepare students and workers for an AI-driven economy and to foster innovation and critical thinking across the nation.

National Strategy
[16 April 2025] US Select Committee on CCP releases report on DeepSeek:
The US Select Committee on the Chinese Communist Party (CCP) has released a report on national security concerns presented by DeepSeek. The report includes findings that: (1) "DeepSeek funnels Americans’ data to the PRC through backend infrastructure connected to a US government-designated Chinese military company"; (2) "DeepSeek covertly manipulates the results it presents to align with CCP propaganda, as required by Chinese law"; (3) "It is highly likely that DeepSeek used unlawful model distillation techniques to create its model, stealing from leading US AI models"; and (4) "DeepSeek’s AI model appears to be powered by advanced chips provided by American semiconductor giant Nvidia and reportedly utilizes tens of thousands of chips that are currently restricted from export to the PRC". The report recommends the US government to take swift action to expand export controls, improve export control enforcement, and address risks from PRC AI models.

[14 April 2025] US Republican senators ask Trump administration to reject Biden-era AI Diffusion Rule:
US Senator Pete Ricketts (R-NE), Thom Tillis (R-NC), Markwayne Mullin (R-OK), Ted Budd (R-NC), Roger Wicker (R-MS), Eric Schmitt (R-MO), and Tommy Tuberville (R-AL) have sent a letter to US Commerce Secretary Howard Lutnick, calling for "immediate action" to repeal the Biden-era "AI Diffusion Rule" before it comes into effect on 15 May 2025 to restrict global access to AI chips. The letter argues that the AI Diffusion Rule will damage US leadership in AI.

Defense & National Security
[9 April 2025] NO FAKES Act re-introduced in US Senate:
US senators Chris Coons (D-DE), Marsha Blackburn (R-TN), Amy Klobuchar (D-MN) and Thom Tillis (R-NC) have reintroduced the NO FAKES (Nurture Originals, Foster Art, and Keep Entertainment Safe) Act alongside House of Representatives members María Elvira Salazar (R-FL-27), Madeleine Dean (D-PA-4), Nathaniel Moran (R-TX-1) and Becca Balint (D-VT-At Large) nearly a year after the bill was first introduced in July 2024. The bill would create a federal IP right to an individual’s voice and likeness. Entertainment organisations like SAG-AFTRA, the RIAA and the MPA had voiced their support of the bill last time, and the newly reintroduced bill has also drawn support from the likes of YouTube and OpenAI.

Generative AI
[3 April 2025] OMB memorandum on federal use of AI:
The Office of Management and Budget Administration (OMB) has released the replacement for OMB M-24-10 (now M-25-21), required under President Trump's Executive Order 14179. The new memorandum provides guidance on federal use of AI based on the three principles: (1) "agencies must remove barriers to innovation and provide best value for the taxpayer" (i.e. remove bureaucratic requirements, develop public AI strategy, maximise existing investments); (2) "agencies must empower AI leaders to accelerate responsible AI adoption" (i.e. set expectations for workforce on appropriate AI use, identify Chief AI Officers); and (3) "agencies must ensure their use of AI works for the American people" (i.e. implement minimum risk management practices for high impact AI).

Cybersecurity
[3 April 2025] OMB memorandum on driving efficient acquisition of AI in government:
The Office of Management and Budget Administration (OMB) has released memorandum M-25-22, as required under President Trump's Executive Order 14179. The new memorandum provides guidance on federal acquisition of AI systems, and sets out the following agency-level requirements: (1) update agency policies; (2) maximise the use of "American-made AI"; (3) protect privacy; (4) protect IP rights and use of government data; (5) spotlight AI acquisition authorities, approaches and vehicles; (6) contribute to a shared repository of best practices; and (7) determine necessary disclosures of AI use in the fulfillment of a government contract.

Generative AI
[2 April 2025] House Judiciary Subcommittee hearing on innovation and competition in AI:
The House Judiciary Subcommittee on the Administrative State, Regulatory Reform, and Antitrust has held a hearing titled "Artificial Intelligence: Examining Trends in Innovation and Competition" to examine critical issues affecting the competitive landscape within the AI sector. Republicans and Democrats both recognized the benefits of AI and that the technology is advancing at a fast clip, but disagreed on whether to lean toward less regulation or more regulation, similar to the EU AI Act. For example, Scott Fitzgerald (R-Wis) advocated for a free enterprise, open competition and 'light touch' regulatory approach, while Jerry Nadler (D-NY) suggested a strong, independent oversight by the Federal Trade Commission to protect consumers against unfair business practices.

Antitrust & Competition
[31 March 2025] CREATE AI Act re-introduced:
House of Representatives members Jay Obernolte (R-CA) and Don Beyer (D-VA) have introduced the draft text of the "Creating Resources for Every American To Experiment with Artificial Intelligence Act of 2025" (CREATE AI Act) (HR 2385), aimed at expanding access to AI research tools by establishing the National Artificial Intelligence Research Resource (NAIRR). This bill was reintroduced into the House of Representatives following a first attempt in 2023. For context, the NAIRR is a pilot program currently managed by the National Science Foundation that was launched in January 2024 and focuses on private sector collaborations to help democratize the computing and data training resources for researchers working with AI systems. It was initially mandated under former President Biden’s 2023 executive order on AI. This bill would seek to codify the NAIRR as a permanent institution within NSF to ensure its funding assistance can continue despite the repeal of Biden’s AI order under the Trump administration.

National Strategy
[26 March 2025] BIS expands export controls to cover additional 80 entities, notably to further restrict China's AI and advanced computing capabilities:
The US Department of Commerce’s Bureau of Industry and Security (BIS) has amended the Export Administration Regulations (EAR), expanding 'Entity List' to cover 80 additional entities (notably from China, the United Arab Emirates (UAE), South Africa, Iran, Taiwan) so that they will be subject to export restrictions and additional licensing requirements on certain sensitive US-made technologies. The update, issued under the Export Control Reform Act, applies to entities involved in advanced computing, AI, quantum technologies, and military-related research across multiple target jurisdictions and who may engage in activities deemed contrary to US national security and foreign policy interests. The stated objectives of this update include: (1) "Restrict the Chinese Communist Party’s (CCP) ability to acquire and develop high-performance and exascale computing capabilities, as well as quantum technologies, for military applications"; (2) "Impede China’s development of its hypersonic weapons program"; (3) "Prevent entities associated with the Test Flying Academy of South Africa (TFASA) from using U.S. items to train Chinese military forces"; (4) "Disrupt Iran’s procurement of unmanned aerial vehicles (UAVs) and related defense items"; and (5) "Impair the development of unsafeguarded nuclear activities and ballistic missile program".

Defense & National Security
[25 March 2025] Leveraging Artificial Intelligence to Streamline the Code of Federal Regulations Act introduced:
US senator Jon Husted (R-Ohio) has introduced a bill to streamline the Code of Federal Regulations (CFR) through the use of AI systems to identify redundant and outdated rules. Currently, the CFR is more than 180,000 pages long. The bill would give the Administrative Procedure Act an expedited process for undoing burdensome regulations, and it would ensure that AI systems are used to review the CFR annually.

[18 March 2025] US Vice President J.D. Vance delivers speech at American Dynamism Summit, reaffirming relaxed AI regulation:
At the third American Dynamism Summit in Washington DC, US Vice President J.D. Vance delivered a speech which, among other things, reaffirmed the Trump administration's policy for relaxed regulation of AI. Key statements include: (1) "For all major AI policy decisions coming from the federal government, the Trump Administration will guarantee American workers a seat at the table"; (2) industry and world leaders who are championing strict regulations on AI due to concerns over the technology are based "on a faulty premise"; and (3) "we over-regulated our industries instead of supporting them; we overtaxed our innovators instead of making it easier for them to build their great companies; and we made it way too hard to build things and invest things in the United States of America. That stopped two months ago and it will continue to stop".

Generative AI
[4 March 2025] US First Lady Melania Trump backs TAKE IT DOWN Act:
US First Lady Melania Trump has hosted a roundtable in support of the TAKE IT DOWN Act, a bill aimed at protecting individuals from deepfake and revenge pornography, which has passed the Senate but not yet the House of Representatives. Among other measures, the bill proposes to make it a federal crime to knowingly publish or threaten to publish non-consensual sexual images on online platforms. It explicitly includes realistic, computer-generated intimate images depicting identifiable individuals. The bill clarifies that consent to create an image does not equate to consent for its publication. The bill would also require tech and social media platforms to remove child sexual abuse material and non-consensual sexual images within 48 hours of being alerted by a victim. It is expected that with the First Lady's support, the bill will be accelerated as a "top priority" for House of Representatives to pass into law.

[21 February 2025] President Trump adopts memo on America First Investment Policy:
President Trump has adopted a memorandum on "America First Investment Policy”, which deals with foreign investment in high-impact sectors such as AI, semiconductors, and technological consumer goods. The memorandum outlines a policy that includes creating a fast-track process for investments from US allies, strengthening the role of the Committee on Foreign Investment in the United States (CFIUS) to restrict investments from adversaries in sensitive sectors (especially AI), reviewing outbound investment to China in sectors like AI, and ensuring US investment supports American growth rather than the military modernization of adversaries.

[11 February 2025] US and UK abstain from signing the Statement on Inclusive and Sustainable Artificial Intelligence for People and the Planet:
The UK and UK have abstained from signing a joint statement on Inclusive and Sustainable Artificial Intelligence for People and the Planet at the AI Action Summit in Paris. The statement sets out priorities including "ensuring AI is open, inclusive, transparent, ethical, safe, secure and trustworthy, taking into account international frameworks for all" and "making AI sustainable for people and the planet". The statement has been signed by 60 countries, including India, China, Japan, Canada, Brazil, France and Australia.

[11 February 2025] JD Vance warns against "excessive regulation" of AI at AI Action Summit in Paris:
At the AI Action Summit in Paris, US Vice President JD Vance delivered a keynote address advocating for a pro-innovation, deregulatory approach to AI and rejecting European-style "excessive regulations". Key quotes include: (1) "excessive regulation of the AI sector could kill a transformative industry just as it's taking off, and we'll make every effort to encourage pro-growth AI policies, and I'd like to see that deregulatory flavour making its way into a lot of the conversations at this conference."; and (2) "we feel very strongly that AI must remain free from ideological bias, and that American AI will not be co-opted into a tool for authoritarian censorship."

Defense & National Security
[6 February 2025] White House Seeks Public Comment on National AI Strategy:
The White House Office of Science and Technology Policy (OSTP) has launched a request for information on the Development of an AI Action Plan. This Plan, as directed by a Presidential Executive Order on January 23, 2025, will define the priority policy actions needed to "sustain and enhance America's AI dominance". In particular, the OSTP seeks input on policy actions that should be in the new AI Action Plan, including but not limited to: hardware and chips, data centers, energy consumption and efficiency, model development, open source development, application and use (either in the private sector or by government), explainability and assurance of AI model outputs, cybersecurity, data privacy and security throughout the lifecycle of AI system development and deployment (to include security against AI model attacks), risks, regulation and governance, technical and safety standards, national security and defense, research and development, education and workforce, innovation and competition, intellectual property, procurement, international collaboration, and export controls. The deadline for submissions is 15 March 2025.

[29 January 2025] Decoupling America’s Artificial Intelligence Capabilities from China Act introduced:
US Senator Hawley has introduced legislation titled "Decoupling America’s Artificial Intelligence Capabilities from China Act " which aims to (1) prohibit the import from or export to China of artificial intelligence technology; (2) prohibit US companies from conducting AI research in China or in cooperation with Chinese companies; and (3) prohibit US companies from investing money in Chinese AI development.

[28 January 2025] Trump to tariff chips made In Taiwan, targeting TSMC:
In his conference speech to the Republican Party in Florida, President Trump has stated, among other matters, that he is preparing to place tariffs beyond Chinese assembled electronics to computer chips made in Taiwan, warning the tariffs could reach as high as 100%. President Trump made specific reference to TSMC, expressing intentions to move TSMC's chip production back to the US (which used to be its base before it had moved to Taiwan). Chips & Data Centres
[23 January 2025] President Trump signs Executive Order to remove barriers to US leadership in AI:
President Trump has signed an Executive Order which calls for "removing barriers to American leadership in Artificial Intelligence". In particular, the order (1) sets out the new national policy "to sustain and enhance America’s global AI dominance in order to promote human flourishing, economic competitiveness, and national security"; (2) requires the Director of the Office of Management and Budget (OMB) along with other executives to develop and submit an action plan to achieve the above policy within 180 days; (3) requires all agencies to review, revise, suspend or rescind any existing policies, directives, regulations, orders and other actions that were taken under the now-revoked Executive Order 14110 that are now inconsistent with the above policy; and (4) requires the OMB to revise its OMB Memoranda M-24-10 and M-24-18 as necessary to make them consistent with the above policy.

The Stargate joint venture entity will start building out data centres and the electricity generation needed for the further development of AI in Texas.

Logistics & Infrastructure
[20 January 2025] Trump administration repeals Biden's executive order on AI:
President Trump has revoked Executive Order 14110 (Safe, Secure, and Trustworthy Development and Use of Artificial Intelligence) signed by the former President Joe Biden which required developers of AI systems that pose risks to US national security, the economy, public health or safety to share the results of safety tests with the US government, in line with the Defense Production Act, before they were released to the public. The order also directed agencies to set standards for that testing and address related chemical, biological, radiological, nuclear, and cybersecurity risks.

Defense & National Security
Cybersecurity
[15 January 2025] US AI Safety Institute issues updated guidelines for managing risk for dual-use foundation models:
The US AI Safety Institute (US AISI) at the National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) has released the second public draft of its guidelines on Managing Misuse Risk for Dual-Use Foundation Models (NIST AI 800-1), which outlines voluntary best practices for identifying, measuring, and mitigating risks to public safety and national security across the AI lifecycle. The updated guidelines include a number of improvements to the initial public draft (released July 2024), including updates such as (1) detailing best practices for model evaluations; (2) expanding domain-specific guidelines on cyber and chemical and biological risk; (3) underscoring a marginal risk framework; (4) addressing open models; and (5) managing risk across the AI supply chain. The comment period on these updated guidelines is open until 15 March 2025.

Generative AI
[14 January 2025] President Biden signs executive order to boost AI infrastructure development in the US:
US President Joe Biden has signed Executive Order to accelerate the development of data centers to enable AI, while also ensuring the new facilities are powered by emissions-free electricity. The order directs the US Department of Defense (DOD) and US Department of Energy (DOE) to lease federal sites to the private sector (via a competitive bid process) for building, owning and operating gigawatt-scale AI data centres and power generation facilities, and "to facilitate this infrastructure’s interconnection to the electric grid, fulfill permitting obligations expeditiously, and advance transmission development around federal sites."

Defense & National Security
[13 January 2025] US White House issues Interim Final Rule on AI diffusion export including controls on sales of AI chips:
The White House issued an Interim Final Rule on Artificial Intelligence Diffusion Export, including controls on sales and export of AI chips. The rule (1) prohibits access to chip exports for stated adversaries, including China, Russia, Iran, and North Korea, and caps exports to approximately 120 countries; (2) exempts 18 allied nations from these restrictions, including Australia, Canada, the United Kingdom, France, South Korea, and Japan; (3) include streamlined licensing that exempts low-risk chip orders with up to 1’700 GPUs from requiring export licenses and expediting shipments for research and healthcare uses; (4) allows trusted entities to obtain "Universal Verified End User" status to be able to deploy up to 7% of their global AI capacity internationally, or "National Verified End User (VEU)" status to be able to purchase up to 320’000 GPUs over two years; (5) limits Non-VEU entities in non-allied nations to a cap of 50’000 GPUs per country, though government-to-government agreements with aligned nations can double their chip quotas; and (6) establishes stringent security measures to protect sensitive AI model weights from being diverted for adversarial use.

[6 January 2025] US and India strengthen strategic technology partnership, covering AI:
The United States and India have issued a declaration to strengthen the existing US-India strategic technology partnership (launched since 2022), including cooperation on AI and quantum computing. Specific commitments included promoting reciprocal investments in AI technology, strengthening cooperation around national security applications of AI, and further cooperation in quantum science and technology.

[23 December 2024] Biden-Harris administration announce actions against China's trade practices in semiconductor sector:
The Biden-Harris administration has announced actions to secure and strengthen the US semiconductor supply chain. Among other items, the actions notably include (1) launching Trade Act Section 301 investigation into China's alleged unfair trade practices in the semiconductor sector, (2) prohibiting federal agencies from procuring chips from certain Chinese entities, and (3) issuing guidance for government procurement of domestic semiconductors.

Trump has stated that Sriram will work closely with the AI & Crypto Czar (David Sacks) to "focus on ensuring continued American leadership in AI, and help shape and coordinate AI policy across Government, including working with the President's Council of Advisors on Science and Technology." Defense & National Security
Cybersecurity
[17 December 2024] US House bipartisan AI taskforce delivers report, outlining detailed AI policy roadmap for Congress:
The House Task Force on Artificial Intelligence has released its sweeping end-of-year report, laying out 66 key findings and over 80 recommendations for US Congress on AI adoption, innovation and governance across 14 sectors, ranging from healthcare to national security to small businesses, and more. On the regulatory and legal front, the Report notably recommends (1) an “incremental” and “agile” approach to AI policy via sector-specific regulations (rather than an AI-specific law), with existing regulators/agencies to exercise their authority within their own domain but also draw upon a federal repository of AI resources (e.g. data, hardware, evaluations, etc); (2) on data privacy, support the development of and access to public datasets, privacy-enhancing technologies, privacy-by-design methods and synthetic data, as well as ensure privacy laws are generally applicable and technology neutral; (3) on intellectual property, clarify IP laws and agency guidance on AI authorship and inventorship, and establish identity-based rights and nationwide protections to appropriately counter the growing harm of AI-created deepfakes (while balancing free speech protections); (4) on content authenticity, have a “risk-based, multipronged approach” of evidence-based education programs, technical solutions, and policy solutions to harmful synthetic content; (5) open source models, their availability need not be restricted but Congress would need to establish mechanisms to monitor any risks that might arise from open-source models in the future; and (6) on government use of AI, require that agency policies include plain language notification and appeals processes for individuals or entities impacted by federal agency determinations that were substantively and meaningfully augmented by an AI system.

Copyright & IP
[11 December 2024] US House passes National Defence Authorisation Act into law, covering AI:
The House of Representatives has passed into law the National Defense Authorization Act (NDAA) for Fiscal Year 2025 (FY25). The FY25 NDAA authorizes funding for all discretionary military programs and activities – including personnel, operations, maintenance, procurement, research, and development. Notably, the 2025 NDAA (1) establishes two pilot programs to advance the department wide use of AI, including a five-year initiative to develop security-focused biotechnological applications and another to create AI-driven software for defense manufacturing facilities; and (2) directs the Pentagon to create policy on AI use in nuclear weapons systems.

Defense & National Security
Generative AI
[11 December 2024] US Senate passes TAKE IT DOWN Act, covering AI generated content:
The US Senate has unanimously passed the draft bill of the "Tools to Address Known Exploitation by Immobilizing Technological Deepfakes on Websites and Networks Act" (or the TAKE IT DOWN Act), sponsored by Senator Ted Cruz (R-Texas). This bill would require covered platforms to remove nonconsensual intimate visual depictions, and for other purposes. In particular, the bill: (1) criminalizes the publication or threat to publish non-consensual intimate images (NCII) in interstate commerce, making it unlawful to knowingly share or threaten to share NCII, including realistic computer-generated pornographic images depicting identifiable individuals, and clarifies that consent to create an image does not imply consent to its publication; (2) protects good faith efforts to assist victims by allowing disclosure of NCII to law enforcement or for medical treatment; (3) requires websites to remove NCII within 48 hours upon notice from the victim and make reasonable efforts to remove copies, with the FTC responsible for enforcement; and (4) protects lawful speech by narrowly targeting the criminalization of knowingly publishing NCII while adhering to First Amendment standards, requiring that computer-generated NCII pass a "reasonable person" test for realistic depiction. The bill now proceeds to the House of Representatives for approval.

US President-elect Donald Trump has said he would be appointing former PayPal Chief Operating Officer, David Sacks, as his "White House AI & Crypto Czar". Generative AI
[2 December 2024] US announce sweeping set of export controls on China relating to chip-manufacturing equipment, memory, and software:
The US Department of Commerce’s Bureau of Industry and Security (BIS) has announced a package of rules designed to further restrict China's capability to produce advanced-node semiconductors that can be used in the next generation advanced weapon systems and in AI and advanced computing, which have significant military applications. The new regulations prevent China from accessing 24 types of chip-manufacturing equipment and three software programs, and place restrictions on the sale to China of high-bandwidth memory (HBM), an advanced class of 3D-stacked computer memory component that is often used in customized AI chips.

It is rumoured at this stage that (1) an AI czar would not require Senate confirmation; and (2) the AI czar role could end up being combined with a "crypto czar" role, and be complementary to the agency chief AI officers established under President Biden’s AI executive order. Further details have yet to be revealed. No names have been put forth for consideration yet.

Defense & National Security
[25 November 2024] TRAIN Act introduced:
US Senator Peter Welch (D-Vt.), a member of the Senate Judiciary Committee, has introduced the Transparency and Responsibility for Artificial Intelligence Networks (TRAIN) Act, a new bill to help creators—musicians, artists, writers, and others—access the courts to protect their copyrighted works if and when they are used to train generative AI models. The TRAIN Act allows copyright holders to access training records used for AI models to determine if their work was used—a process currently used for internet piracy.

Copyright & IP
Generative AI
[20 November 2024] Taskforce formed to coordinate whole-of-government approach to AI safety:
The US Artificial Intelligence Safety Institute at the Department of Commerce’s National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) has announced the formation of the Testing Risks of AI for National Security (TRAINS) Taskforce, which brings together partners from across the US Government to identify, measure, and manage the emerging national security and public safety implications of rapidly evolving AI technology. This announcement comes as the United States is set to host the first-ever convening of the International Network of AI Safety Institutes in San Francisco. The Taskforce will enable coordinated research and testing of advanced AI models across critical national security and public safety domains, such as radiological and nuclear security, chemical and biological security, cybersecurity, critical infrastructure, conventional military capabilities, and more.

Cybersecurity
[16 November 2024] Biden and Xi discuss military AI:
At the sidelines of the 31st APEC Economic Leaders' Meeting (in Lima, Peru), US President Joe Biden and China President Xi Jinping met. Among other matters, the two leaders "affirmed the need to maintain human control over the decision to use nuclear weapons" and "stressed the need to consider carefully the potential risks and develop AI technology in the military field in a prudent and responsible manner" (White House Statement). It was not clear whether the statement would lead to further talks or action on the issue.

Agentic AI
[10 November 2024] US ordered TSMC to halt shipments to China of chips used in AI applications:
It has been reported that the US Department of Commerce has sent a letter to Taiwan Semiconductor Manufacturing Co (TSMC) imposing export restrictions on certain sophisticated chips, of 7 nanometer or more advanced designs, destined for China that power AI accelerator and graphics processing units (GPU). This order followed just weeks after TSMC notified the Commerce Department that one of its chips had been found in a Huawei AI processor.

Defense & National Security
[30 October 2024] US White House releases 1 year update on Executive Order for AI:
The White House has published a fact sheet highlighting the 1 year process since President Biden issued the landmark executive order on AI safety. The fact sheet has confirmed that federal agencies have completed on schedule each action that the Executive Order tasked for this past year - more than 100 in all.

Generative AI
Defense & National Security
Cybersecurity
[28 October 2024] US Treasury issues final rules restricting investments in key tech sectors (including semiconductor and AI) in "countries of concern" (e.g. China):
The US Department of the Treasury has issued final rules, implementing Executive Order 14105. From 2 January 2025, the final rules will prohibit anyone based from engaging in business dealings with persons of a "country of concern" (e.g. China) involving certain technologies that may contribute to the threat to US national security. Semiconductors and microelectronics, quantum information technologies, and AI systems of a certain threshold (e.g. computing power of greater than 10^24 computational operations) are covered under this rule. The final rules will also require US investors to notify the Treasury of investments in less advanced technologies that could still pose national security risks (e.g. AI systems under the prohibited threshold but trained with computing power greater than 10^23 computational operations).

Defense & National Security
[24 October 2024] White House issues sweeping memo to coordinate approach on AI for US national security:
US President Biden has issued the first-ever "National Security Memorandum (NSM) on Artificial Intelligence", which directs the US Government to implement concrete and impactful steps to (1) ensure that the US leads the world’s development of safe, secure, and trustworthy AI; (2) harness cutting-edge AI technologies to advance the US Government’s national security mission; and (3) advance international consensus and governance around AI. Notable items include (among other things): (i) a direction for the creation of a Framework to Advance AI Governance and Risk Management in National Security, providing guidance for AI use in national security missions; (ii) the establishment of the AI Safety Institute as the primary US government point of contact for private sector AI developers to facilitate voluntary pre- and post-deployment testing of frontier AI models for safety, security, and trustworthiness; (iii) a mandate for agencies like the Department of Energy and National Security Agency to develop capabilities for rapid systematic testing of AI models' capacity to generate or exacerbate nuclear, radiological, and cyber risks; (iv) a focus on promoting and securing the US' foundational AI capabilities, including efforts to strengthen the domestic semiconductor industry for AI chip production; (v) an emphasis on prioritising research on AI safety, security, and trustworthiness through partnerships with industry, academia, and civil society; and (vi) a call for revising hiring and retention policies to accelerate responsible AI adoption, including attracting experts from industry and academia.

Defense & National Security
Cybersecurity
[19 October 2024] US and ASEAN statement on promoting safe, secure and trustworthy AI:
At the 12th ASEAN-United States Summit in Vientiane, Laos, the US and ASEAN released a statement outlining 20 key initiatives aimed at enhancing the ASEAN-U.S. Comprehensive Strategic Partnership, focusing on AI governance, capacity building, and promoting safe and trustworthy AI systems. It emphasizes collaboration on digital economy frameworks, inclusivity in AI development, and the importance of cybersecurity and human rights. The commitments also include efforts to close digital divides and empower vulnerable communities, ensuring that the benefits of AI are accessible to all.

Data Privacy & Protection
[18 October 2024] Congressional leaders negotiating potential lame-duck deal to address AI concerns:
It has been reported that congressional leaders in the House and Senate are privately negotiating a deal to address increasing concerns about AI, and are hoping to move a bill during the lame-duck period. The specifics of the package are in flux as Democratic and Republican leadership debate over common ground. Several bills have passed through committees on a bipartisan basis related to AI research and workforce training bills, which could be prime areas for agreement. But other subjects like AI's role in misinformation, elections and national security are areas rife with potential partisan roadblocks and would likely be more difficult to include in a deal.

[15 October 2024] US considers capping advanced AI chips exports to some countries:
It has been reported that US officials have discussed limiting sales of advanced AI chips from NVIDIA, Intel, AMD and other US companies on a country-specific basis in the interests of national security, with a reported focus on Persian Gulf countries. Further details have yet to be revealed, but it is known that the idea has gained traction in recent weeks and deliberations are in early stages and remain fluid.

Defense & National Security
[3 October 2024] US and Poland sign Memorandum of Understanding on cybersecurity and emerging technology cooperation:
The US Department of Homeland Security (DHS) and the Polish Ministry of Digital Affairs (MDA) have signed a Memorandum of Understanding (MOU) to deepen collaboration in cybersecurity and emerging technology (including AI). Among other matters, the MOU highlights an explicit intent for future work related to the development of safe and secure AI.

Cybersecurity
Defense & National Security
[30 September 2024] US sets new rule that could spur AI chip shipments to the Middle East:
It has been reported that the US Commerce Department has unveiled a rule that could ease shipments of AI chips to data centers in the Middle East. For background, since October 2023, US exporters have been required to obtain licenses before shipping advanced chips to parts of the Middle East and Central Asia. Under the new rule, data centers will be able to apply for Validated End User status that will allow them to receive chips under a general authorization, rather than requiring their US suppliers to obtain individual licenses to ship to them.

Defense & National Security
[30 September 2024] US expands Validated End User program to cover data centres:
The US Bureau of Industry and Security (BIS) of the Department of Commerce has adopted a new order expanding the Validated End User (VEU) program to encompass data centers. Under this program, US exporters can now ship designated items to pre-approved entities under a general authorisation, streamlining the process and reducing the need for multiple individual export licenses. The program's vetting process ensures that only data centers committed to the highest security standards gain facilitated access to advanced US. technological innovation. According to the regulator, this action aims to bolster US national security and promote export control compliance within the realms of AI development, as well as the semiconductor industry.

Defense & National Security
[24 September 2024] Artificial Intelligence Civil Rights Act of 2024 (Bill No. S.5152) introduced:
Senator Edward J. Markey (D-Mass.), member of the Senate Committee on Commerce, Science and Transportation, has introduced the draft text of the Artificial Intelligence (AI) Civil Rights Act. The Act seeks to regulate AI algorithms used in decisions in various sectors including employment, banking, healthcare, criminal justice and public services. The Act applies to developers and deployers of such AI algorithms, prohibiting those that discriminate based on protected characteristics or cause disparate impacts. The Act mandates independent pre- and post-deployment audits to identify and mitigate bias, seeks to increase transparency by allowing individuals to appeal algorithmic decisions, and empowers the Federal Trade Commission, state attorneys general, and private individuals to enforce the Act.

Health & Life Sciences
[23 September 2024] US and UAE reaffirm cooperation on AI:
The US and United Arab Emirates have released a statement reaffirming their shared intention to promote cooperation in AI and related technologies. The US and UAE intend to closely collaborate to: (1) advance safe, secure and trustworthy AI; (2) align regulatory frameworks to strengthen innovation ecosystems; (3) promote ethical AI research and development; (4) broaden and deepen cooperation in AI protection and cybersecurity; (5) facilitate opportunities for trusted trade and investment; (6) talent development and exchange; (7) promote clean energy for the AI future; and (8) support AI for sustainable development in developing countries. The US and UAE will develop a government-to-government memorandum of understanding to build upon the above goals.

Cybersecurity
[20 September 2024] Global AI Research Agenda adopted:
The Department of State of the US has adopted the Global AI Research Agenda (GAIRA). The Agenda recommends principles, priorities, and practices for AI research and development (R&D) to advance safe, secure, and trustworthy development of AI systems in international contexts. It aims to strengthen collaboration in researching the interactions between individuals, communities, and society with AI systems, foster innovation, and support equitable access to the benefits of AI. The conclusions presented serve as a starting point to align a global research vision, in which research communities continuously assess the state of AI research, review current publications addressing the presented priorities, and identify gaps to guide future research, focusing on global needs.

Cybersecurity
[19 September 2024] US to convene international network of AI safety institutes in November 2024:
It has been reported that the Biden administration has announced a plan to convene an inaugural meeting of the International Network of AI Safety Institutes on 20-21 November 2024 in San Francisco, California (to be hosted by the US Commerce Secretary and Secretary of State). Inaugural members will include Australia, Canada, the European Union, France, Japan, Kenya, the Republic of Korea, Singapore, the United Kingdom, and the United States. The meeting will include technical experts from each member’s AI safety institute, or equivalent government-backed scientific office, to discuss priority work areas, and advance global collaboration and knowledge sharing on AI safety.

The hearing came as experts, officials and observers have sounded the alarm around the danger that deepfakes and AI-generated content could pose around the upcoming election. Further details and outcomes of the hearing have yet to be revealed.

[5 August 2024] The Unleashing AI Innovation in Financial Services Act introduced:
U.S. Senators Martin Heinrich (D-N.M.) and Mike Rounds (R-S.D.) have introduced the draft text of "The Unleashing AI Innovation in Financial Services Act" which establishes (1) regulatory guardrails at financial regulatory agencies for testing AI projects (i.e. regulated entities would apply through their primary regulator and must be able to demonstrate the project will serve the public interest (including consumer protection), enhance efficiency or increase competitiveness, and not present a systemic risk to the financial system), and (2) regulatory sandboxes for experimenting with new AI-driven financial products and services.

Sandbox
[1 August 2024] New US rule on foreign chip equipment exports to China to exempt some allies:
It has been reported that US President Joe Biden's administration plans to unveil a new rule that will expand US powers under the Foreign Direct Product Rule (FDPR) to stop exports of semiconductor manufacturing equipment from some foreign countries to Chinese chipmakers. For noting, under the FDPR, if a product was made using American technology, the US government has the power to stop it from being sold - including products made in a foreign country. Places whose exports would be affected by the proposed new rule would include Israel, Taiwan, Singapore and Malaysia. But shipments from allies that export key chipmaking equipment - including Japan, the Netherlands and South Korea - will be excluded.

Defense & National Security
[1 August 2024] US and Singapore deepen collaboration on critical technologies:
As part of the 2nd US-Singapore CET Dialogue, the US and Singapore have met again to deepen collaboration in various critical technology areas, including AI. Key points include (1) expanding National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) and Singapore Infocomm Media Development Authority (IMDA)'s governance and risk management frameworks to include generative AI; (2) collaborating on testing and evaluation, including aligning red-teaming guidelines and benchmarks; (3) supporting international standards, frameworks, and best practices for AI at bodies like ISO; (4) advancing AI safety through cooperation between US and Singapore AI Safety Institutes, with a meeting in September 2024; (5) exploring research collaboration between National Science Foundation (NSF) and AI Singapore (AISG) on responsible AI; (6) supporting inclusive AI development through a capacity-building program for Southeast Asian officials; (7) convening an NSF-funded workshop in Singapore to enhance collaboration in responsible AI research.

Cybersecurity
[31 July 2024] Formal bill of NO FAKES Act introduced, following initial discussion draft in October 2023:
U.S. Senators Chris Coons (D-Del.), Marsha Blackburn (R-Tenn.), Amy Klobuchar (D-Minn.), and Thom Tillis (R-N.C.) have introduced the formal bill of the "Nurture Originals, Foster Art, and Keep Entertainment Safe Act of 2024" (NO FAKES Act), which aims to protect the voice and visual likenesses of creators and individuals from the proliferation of digital replicas created without their consent. The introduction of the bill follows the October 2023 release of a discussion draft, an April 2024 Judiciary Subcommittee on Intellectual Property hearing, and extensive conversations with key stakeholders – all intended to improve and strengthen the bill.

[16 July 2024] Trump's allies draft order that aims to reverse Biden's executive order on AI:
It has been reported that The America First Policy Institute, a nonprofit led by Trump's former chief economic advisor and other ex Trump officials, has been drafting a sweeping AI executive order that would (1) launch a series of "Manhattan Projects" to develop AI technology for the military, and (2) reviewing "unnecessary and burdensome regulations", including the reversal of Biden's AI Executive Order. Note that this draft would not represent the official position of Trump, but could signal what kinds of AI policies a second Trump administration may pursue.

Defense & National Security
[11 July 2024] COPIED Act introduced:
Senate Commerce Committee Chair Maria Cantwell (D-Wash.), Sen. Marsha Blackburn (R-Tenn.) and Sen. Martin Heinrich (D-N.M.) introduced the draft text of the Content Origin Protection and Integrity from Edited and Deepfaked Media Act (COPIED Act), which would require platforms that develop or share AI systems and apps to allow users to attach "content provenance information" to their work within two years. Content provenance is defined as machine-readable information documenting the origin and history of a piece of digital content. The bill would prevent companies from using work with such labels to train an AI system or to create synthetic content without the users' consent and compensation.

[11 July 2024] US holds senate committee hearing into privacy and AI:
U.S. Senator Maria Cantwell (D-Wash.), Chair of the Senate Committee on Commerce, Science and Transportation convened a full committee hearing titled "The Need to Protect Americans’ Privacy and the AI Accelerant". This hearing explored how AI has accelerated the need for a federal comprehensive privacy law that protects individual privacy and sets clear guidelines for businesses as they develop and deploy AI systems.

Data Privacy & Protection
[8 July 2024] Senate panel to hold privacy-focused AI hearing:
The Senate Commerce Committee has announced it will hold a hearing on 11 July centered on privacy-related concerns stemming from the rise of AI. The hearing will examine how AI has "accelerated the need for a federal comprehensive privacy law," according to the committee announcement. The hearing was scheduled amid mounting pressure for Congress to put AI rules in place, as well as a comprehensive federal privacy law.

[1 July 2024] Validation and Evaluation for Trustworthy (VET) AI Bill to be introduced:
US Senator John Hickenlooper, Chair of the Senate Subcommittee on Consumer Protection, Product Safety, and Data Security, will introduce the draft bill of the Validation and Evaluation for Trustworthy (VET) AI Act. This bill aims to direct the National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) to work with federal agencies and stakeholders across industry, academia, and civil society to develop detailed specifications, guidelines, and recommendations for the certification of third-party evaluators to work with AI companies to provide robust independent external assurance and verification of their systems.

Cybersecurity
Generative AI
[22 June 2024] US closer to curbing investments in China's AI, tech sector:
It has been reported that the US Treasury Department has issued draft rules which aim to restrict and monitor US investments in China for AI, computer chips and quantum computing that could "threaten" US national security. The US previously proposed similar rules in August 2023 that put an onus on US individuals and companies to determine which transactions will be restricted or banned. Now the current draft rules would ban transactions in AI for certain end uses, and involving systems trained in using a specified quantity of computing power but would also require notification of transactions related to the development of AI systems or semiconductors not otherwise prohibited. Some exceptions would apply to publicly traded securities (e.g. index funds or mutual funds); certain limited partnership investments; buyouts of country-of-concern ownership; transactions between a US parent company and a majority-controlled subsidiary; binding commitments that pre-date the order; and certain syndicated debt financings. The US is on track to implement these rules by the end of 2024. Public comments on the proposed rules will be accepted until 4 August 2024.

[14 June 2024] House Republicans appear poised to fight AI regulation:
It has been reported that House Republicans showed resistance to supporting regulation for the AI industry during a closed-door meeting. They expressed concerns about stifling innovation and emphasized standing with innovators against what they perceive as Democrats' pursuit of government overreach on AI. They believe that minimal regulation has allowed US to dominate the technology industry and wish to maintain that advantage.

[11 June 2024] US weights more limits on China's access to chips needed for AI:
It has been reported that the US government is considering additional restrictions on China's access to advanced chip technology used in AI. The potential measures aim to limit China’s ability to utilise a cutting-edge chip architecture known as gate all-around (GAA) which enhances chip performance and reduces power consumption. The specifics of the proposed rules are still under discussion, and it is unclear when a final decision will be made.

Defense & National Security
[7 June 2024] Bill "HR 8668" introduced:
The Bill amending the Federal Election Campaign Act regarding transparency over AI-generated content (HR 8668) was introduced to the House of Representatives. The Bill will require political advertisements to include a statement within their content if generative AI was used to create any image, audio, or video footage.

[5 June 2024] US and Singapore share principles and collaboration on AI:
US Secretary of Commerce Raimondo and Singapore Minister for Communications and Information Josephine Teo co-led a Roundtable on AI with US and Singapore companies and government officials. The Roundtable underscored the importance of the close and long-standing relationship between the US and Singapore, which has grown to include close economic cooperation on digital issues. Key points include: (1) NIST and IMBA to continue to co-operate through the exchange of best practices and other information concerning AI governance frameworks, including NIST AI Risk Management Framework and IMDA's AI Verify; (2) the US AI Safety Institute and Singapore Digital Trust Center to plan important collaborations on advancing the science of AI safety; (3) Commerce and MCI to collaborate the support the responsible design, development, deployment, and evaluation of AI technologies; and (4) Commerce and IMDA to launch a new AI talent bridge program.

Cybersecurity
[21 May 2024] World leaders sign up to Seoul Declaration and Statement of Intent toward International Cooperation on AI Safety Science:
Australia, Canada, the European Union, France, Germany, Italy, Japan, the Republic of Korea, the Republic of Singapore, the United States of America and the United Kingdom signed the (1) Seoul Declaration for safe, innovative and inclusive AI; and (2) Seoul Statement of Intent toward International Cooperation on AI Safety Science. Together, these documents build upon the Bletchley Declaration, and aim to (a) promote safe, secure, and trustworthy AI development, (b) address global challenges and the protection of human rights, and (c) commit nations to create AI safety institutes and work together on AI safety science, sharing information about AI models, risks, and safety incidents.

[16 May 2024] Schumer and bipartisan group of senators unveil AI roadmap:
A bipartisan working group led by Senate Majority Leader Chuck Schumer (D-N.Y.) released a roadmap for AI policy in the US. Among other recommendations, the roadmap highlighted the following policy priorities of (1) ensuring enforcement of existing laws for AI; (2) addressing challenges posed by deepfakes related to election content and non-consensual intimate images; (3) establishing a strong comprehensive federal data privacy framework; and (4) mitigating the threat of potential long-term risk scenarios.

[16 May 2024] White House unveils critical steps to protect workers from risks of AI:
The White House has unveiled new principles relating to the development and deployment of AI systems in the workplace to protect workers from the risks of AI. These principles include: (1) centering worker empowerment; (2) ethically developing AI; (3) establishing AI governance and human oversight; (4) ensuring transparency in AI use; (5) protecting labor and employment rights; (6) using AI to enable workers; (7) supporting workers impacted by AI; (8) ensuring responsible use of worker data. Microsoft and Indeed have already committed to adopt these principles.

Data Privacy & Protection
[16 May 2024] Senate commits passage of three bipartisan AI and elections bills:
Senator Amy Klobuchar, Chairwoman of the Senate Committee on Rules and Administration, announced the passage of three bipartisan bills addressing the impact of AI on federal elections. The bills include the (1) Protect Elections from Deceptive AI Act (which aims to combat misleading AI-generated content in elections), (2) AI Transparency in Elections Act (which focuses on ensuring transparency in the use of AI in election processes), and (3) Preparing Election Administrators for AI Act (which seeks to equip election administrators with the necessary tools and knowledge to handle AI-related challenges).

National Strategy
[9 May 2024] ENFORCE Act introduced:
The "Enhancing National Frameworks for Overseas Restriction of Critical Exports Act" (ENFORCE Act/HR 8315) was introduced in the US House of Representatives. The ENFORCE Act amends the Export Control Reform Act of 2018 to prevent foreign adversaries from exploiting US artificial intelligence (AI) and other enabling technologies. In particular, it would establish a licensing requirement for US persons to export, re-export, or in-country transfer of certain items. Other activities that may support these items regarding the design, development, production, use, and operation are subject to the licensing requirement as well.

[7 May 2024] Comment Integrity and Management Act passes in House:
Bill H.R. 7528, the Comment Integrity and Management Act of 2024, has passed the US House of Representatives. The Act provides federal agencies with the flexibility and tools necessary to efficiently manage public comments, including the authority to identify and process whether mass comments received are either computer-generated or from an individual.

Cybersecurity
[1 May 2024] Secure Artificial Intelligence Act introduced:
Senators Mark R. Warner and Thom Tillis have put forth the "Secure Artificial Intelligence Act of 2024". The bill's objectives are: (1) to mandate updates to the National Vulnerability Database and the Common Vulnerabilities and Exposures Program, (2) to establish a public database for voluntary reporting of AI security incidents, (3) to encourage the development and adoption of best practices addressing supply chain risks in AI, and (4) to set up an AI Security Center at the NSA for research, guidance, and to promote secure AI adoption.

US federal agencies have completed all 180-day actions in Executive Order 14110 (i.e. the Executive Order on Safe, Secure and Trustworthy AI).

Cybersecurity
[18 April 2024] Future of Artificial Intelligence Innovation Act introduced:
US senators Maria Cantwell (D-Wash.), Chair of the Senate Committee on Commerce, Science and Transportation, and U.S. Senators Todd Young (R-Ind.), John Hickenlooper (D-Colo.), and Marsha Blackburn (R-Tenn.), members of the Commerce Committee, introduced the draft text of the 'Future of AI Innovation Act'. This bill proposes to (1) authorise the NIST AI Safety Institute to develop AI standards; (2) create new AI testbeds with national laboratories to evaluate AI models and develop security risk tools; (3) create grand challenge prize competitions to spur private sector AI solutions and innovation; (4) direct federal science agencies to make curated datasets available for public use to accelerate AI innovation; and (5) create international alliances on AI standards, research and development.

Generative AI
Cybersecurity
[16 April 2024] Child Exploitation and Artificial Intelligence Expert Commission Act introduced:
Congressman N Langworthy has introduced the draft text of the Child Exploitation and Artificial Intelligence Expert Commission Act in the House of Representatives. This legislation would establish a commission to develop a legal framework that will assist law enforcement in preventing, detecting, and prosecuting AI-generated crimes against children. Specifically, it would: (1) investigate and assess how AI may be used to commit a child exploitation crime; (2) evaluate the ability to prevent, detect, and prosecute a child exploitation crime committed using AI under the law in effect during the period of the evaluation of the Commission; and (3) analyse the efficacy of the current legal framework to charge individuals suspected of using AI to create child sexual abuse material and recommend changes to the current statute.

[9 April 2024] Generative AI Copyright Disclosure Act introduced:
House of Representative member Adam Schiff introduced the draft bill of the Generative AI Copyright Disclosure Act which would require a person to submit prior notice to the Register of Copyrights when releasing a generative AI system trained on copyrighted material. A public database of these notices will be established by the Register.

Copyright & IP
[5 April 2024] US-EU Trade and Technology Council joint statement including commitment to a risk-based approach to AI:
The US and the EU, following the sixth ministerial meeting of the TTC (Transatlantic Technology and Trade Council), issued a joint statement including a commitment to a risk-based approach to AI to ensure its safe, secure, and trustworthy development. Key points include (1) continued bilateral and joint participation in international organisations such as G7, OECD, and UN processes; (2) endorsed the Hiroshima Process International Code of Conduct for AI developers; (3) the EU AI Office and US AI Safety Institute to exchange information on their regulatory approaches and agree to establish a dialogue to expand their collaboration further; (4) implementing the Joint Roadmap on Evaluation and Measurement Tools for Trustworthy AI and Risk Management, aiming to establish interoperable international standards.

[1 April 2024] US and UK announce partnership on science of AI safety:
The US and UK AI Safety Institutes have signed a Memorandum of Understanding to collaborate on research, safety evaluations, and guidance for AI safety. They aim to develop shared capabilities through information-sharing, close cooperation, and expert personnel exchanges. The partnership will focus on developing tests for advanced AI models and building a common approach to AI safety testing.

Generative AI
[30 March 2024] US updates export curbs on AI chips and tools to China:
The Biden administration has revised rules aimed at making it harder for China to access US AI chips and chipmaking tools, part of an effort to stifle China's chipmaking industry over national security concerns. The new rules clarify, among other things, that restrictions on chip shipments to China also apply to laptops containing those chips.

Defense & National Security
[28 March 2024] OMB's first government wide policy to mitigate risks of AI:
The White House Office of Management and Budget (OMB) has issued its first government-wide policy which directs federal agencies: (1) to implement concrete safeguards around AI; (2) to improve public transparency in their use of AI; and (3) to designate Chief AI Officers, establish AI governance boards. The OMB will also remove unnecessary barriers to responsible AI innovation; issue a request for information on responsible procurement of AI in government; and direct agencies to expand and upskill their AI talent (including a commitment from the Biden Administration to hire 100 AI professionals by summer 2024).

Cybersecurity
[21 March 2024] Protecting Consumers from Deceptive AI Act introduced:
US Congresswoman Anna G. Eshoo, Co-Chair of the House AI Caucus, and US Congressman Neal Dunn, both members of the bipartisan Task Force on AI, introduced the  'Protecting Consumers from Deceptive AI Act' in the House of Representatives. The Act aims to addresses risks of deepfakes by directing the development of standards for identifying and labelling AI-generated content and requiring generative AI developers and online content platforms to provide disclosures on AI-generated content.

Online Safety & Child Protection
[19 March 2024] AI CONSENT Act introduced:
US senators (Ben Ray Luján and Peter Welch) introduced the draft bill of the "Artificial Intelligence Consumer Opt-In, Notification Standards, and Ethical Norms for Training Act" (the AI CONSENT Act). This bill that would require covered entities to obtain consumers' "express informed consent" before using their personal data (known as "covered data") to train AI models. Failure to do so would be considered an unfair or deceptive practice, subject to Federal Trade Commission (FTC) enforcement. The bill also directs the FTC to study the efficacy of data de-identification (e.g. anonymising data).

Data Privacy & Protection
Generative AI
[13 March 2024] US introduces draft UN resolution on AI:
The US has introduced a draft resolution at the United Nations promoting "safe, secure and trustworthy" AI systems. It calls for "effective safeguards for the use of AI, including physical and security systems and risk management. The draft also "encourages the private sector to adhere to applicable international and domestic laws". The resolution, which is co-sponsored by more than 50 nations, would be nonbinding.

Generative AI
Cybersecurity
Data Privacy & Protection
[5 March 2024] Federal AI Governance and Transparency Act introduced:
House Committee on Oversight and Accountability Chairman James Comer and Ranking Member Jamie Raskin introduced the Federal AI Governance and Transparency Act (HR 7532) in the House of Representatives. The Act will govern the design, development, acquisition, use, management, and oversight of AI in the US federal government. Key provisions include (1) defining federal standards for responsible AI use; (2) strengthening government-wide federal AI use policy authority and requirements; (3) establishing agency AI governance charters; (4) creating additional public accountability measures; (5) repealing repetitive law (including the AI in Government Act 2020 and Advancing American AI Act 2022); and (6) harmonizes with existing law.

Filter Categories...
[6 May 2026] Google DeepMind, Microsoft, and xAI sign agreements with US CAISI on AI security testing:
The Center for AI Standards and Innovation (CAISI) at the Department of Commerce’s National Institute of Standards and Technology has announced new agreements with Google DeepMind, Microsoft, and xAI to conduct pre-deployment evaluations and targeted research on frontier AI capabilities to enhance AI security. These collaborations, guided by Secretary Howard Lutnick and aligned with America’s AI Action Plan, position CAISI as the primary U.S. government contact for testing and research on commercial AI systems. CAISI has completed over 40 evaluations, including on unreleased models, and emphasizes the importance of independent measurement science for understanding AI's national security implications. The agreements facilitate information-sharing, voluntary product improvements, and government understanding of AI capabilities, while allowing developers to submit models with reduced safeguards for thorough evaluations. The CAISI-convened TRAINS Taskforce, comprising interagency experts, regularly contributes feedback, and the agreements are designed to support testing in classified environments and adapt to ongoing AI advancements.

Defense & Security
[1 May 2026] US DoD announces agreements with frontier AI companies:
The U.S. Department of War has entered into agreements with seven leading artificial intelligence companies—SpaceX, OpenAI, Google, NVIDIA, Reflection, Microsoft, and Amazon Web Services—to deploy their advanced AI capabilities on the Department's classified networks for lawful operational use. These agreements aim to transform the U.S. military into an AI-first fighting force, enhancing decision-making across all warfare domains by integrating AI into Impact Level 6 (IL6) and Impact Level 7 (IL7) network environments to streamline data synthesis and improve situational understanding. This initiative supports the Department's AI Acceleration Strategy, enabling new capabilities in warfighting, intelligence, and enterprise operations while preventing AI vendor lock-in and ensuring long-term flexibility for the Joint Force.

Defense & Security
[30 April 2026] Google signs AI deal with US Pentagon:
It is reported that Google has signed an agreement with the US Department of Defense to provide its AI models for classified use, joining other firms like OpenAI and xAI. This deal allows the Pentagon to utilize Google's AI for any lawful government purpose while incorporating safety filters and explicitly prohibiting the use of AI for domestic surveillance or autonomous weapons without human oversight. The Pentagon has previously encouraged AI companies to relax restrictions on their tools for classified networks, with agreements potentially worth up to $200 million each. It is reported that Google is required to assist in adjusting AI safety settings at the government's request but retains no control over lawful operational decisions.

[29 April 2026] US debates partisan issues in AI cost and interstate transmission:
The U.S. House Committee on Energy and Commerce has held a hearing on titled 'Meeting Growing Power Demand While Protecting Ratepayers,' to discuss legislative solutions for the increased electricity demand from AI data centers, with Chairman Bob Latta highlighting the importance of reliable and affordable energy for U.S. AI leadership; the hearing addressed the need to balance power infrastructure expansion with consumer protection against rate increases, focusing on interstate electricity transmission cost allocation and the effects of AI-related energy consumption on the national grid, while exploring policy options to prevent the financial burden of grid upgrades from disproportionately impacting residential and small business customers.

Energy & Environment
[24 April 2026] Justice Department Intervenes in xAI lawsuit challenging Colorado’s ‘Algorithmic Discrimination’ Law:
The US Department of Justice has filed a complaint in intervention in the US District Court for the District of Colorado regarding a lawsuit by X.AI LLC against the Colorado Attorney General, challenging the constitutionality of Colorado's Consumer Protections for Artificial Intelligence Act (SB24-205), enacted in May 2024 and effective from June 30, 2026. This law mandates that developers and deployers of high-risk AI systems, which impact Colorado residents in various sectors, take measures to prevent algorithmic discrimination based on protected characteristics. Compliance requirements include annual assessments and disclosures, while the law excludes AI aimed solely at increasing diversity or addressing historical discrimination. The Justice Department raises two constitutional objections under the Equal Protection Clause, arguing that the law's requirements compel race, sex, and religion-conscious adjustments to AI models without judicial findings of discrimination, and that its exemption for diversity-focused AI constitutes intentional differential treatment lacking evidence of prior discrimination in the AI field. The Department seeks a declaration of unconstitutionality for SB24-205 and a permanent injunction against its enforcement.

[16 April 2026] Senator Hassan Presses Leading AI Voice Cloning Companies to Prevent Exploitation by Scammers:
US Senator Maggie Hassan (D-NH) has pressed leading AI voice cloning companies ElevenLabs, LOVO, Speechify, and VEED to enhance measures against the exploitation of their products by scammers, following an FBI report indicating that AI-related scams resulted in $893 million in losses in 2025. As Ranking Member of the Joint Economic Committee, Senator Hassan (1) highlighted the increasing use of AI voice-generating tools by global criminal networks to create deepfake materials for personalized scams, including impersonations of public figures and loved ones; (2) emphasized the need for collaboration between public and private sectors to combat these scams, citing investigations revealing inadequate safeguards against nonconsensual voice cloning among popular AI platforms; and (3) referenced specific cases, including a New York man's sentencing for a grandparent scam that utilized AI to mimic voices, and ongoing investigations into the roles of AI companies and other entities in protecting Americans from fraud.

[10 April 2026] Department of Commerce launches call for proposals on AI exports program:
The US Department of Commerce has launched a Call for Proposals for the American AI Exports Program, effective 1 April 2026, inviting US companies to form industry-led consortia to submit proposals for delivering full-stack US AI technology packages to international partners, with applications accepted until 30 June 2026. These packages should be structured as integrated offerings that provide products or services for foreign markets that include the following AI stack layers: AI-optimized hardware, data pipelines and labeling systems, AI models and systems, security and cybersecurity measures for AI models and systems, and AI applications for sector-specific or functional use cases. This initiative aligns with President Trump's Executive Order aimed at expanding the global deployment of secure American AI technologies, promoting economic and national security, and strengthening ties with allies.

[9 April 2026] US defense official overseeing AI reaped millions selling xAI stock after Pentagon entered agreement with company:

This stake, initially valued between $500,000 and $1 million when he joined the department, appreciated significantly following the Pentagon's agreement with xAI to integrate its AI capabilities into military systems. Defense & Security
[8 April 2026] Anthropic denied emergency stay of DoW supply chain risk designation:
The US Court of Appeals for the DC Circuit has denied Anthropic's motion for an emergency stay against the Department of War's designation of the company as a supply chain risk. The court determined that the balance of equities favoured the government, reasoning that “[o]n one side is a relatively contained risk of financial harm to a single private company" and "[o]n the other side is judicial management of how, and through whom, the Department of War secures vital AI technology during an active military conflict". Further, the judges suggested Anthropic actually benefited financially given the surge in app store downloads amid its rift with the Pentagon. The case was expedited with oral arguments scheduled for 19 May 2026. This decision contrasts with a previous ruling by a California federal judge that temporarily blocked the designation.

[31 March 2026] SEC focuses on AI oversight and governance:
It is reported that the US Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) has intensified its focus on AI oversight and governance, recognizing the transformative potential of AI in financial markets. In August 2025, the SEC established an AI Task Force to centralize efforts, remove barriers to progress, and implement AI solutions that enhance the agency's mission. Additionally, the SEC appointed a Chief Artificial Intelligence Officer to lead AI innovation and ensure compliance with relevant guidelines. The SEC's Investor Advisory Committee has recommended that issuers define 'Artificial Intelligence,' disclose board oversight mechanisms for AI deployment, and report on AI's material effects on internal operations and consumer-facing matters.

[27 March 2026] Top AI conference reverses ban on papers from US-sanctioned entities after Chinese boycott:
It is reported that the Conference on Neural Information Processing Systems (NeurIPS) has reversed a policy change that would have banned papers from researchers at entities under US sanctions, following a boycott from China's largest federation for technology professionals, the China Association for Science and Technology (CAST). Initially, NeurIPS announced the policy to comply with U.S. law, expanding previous restrictions that only targeted entities on the U.S. Treasury's Specially Designated Nationals List. The announcement caused significant backlash in China amid an ongoing AI competition with the U.S., prompting CAST to halt funding applications for members wishing to attend NeurIPS and redirect them to other conferences. NeurIPS later clarified that the restrictions were issued in error due to miscommunication with its legal team and apologized for the confusion, stating that the updated policy would only restrict submissions from those on the SDN list.

[26 March 2026] FTC chairman warns of 'serious trouble' if US doesn't dominate AI space:
It is reported that the Federal Trade Commission (FTC) has been actively monitoring the AI sector to ensure robust competition and prevent market consolidation. Chairman Andrew Ferguson has emphasized the importance of cautious regulatory approaches, warning against 'knee-jerk' reactions that could stifle innovation. Commissioner Melissa Holyoak highlighted potential risks of market consolidation due to high fixed costs and network effects, which could lead to dominance by a few firms and raise national security concerns. The FTC supports open AI models to foster innovation and competition but remains vigilant about potential anticompetitive practices and deceptive claims in AI advertising. Additionally, the agency is attentive to the risks AI technologies may pose to children, advocating for protective measures while cautioning against overregulation.

[23 March 2026] US Senator Warren launches probe of Defense dealings with Anthropic, OpenAI:

The defendants allegedly used a front company to acquire NVIDIA Graphics Processing Units (GPUs) with AI applications, which they then attempted to smuggle to China without the required export licenses. The scheme involved falsifying shipping documents and routing the shipments through third countries to evade U.S. export controls. The indictment also seeks the forfeiture of 50 NVIDIA H200 GPUs intended for illegal export.

[19 March 2026] Senate requests information from NVIDIA on AI semiconductor competition concerns:
United States Senators have sent a letter to NVIDIA Corporation CEO regarding NVIDIA's December 2025 agreement with Groq, an AI chip company, expressing concerns about competition in the AI semiconductor sector. For background, on 24 December 2025, NVIDIA announced a $20 billion agreement to acquire a non-exclusive license for Groq's inference chip design technology and hire key Groq employees, including its CEO and president. The Senators are worried that this agreement, which transfers most of Groq's assets without a formal acquisition, may be structured to evade antitrust scrutiny and could further entrench NVIDIA's dominant 90% market share in the high-end data center GPU market, thereby reducing competitive pressure in the inference chip sector. They have requested detailed information on the agreement's structure, asset transfers, and workforce changes by 3 April 2026.

[14 March 2026] US Commerce Department withdraws planned rule on AI chip exports:
It is reported that the US Commerce Department has withdrawn a planned rule on AI chip exports, marking a reversal by the Trump administration in its strategy to secure American leadership in AI. No explanation was given for the withdrawal. The draft rule, intended to replace a Biden-era regulation on global access to AI chips, was circulated for feedback but was ultimately pulled, with officials stating it was always a preliminary draft. The proposed rule had suggested requiring foreign investments in US data centers or security guarantees for exporting large quantities of chips, contrasting sharply with the Biden administration's tiered approach to chip distribution based on geopolitical considerations. The withdrawal reflects internal disagreements within the Trump administration regarding the best path to achieving global AI supremacy while addressing national security concerns.
