[9 March 2026] Anthropic sues US government for calling it a risk:
It is reported that Anthropic has filed a lawsuit against the US government, claiming it was unlawfully labeled a "supply chain risk" after the Pentagon's retaliation for the company's refusal to allow unrestricted military use of its AI tools. The lawsuit, led by CEO Dario Amodei, targets multiple government officials and agencies, asserting that the government's actions violate the Constitution and infringe on the company's First Amendment rights. Anthropic argues that its reputation and future contracts are jeopardized by the government's public condemnation, particularly following President Trump's directive to cease using its tools, which has caused significant economic harm. The company seeks a court ruling to declare the government's actions unconstitutional, while support for Anthropic has emerged from employees at rival firms Google and OpenAI, emphasizing the need for safeguards against the misuse of AI technology.

Defense & Security
Public Sector & Governance
[9 March 2026] NIST publishes report examining challenges in monitoring deployed AI systems:
The National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) has published a report (NIST AI 800-4) examining challenges in monitoring deployed AI systems. The report, based on a year-long inquiry led by the Center for AI Standards and Innovation (CAISI) with input from model developers, compute providers, and federal agencies, outlines a framework for post-deployment measurement to ensure AI systems operate reliably, track unforeseen outputs, and identify unexpected outcomes in changing contexts. It identifies six key monitoring categories, functionality, operational consistency, human factors, security, regulatory compliance, and large-scale impacts, and classifies challenges into cross-cutting issues, category-specific challenges, and open questions, such as optimal monitoring frequency and balancing automated versus human oversight. While relevant across the AI ecosystem, the report highlights particular importance for frontier generative AI systems and provides a foundation for future guidance on field studies and incident monitoring.

Cybersecurity
[6 March 2026] US mulls new rules for AI chip exports, including requiring US investments by foreign firms:
It is reported that the US Commerce Department has drafted regulations that would require companies to obtain US approval for exporting AI chips globally. This proposed framework would mandate that firms like Nvidia and AMD seek permission for nearly all AI accelerator exports, expanding current restrictions from approximately 40 countries to a worldwide scope. The regulations introduce a tiered approval process: shipments of up to 1,000 units of Nvidia's latest GB300 GPUs would undergo a relatively straightforward review, while larger deployments would necessitate more stringent scrutiny, including potential conditions such as foreign governments investing in US AI infrastructure or providing security assurances. For deployments exceeding 200,000 units in a single country, the host nation's government would need to be involved, with approvals granted only to allies making significant security commitments and matching investments in American AI. These measures aim to control the proliferation of advanced AI capabilities and maintain U.S. leadership in the sector.

[5 March 2026] Anthropic officially designated a supply chain risk by Pentagon:
According to a press statement by Anthropic, the US Department of War has formally designated the Anthropic as a supply-chain risk due to its attempts to restrict the Pentagon's use of its Claude AI model, a label typically reserved for foreign firms linked to U.S. adversaries, which may compel companies working with the U.S. military to sever ties with Anthropic. The Pentagon emphasized the necessity for military access to technology for lawful purposes and stated that it would not permit vendors to limit the use of critical capabilities, thereby endangering warfighters. Anthropic's CEO, Dario Amodei, previously communicated to Defense Secretary Pete Hegseth that Claude would not be used for domestic surveillance or autonomous weapons, and the company plans to contest the supply-chain risk designation in court.

Defense & Security
[4 March 2026] AI companies sign Ratepayer Protection Pledge:
President Trump has secured commitments from leading AI companies and hyperscalers—including Amazon, Google, Meta, Microsoft, OpenAI, Oracle, and xAI—to sign the Ratepayer Protection Pledge. This pledge ensures these companies will build, bring, or buy new generation resources and cover all power delivery infrastructure upgrades required for their data centers, preventing these costs from being passed on to US households. Additionally, the companies will negotiate separate rate structures with utilities and state governments, pay these rates regardless of electricity usage, coordinate with grid operators to provide backup generation resources, and invest in local communities by hiring and training local talent, thereby creating thousands of jobs and enhancing workforce skills.

Chips & Data Centres
Energy & Environment
[2 March 2026] Supreme Court denies petition in Thaler v Perlmutter on copyright:
The Supreme Court of the United States denied a petition for a writ of certiorari in Stephen Thaler v Shira Perlmutter, Register of Copyrights and Director of the United States Copyright Office. The case concerned the copyrightability of “A Recent Entrance to Paradise”, a visual work generated by an artificial intelligence system known as the Creativity Machine. The petitioner challenged earlier decisions of the District Court for the District of Columbia and the Court of Appeals for the District of Columbia Circuit, which held that the Copyright Act requires human authorship. The petition for certiorari was filed on 9 October 2025. Following a briefing by the parties, the Supreme Court declined to review the case. As a result, the lower court rulings remain in place, maintaining the position that copyright protection under US law applies to works created by human authors.

Copyright & IP
[27 February 2026] President Trump orders US federal agencies to stop use of Anthropic technology amid dispute over ethics of AI:
In a post on Truth Social, President Donald Trump said he will be directing all federal agencies to immediately cease using technology from Anthropic following a deadlock between the Department of Defense and Anthropic over ethical guidelines for AI systems. The Pentagon had demanded that Anthropic relax its ethical constraints, but the company refused, leading to the termination of their collaboration. Defense Secretary Pete Hegseth subsequently designated Anthropic as a supply-chain risk to national security, a classification typically reserved for foreign adversaries, potentially jeopardising the company's partnerships with other businesses.

Defense & Security
[25 February 2026] US Defense Secretary threatens Anthropic with deadline in dispute on AI safeguards:
It is reported that the US Secretary of Defense Pete Hegseth has threatened to remove Anthropic from the agency's supply chain if the company does not permit its AI technology to be utilized for military applications, following a meeting with Anthropic CEO Dario Amodei at the Pentagon. Hegseth has given Anthropic until Friday evening to comply, with a senior Pentagon official indicating that failure to do so may lead to invoking the Defense Production Act, which could enforce unrestricted use of Anthropic's products for national security. While discussions were described as cordial, Anthropic has outlined its red lines, including opposition to autonomous military operations and mass domestic surveillance. The Pentagon maintains that the current dispute is not related to these issues, and Anthropic, known for its safety-oriented AI approach, has previously faced scrutiny regarding its technology's use in military operations.

Defense & Security
[25 February 2026] Trump announces data center energy deals with tech companies in State of Union address:
US President Donald Trump has announced during his State of the Union address that his administration has instructed major technology companies to construct their own power plants for data centers to mitigate rising electricity costs for consumers - "Many Americans are also concerned that energy demand from AI data centers could unfairly drive up their electric utility bills. Tonight, I'm pleased to announce that I have negotiated the new Ratepayer Protection Pledge. You know what that is. We're telling the major tech companies that they have the obligation to provide for their own power needs." President Trump stated that the White House plans to formalize this effort with the companies in early March 2026. The announcement comes amid concerns regarding the impact of AI data centers on energy prices, which could pose challenges for Republicans ahead of the upcoming midterm elections.

[19 February 2026] Treasury releases resources to guide AI use in the financial sector:
The US Department of the Treasury has released two new resources to guide the financial sector in the responsible use of AI. These resources aim to assist financial institutions in implementing AI technologies while ensuring compliance with existing regulations and promoting ethical practices. The guidance emphasizes the importance of transparency, accountability, and risk management in AI applications within the financial industry.

Finance
[17 February 2026] NIST announces the "AI Agent Standards Initiative" for interoperable and secure innovation:
The National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) has launched the AI Agent Standards Initiative to promote the secure and interoperable adoption of autonomous AI agents. This initiative focuses on three strategic pillars: facilitating industry-led standards through technical convenings and gap analyses, fostering community-led protocols by engaging with the AI ecosystem to reduce interoperability barriers, and investing in research on agent authentication and identity infrastructure to enable secure interactions. NIST is seeking public input on AI agent security through a Request for Information, with a submission deadline of 9 March 2026.

Agentic AI
[16 February 2026] Federal judge rules AI chatbot conversations were not protected by attorney-client privilege:
In the US v. Heppner, No. 25-cr-503-JSR (S.D.N.Y. Feb. 17, 2026), District Judge Jed Rakoff ruled that conversations with AI chatbots, such as Anthropic's Claude, were not protected under attorney-client privilege and can be seized as evidence in fraud cases. This decision arose from the case of Bradley Heppner, a former financial services executive facing federal securities fraud charges, who used Claude to research his legal exposure. The court determined that AI chatbots are not attorneys, their communications lack confidentiality due to data retention and sharing policies, and materials prepared independently without direct attorney involvement do not qualify for work product protection. This ruling underscores the legal risks of using consumer AI platforms for sensitive legal inquiries without proper safeguards.

Privilege
[13 February 2026] US Department of Labor releases AI literacy framework providing foundational content areas, delivery principles to guide nationwide efforts:
The US Department of Labor's Employment and Training Administration has released a framework for AI literacy, aiming to guide nationwide efforts across workforce and education systems. This framework outlines five foundational content areas and seven delivery principles to assist in the design and implementation of AI literacy programs, ensuring adaptability across various industries, roles, and educational sectors. The initiative underscores the department's commitment to equipping American workers with the necessary skills to navigate and thrive in an AI-integrated labor market.

[3 February 2026] Senator Markey opens investigation into autonomous vehicle companies’ use of remote human operators:
Senator Edward J. Markey (D-Mass.) has initiated an investigation into the use of remote human operators by autonomous vehicle companies, including Waymo, Tesla, Zoox, Aurora, Motional, May Mobility, and Nuro. Senator Markey expressed concerns about the safety, national security, and privacy risks associated with these remote assistance systems, particularly when operators are located overseas, potentially making them vulnerable to hostile actors. Senator Markey has requested detailed information from these companies by 17 February 2026, regarding the roles, locations, qualifications, and operational procedures of their remote assistance operators. This inquiry underscores the need for transparency and robust safeguards in the deployment of autonomous vehicle technologies.

Transport
[14 January 2026] President Trump signs proclamation with respect to imports of semiconductors:
President Trump has signed a Proclamation invoking Section 232 of the Trade Expansion Act of 1962 (Act) to address national security concerns with respect to imports of semiconductors, semiconductor manufacturing equipment, and their derivative products. Following a Department of Commerce investigation which determined that current import levels threaten to impair national security, the President has directed the Secretary of Commerce and US Trade Representative to negotiate international agreements while immediately imposing a 25% tariff on specific advanced computing chips, such as the NVIDIA H200 and AMD MI325X. These measures include exemptions for imports that support the domestic supply chain and are expected to be followed by broader tariffs and a manufacturing offset program designed to incentivize local production. By reducing reliance on foreign sources for essential components like advanced lithography and etching tools, the administration aims to rectify insufficient domestic capacity and protect the nation’s economic and military strength, further advancing an "America First" trade policy that has previously used Section 232 to secure critical industries like steel and aluminium.

Defense & National Security
[12 January 2026] US War Department launches AI Acceleration Strategy to secure American military AI dominance:
The US War Department has launched an AI Acceleration Strategy to secure American military AI dominance by transforming into an "AI-first" force that integrates frontier technology across all combat domains. Mandated by President Trump and led by Secretary Pete Hegseth, this initiative adopts a wartime pace to eliminate bureaucratic hurdles and deploy three million personnel-strong capabilities focused on warfighting, intelligence, and enterprise operations. At the heart of the strategy are seven "Pace-Setting Projects," such as Swarm Forge and GenAI.mil, which leverage high-level compute infrastructure and partnerships with industry leaders like Google and xAI across all domains from the Pentagon to the tactical edge. Other key initiatives include establishing a unified innovation ecosystem under a single Chief Technology Officer, investing heavily in AI compute infrastructure, and aggressively recruiting top tech talent to ensure the US remains the world's leading AI-enabled fighting force.

Defense & National Security
Generative AI
[12 January 2026] CAISI Issues Request for Information About Securing AI Agent Systems:
The Center for AI Standards and Innovation (CAISI) at the National Institute of Standards and Technology NIST has issued a Request for Information (RFI) seeking input from industry, academia, and the security community on securing AI agent systems. These systems, capable of autonomous actions affecting real-world environments, present unique security challenges, including risks from adversarial data interactions, use of compromised models, and unintended harmful actions. The RFI poses questions on topics including: (1) unique security threats affecting AI agent systems, and how these threats may change over time; (2) methods for improving the security of AI agent systems in development and deployment; (3) promise of and possible gaps in existing cybersecurity approaches when applied to AI agent systems; (4) methods for measuring the security of AI agent systems and approaches to anticipating risks during development; and (5) interventions in deployment environments to address security risks affecting AI agent systems, including methods to constrain and monitor the extent of agent access in the deployment environment. The RFI aims to gather insights on identifying and mitigating these threats to inform future guidelines and best practices. The comment period closes on 9 March 2026.

[9 January 2026] NIST opens consultation on security of AI agent systems:
The National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) has opened a consultation on the security of AI agent systems, particularly the distinct security risks arising from AI model outputs interacting with software systems, such as indirect prompt injection, data poisoning, and specification gaming. The information gathered will inform the development of voluntary guidelines and best practices aimed at addressing security challenges that could impact public safety and national security. The consultation will close on 9 March 2026.

[9 January 2026] US Justice Department establishes AI Litigation Taskforce:
The US Attorney General has issued a memorandum establishing an AI Litigation Task Force within the Department of Justice (DOJ), as mandated under Executive Order 14365 (Ensuring a National Policy Framework for AI). The Task Force is mandated to challenge state AI laws deemed inconsistent with federal AI policy "on grounds that such laws unconstitutionally regulate interstate commerce, are preempted by existing Federal regulations, or are otherwise unlawful". The Task Force will be chaired by the Attorney General or a designee and include senior DOJ divisions. Coordination is provided with White House advisors on AI, science and technology, and economic policy.

[8 January 2026] Trump shifts FTC pick to White House role advising on tech and competition:
It is reported that the US White House is withdrawing its nomination of Ryan Baasch for a Federal Trade Commission seat and instead naming him deputy director of the National Economic Council, elevating his role in shaping tech, telecom and competition policy. Baasch will serve as deputy assistant to President Trump and replace Robin Colwell at the NEC, which advises on economic policy. The move comes as President Trump seeks greater influence over agencies and tech regulation following his firing of two Democratic FTC commissioners in March 2025. In his previous role as Texas Attorney General, Baasch oversaw a series of privacy suits against Google and Meta Platforms over the tech giants’ use of facial recognition technology, as well as Google’s harvesting of consumers’ location information and other personal data through the "Incognito" private browsing mode in the Chrome browser. Under Baasch, Texas also brought ongoing privacy litigation against General Motors and Allstate over the alleged illegal sharing of personal data between carmakers, insurance companies and data analytics companies.

Antitrust & Competition
[22 December 2025] FTC sets aside prior ruling in lawsuit against Rytr for allegedly generating false reviews with AI-powered tools:
The Federal Trade Commission (FTC) has set aside its prior ruling in a lawsuit against Rytr LLC for allegedly generating false reviews with AI-powered tools. Following review, the FTC concluded the original order would have unduly burdened AI development, contravening the Trump Administration's Executive Order 14179, "Removing Barriers to American Leadership in Artificial Intelligence" and 2025 AI Action Plan. The order would have banned Rytr LLC from advertising, marketing, promoting, offering for sale, or selling any service dedicated to generating consumer reviews or testimonials, and would have required Rytr to submit annual compliance reports for five years. Rytr would also have been required to obtain acknowledgements of receipt of the order from all relevant personnel and entities.

[19 December 2025] US launches review of advanced Nvidia AI chip sales to China:
It is reported that, according to inside sources, the Trump administration has initiated an inter-agency review to authorize the export of Nvidia’s H200 AI chips to China, a move that reverses long-standing restrictions on high-end semiconductor sales. Under this proposal, the U.S. government would collect a 25% fee on the shipments, with President Trump arguing that providing American hardware will maintain U.S. technological dominance by reducing Chinese reliance on domestic chipmakers. The Department of Commerce has referred license applications to the State, Energy, and Defense Departments for a 30-day evaluation period; however, while officials emphasize the review will be rigorous, the final decision-making authority rests with the President. This shift marks a significant pivot from the previous administration’s policy of strictly limiting Chinese access to advanced technology to mitigate national security risks.

Defense & National Security
[18 December 2025] FERC directs nation’s largest grid operator to create new rules on the connection of AI-driven data centers and other large electricity loads located next to power plants:
The US Federal Energy Regulatory Commission (FERC) has directed grid operator PJM to create clear and transparent rules for serving large, co-located loads such as AI-driven data centers alongside generating facilities. This action addresses concerns that PJM’s current tariff lacks clarity and fairness in rates, terms, and conditions for such arrangements, which could impact grid reliability and consumer costs. FERC found the existing rules unjust and unreasonable and is requiring PJM to revise its tariff to include detailed provisions for interconnection customers and introduce new transmission service options. PJM must also update its Behind-the-Meter Generation rules, establish a transition period, and grandfather certain contracts. Additionally, PJM is required to submit a reliability report by 19 January 2026, and participate in a paper hearing to determine fair rates for new services, with initial briefs due by 16 February 2026. These changes aim to support innovation, maintain reliability, and protect consumers in PJM’s 13-state territory.

[16 December 2025] NIST releases preliminary draft of Cyber AI profile:
The National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) has released a preliminary draft of the Cybersecurity Framework Profile for Artificial Intelligence (Cyber AI Profile), designated as NIST IR 8596. This profile aims to assist organizations in strategically adopting AI technologies while effectively managing associated cybersecurity risks. It focuses on three key areas: securing AI system components, conducting AI-enabled cyber defense, and thwarting AI-enabled cyber attacks. NIST is inviting public comments on this draft until 30 January 2026, and has scheduled a hybrid workshop on 14 January 2026, to discuss the profile and provide updates on related initiatives.

[8 December 2025] NDAA would mandate new DOD steering committee on AGI:
The draft text of the fiscal 2026 National Defense Authorization Act is revealed, and it appears to mandate the Secretary of Defense to establish an "Artificial Intelligence Futures Steering Committee" by 1 April 2026, co-chaired by the Deputy Secretary of Defense and the Vice Chairman of the Joint Chiefs of Staff, with members including service vice chiefs and other top officials. This committee is tasked with developing policies for evaluating, adopting, governing, and mitigating risks associated with advanced AI systems, including those approaching artificial general intelligence (AGI). Additionally, it will analyze emerging AI models and technologies that could lead to AGI, assess the operational impacts of integrating such AI into Department of Defense systems, and examine adversaries' advancements in this field to develop counter-strategies.

Cybersecurity
Generative AI
[26 November 2025] USTPO revises guidance on inventorship of AI assisted inventions:
The US Patent and Trademark Office (USPTO) has released the Revised Inventorship Guidance for AI-Assisted Inventions and rescinded the guidance issued on 13 February 2024. The previous guidance, which applied the Pannu factors to AI-assisted inventions, was withdrawn. The USPTO clarified that the Pannu factors apply only to determining whether multiple natural persons qualify as joint inventors, because artificial intelligence systems are not natural persons and cannot be joint inventors. The guidance states that the same legal standard for determining inventorship applies to all inventions. AI systems cannot be named as inventors or joint inventors. Inventorship is based on conception, which requires a definite and permanent idea of the complete and operative invention. It also explains the fact-intensive assessment of conception, treats AI systems as instruments without inventorship status, and outlines joint inventorship principles for multiple natural persons. The guidance applies to utility, design, and plant patents. It also clarifies priority requirements, stating that the same natural person or at least one joint inventor must be named in common with a prior-filed application. A priority claim to a foreign application naming an AI system as the sole inventor will not be accepted.

[24 November 2025] President Trump signs executive order on national effort to accelerate scientific discovery using AI:
President Donald Trump has signed an executive order initiating the "Genesis Mission," a national initiative aimed at accelerating scientific discovery through AI. This mission seeks to integrate federal scientific datasets with AI to develop models and agents capable of automating research processes and expediting breakthroughs. The Department of Energy is tasked with creating a unified AI platform that leverages the nation's research resources, including national laboratories, private sector partners, and academic institutions. The Genesis Mission focuses on addressing critical challenges in areas such as advanced manufacturing, biotechnology, critical materials, nuclear energy, quantum information science, and semiconductors, with the goal of enhancing national security, achieving energy dominance, boosting workforce productivity, and reinforcing US global technological leadership.

Defense & National Security
[28 October 2025] US Energy Department announces new partnership with NVIDIA and Oracle to build AI supercomputer:
The U.S. Department of Energy (DOE), in collaboration with Argonne National Laboratory, NVIDIA, and Oracle, has announced a public-private partnership to develop the DOE's largest AI supercomputer, aiming to accelerate scientific discovery. This initiative includes the construction of two AI supercomputing systems at Argonne: the Solstice system, featuring 100,000 NVIDIA Blackwell GPUs, and the Equinox system, with 10,000 NVIDIA Blackwell GPUs. Construction of Equinox is set to begin immediately, with delivery expected in 2026. These systems will integrate with the DOE's extensive network of scientific instruments and data assets to tackle critical challenges in energy, security, and discovery science. Additionally, Oracle will provide immediate access to AI computing resources utilizing NVIDIA's Hopper and Blackwell architectures, enhancing DOE researchers' capabilities in AI-driven scientific research.

Chips & Data Centres
[21 October 2025] International Trade Administration announces development of American AI Exports Program:
The International Trade Administration has announced the development of the American AI Exports Program as required under Executive Order 14320 (re Promoting the Export of the American AI Technology Stack). The programme aims to support the global deployment of American AI technologies through industry-led consortia. It will establish evaluation criteria for defining and assessing components of the AI technology stack, outline participation and governance structures for consortia, and design business and operational models consistent with federal incentives and ownership requirements. The initiative will also ensure compliance with export controls, outbound investment rules, and national security regulations, with the objective of promoting AI exports and reducing dependence on technologies from countries of concern. The public consultation on the development of the program will commence after notice’s publication in the Federal Register.

Defense & National Security
[13 October 2025] California governor signs various bills targeting online safety and AI:
California Governor Gavin Newsom has signed a series of bills targeting child online safety as concerns over the risks associated with AI and social media use keep mounting. Collectively, the bills add required features for platforms and products such as age verification, protocols to address suicide and self-harm, warnings regarding social media and companion chatbots, and stronger penalties for those who profit from illegal deepfakes. Notably, SB 243 is the first state law of its kind and requires chatbots to disclose that they are AI and tell minors every three hours to “take a break.” Chatbots providers will also need to implement tools to protect against harmful behaviours and disclose certain instances to a crisis hotline.

[10 October 2025] Singapore and US authorities probe Nvidia customer Megaspeed over alleged China export violations:
It is reported that Singaporean and U.S. authorities are investigating Megaspeed, a client of Nvidia, for potential violations of export controls. The investigation focuses on allegations that Megaspeed may have misrepresented the final destination of U.S.-manufactured servers, possibly containing Nvidia's advanced AI chips, by shipping them to Malaysia, with concerns that they might have ultimately reached China. This scrutiny arises amid broader efforts to prevent the unauthorized transfer of sensitive technologies to China, especially in light of U.S. export restrictions on advanced semiconductors. Singapore's Home Affairs and Law Minister, K Shanmugam, confirmed that the servers in question were supplied by Dell Technologies and Super Micro Computer, and emphasized that authorities are working closely with U.S. counterparts to investigate the matter.

[9 October 2025] US federal agencies publish plans on their AI usage, revealing challenges:
It is reported that US federal agencies under the Trump administration are encountering persistent challenges in implementing AI, including issues with data access and quality, IT infrastructure limitations, a shortage of AI-skilled personnel, and resource constraints. The 2025 AI compliance plans - which were required to be published by federal agencies by 30 September under Trump’s AI governance memo - reveal that while some agencies have made progress in identifying and addressing these barriers, there remains significant variability in how agencies are managing high-impact AI use cases. Notably, the Department of Transportation highlighted structural impediments such as inadequate computing tools and processes for security and compliance, which hinder effective AI deployment. Additionally, the Department of Homeland Security is focusing on enhancing IT infrastructure and data governance to improve AI utilization. These findings underscore the ongoing efforts and challenges federal agencies face in advancing AI initiatives.

This governance structure is tasked with developing new methods to apply advanced technologies, including AI, in medical research and practice, as well as identifying opportunities for the Childhood Cancer Data Initiative (CCDI) at the National Cancer Institute to expand data generation, collection, and analysis.

[29 September 2025] California governor signs SB 53 (Transparency in Frontier AI Act) into law:
California Governor Gavin Newsom has signed Senate Bill 53, the Transparency in Frontier Artificial Intelligence Act, into law, establishing California as a leader in safe and trustworthy AI development. This legislation introduces guardrails on the creation of advanced AI models, aiming to enhance online safety and build public trust while fostering innovation. SB 53 establishes the following new requirements for frontier AI developers: (1) requiring large frontier developers to publicly publish a framework on its website describing how the company has incorporated national standards, international standards, and industry-consensus best practices into its frontier AI framework; (2) establishing a new consortium within the Government Operations Agency to develop a framework for creating a public computing cluster. The consortium, called CalCompute, will advance the development and deployment of AI that is safe, ethical, equitable, and sustainable by fostering research and innovation; (3) creating a new mechanism for frontier AI companies and the public to report potential critical safety incidents to California’s Office of Emergency Services; (4) protecting whistleblowers who disclose significant health and safety risks posed by frontier models, and creates a civil penalty for noncompliance, enforceable by the Attorney General’s office; and (5) directing the California Department of Technology to annually recommend appropriate updates to the law based on multistakeholder input, technological developments, and international standards.

[24 September 2025] NIST issues broad announcement for proposals to advance microelectronics technologies, covering semiconductor and machine learning innovation:
The National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) has released a broad agency announcement (BAA) soliciting proposals for the following topic areas: (1) Semiconductors, including research and prototyping of advanced semiconductor technologies and growing the domestic semiconductor workforce; (2) Application of AI for advanced microelectronics research and development; (3) Application of quantum technology for advanced microelectronics research and development; (4) Application of biotechnology and biomanufacturing technology for advanced microelectronics research and development; (5) Commercialization of innovations; and (6) Standards development. The initiative is part of the larger CHIPS for America program, seeking to enhance technological advancements that underpin national economic and security goals.

National Strategy
[12 September 2025] NIST launches consultation on standards for documentation of AI datasets and models:
The National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) has opened a public consultation on the extended outline for the proposed zero draft of a standard on documentation of AI datasets and AI models under its AI Standards Zero Drafts pilot project. The draft applies to AI developers, providers, and organisations using datasets and models, aiming to harmonise documentation practices across the AI lifecycle. It proposes templates for dataset and model documentation to balance detail and flexibility, incorporating testing, evaluation, verification, and validation (TEVV) descriptors, alongside guidance on public-facing documentation processes and outcomes. The standard seeks to improve transparency, comparability, and trustworthiness in AI while remaining domain-agnostic and adaptable to different audiences and use cases. The consultation closes on 17 October 2025.

[11 September 2025] FTC launches inquiry into AI chatbots acting as companions:
The Federal Trade Commission (FTC) has initiated an investigation into seven companies that operate consumer-facing AI chatbots, issuing 6(b) orders to Alphabet, Inc., Character Technologies, Inc., Instagram, LLC, Meta Platforms, Inc., OpenAI OpCo, LLC, Snap, Inc., and X.AI Corp. The inquiry, approved by a 3-0 vote, seeks to understand the chatbots' capabilities, intended audience, and potential negative impacts, as well as the companies' data collection and handling practices. The FTC is also examining how these firms monitor and enforce compliance with their own rules and terms of service, and how they use or share personal information obtained through user conversations.

Online Safety & Child Protection
[6 September 2025] Nvidia says GAIN AI Act would restrict competition, likens it to AI Diffusion Rule:
It is reported that according to Nvidia's spokesperson, Nvidia has voiced concerns that the Guaranteeing Access and Innovation for National Artificial Intelligence Act (AI GAIN Act) would restrict global competition for advanced chips. For background, the GAIN AI Act was introduced as part of the National Defense Authorization Act and stipulates that AI chipmakers prioritize domestic orders for advanced processors before supplying them to foreign customers. The rules mirror some conditions under the former Biden-era AI Diffusion Rule, which allocated certain levels of computing power to allies and other countries. If passed into law, the bill would enact new trade restrictions mandating exporters obtain licenses and approval for the shipments of silicon exceeding certain performance caps.

[25 August 2025] US state attorney generals submit letter to AI companies calling for safeguards to protect children from sexually inappropriate conversations:
44 US State Attorneys General, led by Tennessee Attorney General, have issued letters to AI companies, including Google, Meta, Microsoft, OpenAI, xAI, Anthropic, Character Technologies, Perplexity AI, Apple, Chai AI, Luka Inc., Nomi AI and Replika. The communication referred to reports of AI chatbots engaging in sexualised conversations with children and allegedly encouraging harmful behaviour in teenagers, including suicide and murder. The letter called on AI developers to introduce safeguards against the sexualisation of children in their policies and noted that oversight bodies would take enforcement actions if the products cause harm to children.

[25 August 2025] FTC sues Air AI over alleged deceptive claims targeting small businesses:
The Federal Trade Commission (FTC) has filed a complaint in the District Court for the District of Arizona against Air AI Technologies, its owners and affiliated companies. The FTC has alleged that Air AI Technologies engaged in deceptive practices by making false or unsubstantiated claims about earnings, misrepresenting refund guarantees and services and failing to comply with disclosure and refund obligations under the Telemarketing Sales Rule and the Business Opportunity Rule. The FTC claimed that since February 2023, Air AI promoted coaching services, resale licences and a conversational AI product with promises of rapid and substantial profits and full refunds, which were rarely delivered.

[21 August 2025] FTC issues ruling against Workado over unsubstantiated advertising claims concerning AI content detection tools:
The US Federal Trade Commission (FTC) has issued a ruling against Workado LLC, formerly Content at Scale Artificial Intelligence. The case concerned unsubstantiated claims relating to AI content detection tools. The ruling applies to marketing products that claim to detect or verify AI-generated or altered content. It prohibits misleading representations unless supported by competent and reliable scientific evidence. It requires preservation of testing data, customer notification, annual compliance reporting, and recordkeeping for ten years. Workado must also ensure acknowledgements of the ruling by relevant personnel. The ruling will remain in effect for twenty years from 21 August 2025, with possible extension if new complaints are filed.

[15 August 2025] NIST releases concept paper on control overlays for securing AI systems:
The National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) has released a concept paper and proposed action plan for developing a series of NIST SP 800-53 Control Overlays for Securing AI Systems, as well as a launching a Slack channel for this community of interest. The concept paper outlines proposed AI use cases for the control overlays to manage cybersecurity risks in the use and development of AI systems, and next steps. The use cases address generative AI, predictive AI, single and multi-agent AI systems, and controls for AI developers.

[5 August 2025] US charges two Chinese nationals for illegally shipping Nvidia AI chips to China:
According to the US Department of Justice, two Chinese nationals residing in California have been arrested for allegedly exporting sensitive microchips used in AI applications to China without the required licenses. Operating through their company, ALX Solutions Inc., from October 2022 to July 2025, the defendants have been accused of shipping advanced Nvidia AI chips, including H100s and RTX 4090 GPUs, to China via transshipment points in Singapore and Malaysia to evade US export controls. Both are charged with violating the Export Control Reform Act, carrying a potential maximum penalty of 20 years in prison. The investigation remains ongoing.

Richie Torres (D-NY), Subcommittee on Digital Assets, Financial Technology, and Artificial Intelligence Chairman Bryan Steil (R-WI), and Rep. Generative AI
[30 July 2025] Keep Call Centres in America Act introduced:
US senators Ruben Gallego (D-AZ) and Jim Justice (R-W) have introduced a new bipartisan bill, called the "Keep Call Centers in America Act of 2025" which proposes to ensure call centre jobs remain in the US by limiting federal benefits for companies who ship them overseas. Notably, the bill will require call center workers to immediately disclose to callers the physical location of the call center and/or whether artificial intelligence is being used. Call workers are further required to transfer communications to a call center located in the US if a customer requests that they do so.

Data Privacy & Protection
[29 July 2025] US GAO releases report on Generative AI use and management at federal agencies:
The US Government Accountability Office has released a report on use and management of generative AI at US federal agencies. The headline finding was that, across the 11 selected agencies GAO reviewed with AI inventories, the total number of reported AI use cases nearly doubled from 571 in 2023 to 1,110 in 2024. At the same time, generative AI use cases increased about nine-fold, from 32 to 282. GAO also found that agency officials faced several challenges to using generative AI, such as: complying with existing federal policies and guidance, having sufficient technical resources and budget, and maintaining up-to-date appropriate use policies. For example, officials at 10 of 12 selected agencies said existing federal policy, such as data privacy policy, could present obstacles to adoption.

[23 July 2025] Smart Cities and Communities Act introduced:
US House of Representative members Suzan DelBene (WA-01) and Yvette Clarke (NY-09) have introduced The Smart Cities and Communities Bill to the House. The Bill aims to accelerate the deployment of smart technologies (including AI) by (1) establishing an Interagency Council on Smart Cities; (2) providing up to USD 100 million a year from 2026 to 2030 for Technology Demonstration Grants in urban, small town, rural and Tribal settings; (3) allocating a further USD 100 million annually to a TechHire Workforce Training and Development Programme, which will award competitive grants to prepare workers for smart city roles; and (4) mandating a Cybersecurity Working Group to develop evaluation tools for technology security, Department of Energy technical assistance, a smart city voucher scheme granting access to National Laboratory expertise and a comprehensive resource guide for local authorities.

Cybersecurity
[16 July 2025] House Judiciary Subcommittee hearing on AI and criminal exploitation:
The US House Judiciary Subcommittee on Crime and Federal Government Surveillance will hold a hearing on AI and criminal exploitation which will examine the growing threat of AI-enabled crime, including how criminals are leveraging AI to conduct fraud, identity theft, child exploitation, and other illicit activities. It will also explore the capabilities and limitations of law enforcement in addressing these evolving threats, as well as potential legislative and policy responses to ensure public safety in the age of AI.

[14 June 2025] SEC withdraws AI and ESG proposed rules:
The Securities and Exchange Commission has withdrawn several rules proposed initially during the Biden administration, including a rule intended to rein in firms’ conflicts of interest when using AI. This "predictive data analytics" rule would have required firms to “eliminate or neutralise” conflicts if using those data tools (such as AI) could place firms’ interests ahead of clients.

[12 June 2025] NIST publishes new AI Security Competency Area for the NICE Framework:
The National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) has updated the National Initiative for Cybersecurity Education (NICE) Workforce Framework for Cybersecurity to include a new competency area on AI security, which describes foundational knowledge and skills needed to understand the intersection between AI and cybersecurity and the risks and opportunities this may present. This work is currently available for public comment.

Cybersecurity
[30 May 2025] NIH seeks input on effective strategies for mitigating controlled-access human genomic data leakage when developing and sharing generative AI tools and applications:
The National Institutes of Health (NIH) has issued a request for public input on strategies to mitigate the risk of controlled-access human genomic data leakage when developing and sharing generative AI tools, while still enabling responsible innovation in biomedical research. Due to privacy concerns—such as the potential for generative AI models to memorize and inadvertently disclose sensitive genomic data—the NIH has temporarily paused the sharing and retention of generative AI models trained on controlled-access genomic data. NIH seeks feedback from researchers, developers, institutions, and the public on effective privacy-preserving methods and policies. This initiative aims to ensure NIH policies remain aligned with advances in AI technology and uphold participant privacy protections. The consultation closes on 16 July 2025.

[28 May 2025] US senator calls for AI competition in Pentagon contracting:
US Senator Elizabeth Warren (D-Mass.) has written a letter asking US Secretary of Defense Pete Hegseth to explain how he will ensure the Department of Defense’s (DOD) AI contracting processes will protect government data, save taxpayer funds, and promote competition. The letter emphasizes the importance of the Department of Defense's (DoD) procurement decisions in fostering competition and preventing market consolidation, which can lead to higher prices and reduced innovation. The letter requests Secretary Hegseth to outline strategies for avoiding vendor lock-in, safeguarding government data, and promoting competition in DoD system procurement by 11 June 2025.

Data Privacy & Protection
[23 May 2025] US, UK, Australia and New Zealand jointly release guidance on AI data security:
The US National Security Agency’s Artificial Intelligence Security Center (NSA AISC), the Cybersecurity and Infrastructure Security Agency (CISA), the Federal Bureau of Investigation (FBI), the Australian Signals Directorate’s Australian Cyber Security Centre (ASD’s ACSC), New Zealand’s National Cyber Security Centre (NCSC-NZ), and the United Kingdom’s National Cyber Security Centre (NCSC-UK) have issued a joint guidance on securing data across the AI lifecycle. The guidance addresses critical risks such as data poisoning, supply chain vulnerabilities, and "data drift" (i.e. changes in the underlying statistical properties of the input data to an operational AI system whereby the input data becomes significantly different from its original state over time). The guidance provides mitigation strategies on data management, data quality testing, and input and output monitoring.

[15 May 2025] FTC Commissioner outlines FTC priorities:
In his written testimony before the US House Committee on Appropriations Subcommittee on Financial Services and General Government, Federal Trade Commissioner (FTC) Andrew N. Ferguson has outlined the priorities of the FTC, including AI, cyber, and privacy issues. On the topic of AI, Commissioner Ferguson highlighted the FTC's enforcement efforts in reducing robocalls, and empowering innovation and addressing fraud in the AI sector. In his oral testimony, Commissioner Ferguson stated the FTC's approach as follows: "We see how things go and then we address problems as they arise … Equally important is making sure that government regulators don't intervene too early, particularly with a technology that is transforming constantly, faster than even its engineers can predict".

Copyright & IP
Generative AI
[9 May 2025] US Copyright Office releases part 3 of AI and copyright report, concluding that fair use exception likely does not apply to commercial AI training:
The US Copyright Office has released a pre-publication version of Part 3 of its report series into AI and copyright in response to congressional inquiries and expressions of interest from stakeholders. A final version of Part 3 will be published in the near future, without any substantive changes expected in the analysis or conclusions. The Part 3 report concludes that the fair use exception likely does not apply to commercial AI training, noting that "making commercial use of vast troves of copyrighted works to produce expressive content that competes with them in existing markets, especially where this is accomplished through illegal access, goes beyond established fair use boundaries." In terms of policy solution, the report notes that given the robust growth of voluntary licensing, as well as the lack of stakeholder support for any statutory change, government intervention would be premature at this time. Rather, licensing markets should continue to develop, extending early successes into more contexts as soon as possible. In those areas where remaining gaps are unlikely to be filled, alternative approaches such as extended collective licensing should be considered to address any market failure.

Copyright & IP
[3 May 2025] US judicial panel advances proposal to regulate AI-generated evidence:
It is reported that a US federal judicial panel has advanced a proposal to regulate the use of AI-generated evidence in court. At a meeting in New York, the Advisory Committee on Evidence Rules agreed to draft a rule -similar to those governing expert testimony -that would require rigorous scrutiny of AI-generated evidence for reliability and accuracy before it can be admitted at trial. While the committee agreed on the need for such a rule, there was less consensus on whether a separate rule is needed specifically for deepfakes, though members acknowledged the importance of preparing for future challenges as AI technology rapidly evolves. The proposed rule is expected to be reviewed for public comment in May 2025.

[30 April 2025] Trump officials plan changes to Biden's AI chip export rule:
It is reported that according to internal sources, the Trump administration is working on changes to a Biden-era 'Framework for Artificial Intelligence Diffusion' rule which is set to go into effect on 15 May 2025 to limit global access to AI chips under a three-tiered system. The sources suggest that the administrarion is planning to remove the tiered system, and replacing it with a global licensing regime with government-to-government agreements to regulate access to US AI chips (potentially as a negotiating tool in trade talks). The plans are still under discussion and subject to change.

[28 April 2025] FTC order requires Workado to back up AI detection claims:
The Federal Trade Commission has issued a proposed order requiring Workado LLC to stop advertising the accuracy of its AI detection products unless it maintains competent and reliable evidence showing those products are as accurate as claimed. The FTC has alleged that Workado's AI Content Detector was only trained to classify academic content, despite the company promoting it as "98 percent" accurate in distinguishing between AI and human-written text. The FTC claimed this accuracy assertion was false, misleading, or unsubstantiated, constituting a violation of the FTC Act. The proposed order for settlement will be subject to public comment before becoming final.

Generative AI
[23 April 2025] US President signs executive order to advance AI education:
US President Trump has signed an executive order establishing a comprehensive national initiative to advance AI education for American youth, aiming to ensure the United States maintains global leadership in AI. The order creates a White House Task Force on AI Education, chaired by the Director of the Office of Science and Technology Policy, and directs federal agencies—including the Departments of Education and Labor and the National Science Foundation—to prioritise AI literacy, teacher training, and workforce development. Key measures include promoting AI courses and certification opportunities for high school students, incentivising AI-related apprenticeships, encouraging public-private partnerships to expand K-12 AI resources, and launching a Presidential AI Challenge to highlight student and educator achievements. The directive emphasises early exposure to AI concepts, professional development for educators, and lifelong learning opportunities, all designed to prepare students and workers for an AI-driven economy and to foster innovation and critical thinking across the nation.

It is reported that a draft executive order is set to instruct federal agencies to train students in AI usage and integrate it into educational tasks. The order mandates professional development for educators to incorporate AI across all subjects and proposes a "Presidential AI Challenge" for students and educators to showcase their AI skills. Additionally, it directs the creation of registered apprenticeships in AI-related fields, while also highlighting the need for resources to support lifelong learning for a changing workforce, primarily focusing on K-12 education.

[22 April 2025] FTC member says agency will avoid "excessive regulation" of AI companies:
It is reported that, at the International Association of Privacy Professionals’ annual conference, Federal Trade Commission (FTC) member Melissa Holyoak said that the FTC under the leadership of current chairman Andrew Ferguson "will promote AI growth and innovation, not hamper it with misguided enforcement actions or excessive regulation". Holyoak also said the FTC (1) is seeking to create a "predictable" regulatory and enforcement ecosystem that promotes innovation; (2) will consider "alternatives to such regulations that are better suited to balancing privacy concerns with interest in fostering innovation and competition"; and (3) will continue to focus privacy enforcement efforts on data brokers selling Americans’ location data, with a particular emphasis on those peddling the data to foreign adversaries.

[21 April 2025] Department of Justice begins antitrust trial against Google:
It is reported that as the Department of Justice's (DOJ) antitrust trial against Google begins, the DOJ is seeking an order from the court that would require Google to divest Chrome and end exclusive deals with device makers. The DOJ argue (1) Google’s dominance in online search fuels its AI advantage, blocking competitors and risking control over future tech markets; and (2) Google could use its AI products to extend its dominance in online search. Google defends that its AI products are outside the scope of the case, which focused on search engines, and that the company will appeal once a final judgment is entered.

Defense & National Security
[16 April 2025] US Select Committee on CCP releases report on DeepSeek:
The US Select Committee on the Chinese Communist Party (CCP) has released a report on national security concerns presented by DeepSeek. The report includes findings that: (1) "DeepSeek funnels Americans’ data to the PRC through backend infrastructure connected to a US government-designated Chinese military company"; (2) "DeepSeek covertly manipulates the results it presents to align with CCP propaganda, as required by Chinese law"; (3) "It is highly likely that DeepSeek used unlawful model distillation techniques to create its model, stealing from leading US AI models"; and (4) "DeepSeek’s AI model appears to be powered by advanced chips provided by American semiconductor giant Nvidia and reportedly utilizes tens of thousands of chips that are currently restricted from export to the PRC". The report recommends the US government to take swift action to expand export controls, improve export control enforcement, and address risks from PRC AI models.

The company will build and test its advanced chips in Arizona and its AI supercomputers in Texas over a million square feet of new manufacturing space.

[11 April 2025] US Customs issues updated guidance on reciprocal tariff exclusion for specificed products, including semiconductors and ICs:
The US Customs and Border Protection has issued updated guidance which sets out a list of specified products which will be exempt from the reciprocal tariffs imposed by President Trump under Executive Order 14257. The exemptions broadly cover semiconductors, integrated circuits and smartphones - meaning that Chinese products in those categories will likely be spared from Trump's 125% tariffs.

National Strategy
[10 April 2025] Health Tech Investment Act introduced, covering AI-enabled medical devices:
US Senators Mike Rounds (R-S.D.) and Martin Heinrich (D-N.M.), co-chairs of the Senate Artificial Intelligence Caucus have introduced draft legislation titled the Health Tech Investment Act, which is aimed at improving health outcomes for Medicare patients by encouraging the use of cutting-edge, AI-enabled medical devices. The bill will assign all US Food and Drug Administration (FDA) approved AI-enabled medical devices to a New Technology Ambulatory Payment Classification (APC) in the Hospital Outpatient Prospective Payment System (OPPS) a minimum of 5 years so that adequate data regarding delivery and service costs is acquired before assignment of a permanent payment code. Specifically, the bill would: (1) develop a formalized payment pathway for ABHS FDA-cleared medical devices; (2) provide patients with access to innovative, AI-enabled clinical technology; (3) provide manufacturers and providers with the certainty they need to invest in developing next-generation healthcare technologies and bringing them to market, and (4) improve patient outcomes, providing resources for providers to meet ABHS standards of care.

[9 April 2025] TAME Extreme Weather and Wildfires Act introduced to enable use of AI for weather predictions:
US Senators Brian Schatz (D-Hawai‘i) and Tim Sheehy (R-Mont.) have introduced the TAME Extreme Weather and Wildfires Act, bipartisan legislation which would require the National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration to take several actions to support the use of AI forecasting and weather models, including: developing a dataset to train AI forecasting models, supporting the deployment of AI weather models into forecasts, and partnering with private sector and academia on AI weather and wildfire forecasting. The bill (S. 1378; H.R. 2770) was initially introduced in the House and Senate last Congress but did not advance out of either chamber. The legislation did, however, advance out of the Senate Commerce, Science, and Transportation Committee in July 2024 as an amendment to the Fire Ready Nation Act. The new legislation remains largely unchanged but adds a focus on wildfires.

The scheme reportedly involved misleading investors about the potential profitability of the AI system, resulting in significant financial losses. Antitrust & Competition
[24 March 2025] NIST publishes guidelines on Adversarial Machine Learning:
The US National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) has published its finalised report titled "Adversarial Machine Learning: A Taxonomy and Terminology of Attacks and Mitigations (AI 100-2 E2025)", which provides a taxonomy of concepts and defines terminology in the field of adversarial machine learning (AML). The taxonomy is arranged in a conceptual hierarchy that includes key types of ML methods, life cycle stages of attack, and attacker goals, objectives, capabilities, and knowledge. This report also identifies current challenges in the life cycle of AI systems and describes corresponding methods for mitigating and managing the consequences of those attacks. The terminology used in this report is consistent with the literature on AML and is complemented by a glossary of key terms associated with the security of AI systems. Taken together, the taxonomy and terminology are meant to inform other standards and future practice guides for assessing and managing the security of AI systems by establishing a common language for the rapidly developing AML landscape.

[24 March 2025] US big tech companies lobby for AI deregulation:
It is reported that US President Donald Trump's call for AI deregulation is receiving substantial support from Big Tech companies based on submissions from the sector in response to the White House Office of Science and Technology Policy's consultation on the development of a national AI Action Plan. Ideas proposed by major AI companies, including Meta, Google, and OpenAI, have included: (1) seeking exemptions from state AI laws; (2) legal clearance to use copyrighted training data; (3) access to federal resources like energy and tax incentives; and (4) increased government support to counter cybersecurity threats amid an accelerating AI race with China.

Cybersecurity
[21 March 2025] US judge approves 'novel' Clearview AI class action settlement:
A US judge in Chicago has approved a unique nationwide class-action settlement that will resolve privacy claims against facial recognition company Clearview AI without any immediate and specific monetary payout for victims. In her ruling, US District Judge Sharon Johnson Coleman said the structure of the accord, which will be the basis for an eventual settlement fund with multiple options, was fair and reasonable. For background, a class action lawsuit was initiated against Clearview for alleged scraping of facial images from the web and sale of that personal information without consent (in violation of Illinois biometric privacy law). The settlement deal has been considered a "novel" resolution because rather than establishing a settlement fund, it provides class action members with a potential total holding of a 23% stake in the company. If Clearview goes public through an IPO or is liquidated through a merger or sale, the fund would be based on a percentage of the company's value. Clearview's current value could be as high as $225 million, which would yield a $51.75 million settlement fund.

[17 March 2025] Hollywood actors sign open letter urging government not to loosen copyright laws for AI:
Over 400 US-based actors, writers, directors, producers, musicians and executives have signed an open letter calling on the US government to uphold copyright laws for the training of AI. The open letter has been sent to the White House Office of Science and Technology (OSTP) in response to public submissions on the US AI Action Plan. The letter challenges recent submissions from OpenAI and Google that claim domestic law either allows or should allow AI companies to train on copyrighted works, without any compensation or permission of copyright owners. The group behind the open letter is led by actress Natasha Lyonne, and includes Bette Midler, Aubrey Plaza, Ava DuVernay, Paul Simon, Mark Ruffalo and hundreds of others.

This development follows the 118th Congress during which the Committee uncovered (1) "how the Biden-Harris Administration repeatedly pressured online platforms to censor Americans directly and by proxy"; and (2) "the Administration's efforts to control AI to suppress speech, such as the efforts to push over a dozen AI companies to mitigate so-called "harmful bias" and "algorithmic discrimination" in the development and use of their AI models".

[12 March 2025] US communications regulator to create council to counter China technology threats:
It is reported that, according to the new chair of the Federal Communications Commission (FCC) Brendan Carr, the FCC is establishing a national security council to address threats from Chinese cyberattacks and to stay ahead in critical technologies like AI. This council aims to mitigate vulnerabilities related to cyberattacks, espionage, and supply chain dependencies on adversarial nations, ensuring the US remains competitive in key technologies such as 5G, AI, and quantum computing. Traditionally, the FCC has been tasked with overseeing telecommunications infrastructure. However, with escalating cyber threats and geopolitical tensions, its mandate is rapidly expanding into national security. The newly created national security council will shift the focus from targeting individual Chinese firms—such as past bans on Huawei and ZTE—to a broader sector-wide strategy. Further details of this council have yet to be revealed.

Defense & National Security
Cybersecurity
[6 March 2025] NIST finalises guidelines for evaluating 'differential privacy' guarantees to de-identify data:
The US National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) has published its finalised Guidelines for Evaluating ‘Differential Privacy’ Guarantees to De-Identify Data (NIST Special Publication 800-226). Differential privacy works by adding random "noise" to the data in a way that obscures the identity of the individuals but keeps the database useful overall as a source of statistical information. However, noise applied in the wrong way can jeopardise privacy or render the data less useful. These guidelines aim to help practitioners of all backgrounds better understand how to think about differentially private software solutions. Multiple factors for consideration are identified in a differential privacy pyramid along with several privacy hazards, which are common pitfalls that arise as the mathematical framework of differential privacy is realized in practice.

Defense & National Security
Cybersecurity
[29 January 2025] US Copyright Office releases Part 2 of AI Report:
The US Copyright Office has released Part 2 of its Report on the legal and policy issues related to copyright and AI. This Part 2 Report addresses the copyrightability of outputs created using generative AI. The Office (1) affirms that existing principles of copyright law are flexible enough to apply to this new technology, as they have applied to technological innovations in the past; (2) concludes that the outputs of generative AI can be protected by copyright only where a human author has determined sufficient expressive elements. This can include situations where a human-authored work is perceptible in an AI output, or a human makes creative arrangements or modifications of the output, but not the mere provision of prompts; (3) confirms that the use of AI to assist in the process of creation or the inclusion of AI-generated material in a larger human-generated work does not bar copyrightability; and (4) finds that the case has not been made for changes to existing law to provide additional protection for AI-generated outputs.

Generative AI
[17 January 2025] FTC releases report examining partnerships of AI and cloud companies:
The Federal Trade Commission (FTC) has issued a report examining the partnerships among AI and cloud service provider (CSP) companies, namely Google, Amazon, Microsoft OpenAI and Anthropic. The report explores important aspects of the structure of CSP and AI developer collaborations, such as the equity and revenue-sharing rights retained by CSPs in these partnerships and certain consultation, control and exclusivity rights that CSPs gain by investing in AI firms. The report also covers potential competition implications, such as how these partnerships could affect access to certain inputs like computing resources and engineering talent, increase switching costs for the AI developer partners as well as provide CSPs access to sensitive technical and business information unavailable to others.

[16 January 2025] Department of Commerce publishes guidelines on open data for generative AI models:
The US Commerce Data Governance Board of the Department of Commerce has released the "Generative AI and Open Data: Guidelines and Best Practices". This guidance provides actionable guidelines and best practices for publishing open data optimized for generative AI systems, namely in relation to: (1) documentation; (2) data and metadata formats; (3) data storage and dissemination; (4) data licensing and usage; and (5) data quality and integrity. While it is designed for use by the Department of Commerce and its bureaus, this guidance has been made publicly available to benefit open data publishers globally.

[15 January 2025] USPTO launches AI Strategy:

Copyright & IP
[15 January 2025] US AI Safety Institute issues updated guidelines for managing risk for dual-use foundation models:
The US AI Safety Institute (US AISI) at the National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) has released the second public draft of its guidelines on Managing Misuse Risk for Dual-Use Foundation Models (NIST AI 800-1), which outlines voluntary best practices for identifying, measuring, and mitigating risks to public safety and national security across the AI lifecycle. The updated guidelines include a number of improvements to the initial public draft (released July 2024), including updates such as (1) detailing best practices for model evaluations; (2) expanding domain-specific guidelines on cyber and chemical and biological risk; (3) underscoring a marginal risk framework; (4) addressing open models; and (5) managing risk across the AI supply chain. The comment period on these updated guidelines is open until 15 March 2025.

[13 January 2025] FTC issues final order against IntelliVision:
The Federal Trade Commission (FTC) has issued a final order in relation to an investigation into IntelliVision Technologies Corporation for alleged misrepresentations around the accuracy and bias of its AI-powered facial recognition software. Under this order, IntelliVision is prohibited from misrepresenting the accuracy and efficacy of its facial recognition software, including its comparative performance in relation to different genders, ethnicities, and skin tones. The order also prohibits Intellivision from making representations about the effectiveness, accuracy, or lack of bias of its technology to detect spoofing. This order follows a previously proposed consent order issued in December 2024.

[10 January 2025] HHS releases AI Strategic Plan:
The US Department of Health and Human Services (HHS) has released its AI Strategic Plan with the vision of becoming a global leader in responsible AI adoption to advance health and well-being. The plan aims to (1) catalyze health AI innovation to improve lives through expanded use cases, infrastructure modernization, and public-private collaboration; (2) promote trustworthy AI development by addressing risks like bias, privacy, and biosecurity; (3) democratize AI technologies, ensuring equitable access to data, tools, and resources; and (4) cultivate AI-empowered workforces through training, talent pipelines, and organizational support.

Data Privacy & Protection
[8 January 2025] FCC's order on Robocall Mitigation Database enters into force:
The Federal Communications Commission’s (FCC) order on improving the effectiveness of the robocall mitigation database (FCC-24-135) has entered into force. The order includes (1) filing requirements for the Robocall Mitigation Database, with a grace period until 1 March 2025, to enhance compliance and awareness among voice service providers regarding their responsibilities to protect consumers; (2) requirements for providers to re-certify annually by 1 March and pay a USD 100 filing fee; and (3) mandate for providers to provide timely updates on company information, with fines of USD 10'000 for false or inaccurate submissions and USD 1'000 for outdated information. To improve the database's reliability and security, the FCC will establish a reporting mechanism, issue additional guidance, and implement two-factor authentication.

Cybersecurity
Online Safety & Child Protection
[7 January 2025] FDA offers new draft guidance to developers of AI-enabled medical devices:
The US Food and Drug Administration (FDA) has published draft guidance regarding the contents of marketing submissions for devices that include AI enabled device software functions including documentation and information that will support the FDA's evaluation of safety and effectiveness. To support the development of appropriate documentation for FDA’s assessment of the device, this draft guidance also proposes recommendations for the design, development, and implementation of AI-enabled devices that sponsors may wish to consider using throughout the total product lifecycle.

Health & Life Sciences
[30 December 2024] FTC approves final order against AI-enabled consumer review platform Sitejabber:
The Federal Trade Commission (FTC) has approved a final order against Sitejabber, the provider of an AI-enabled consumer review platform, prohibiting the company from making or facilitating misrepresentations about ratings and reviews.

Online Safety & Child Protection
[12 December 2024] Trump's pick for FTC chair wants to avoid AI crackdown:
President-elect Donald Trump has picked Andrew Ferguson as the new chair of the Federal Trade Commission (FTC). It is reported that Ferguson, through previous statements, is likely to have the following approach to FTC enforcement priorities: (1) a hands-off approach to regulating AI, based on Ferguson's dissenting statement regarding the social media and video streaming services report that the "pro-regulation side of the AI debate...is the wrong one" (19 September 2024); and (2) confronting Big Tech companies in relation to competition and censorship concerns, based on Ferguson's social media post stating to "end Big Tech’s vendetta against competition and free speech" (X post, 11 December 2024) and other expressed opinions regarding Big Tech platforms’ content moderation around Covid-19 and the 2020 election.

Generative AI
[11 December 2024] US House passes National Defence Authorisation Act into law, covering AI:
The House of Representatives has passed into law the National Defense Authorization Act (NDAA) for Fiscal Year 2025 (FY25). The FY25 NDAA authorizes funding for all discretionary military programs and activities – including personnel, operations, maintenance, procurement, research, and development. Notably, the 2025 NDAA (1) establishes two pilot programs to advance the department wide use of AI, including a five-year initiative to develop security-focused biotechnological applications and another to create AI-driven software for defense manufacturing facilities; and (2) directs the Pentagon to create policy on AI use in nuclear weapons systems.

Defense & National Security
Generative AI
[10 December 2024] FCC makes enforcement order against 2,400 voice service providers who have failed to register with Robocall mitigation database:
The Federal Communications Commission (FCC) filed an order demanding 2,411 voice service providers who have failed to properly file entries in the Robocall Mitigation Database (RMD) to provide evidence for why their entries should not be removed. For background, the RMD monitors compliance with rules to prevent illegal robocalls from reaching consumers. Removal from the RMD could result in loss of call traffic as their calls are blocked by other providers, reputational damage, and further enforcement action from the FCC, including fines or penalties for non-compliance. The FCC has also proposed new measures to uplift the RMD program, including higher fines for non-compliance and a dedicated reporting mechanism for shared oversight among all stakeholders.

Online Safety & Child Protection
Cybersecurity
[3 December 2024] FTC issues consent order on Intellivision regarding facial recognition claims:
The Federal Trade Commission (FTC) has issued a consent order with respect to Intellivision Technologies Corp, in which Intellivision has agreed to refrain from making misrepresentations about the accuracy, efficacy or lack of bias of its facial recognition software, unless it could first substantiate such claims with reliable testing and documentation as set forth in the consent order. For background, the FTC brought an enforcement action against Intellivision over its public statements that its facial recognition software (which is used in home security systems and smart home touch panels) were entirely free of any gender or racial bias as shown by rigorous testing. FTC argued that Intellivision did not have adequate evidence to support the above claim, and that there were research findings to the contrary.

[2 December 2024] House Financial Services Committee leaders eye AI regulatory push:
It is reported that Reps. Patrick McHenry (R-N.C) and Maxine Waters (D-Calif), the chair and ranking member of the committee, respectively, announced the introduction of (1) a resolution to acknowledge the rising use of AI in financial services and in the housing industry, and (2) a bill titled "Analysis and Improvement Act of 2024" that calls on the Federal Reserve, the Federal Deposit Insurance Corp., the Office of the Comptroller of the Currency, the Consumer Financial Protection Bureau and the National Credit Union Administration to deliver a report to the House Financial Services Committee that examines a variety of AI-related issues in the agencies’ respective sectors (including the use of AI in home valuation, loan underwriting and servicing, how banking institutions use AI to identify fraud, money laundering and cybercrime, and how AI is used in debt collection and foreclosures).

[26 November 2024] FTC files lawsuit against Evolv Technologies Holdings, Inc:
The Federal Trade Commission (FTC) has filed a lawsuit in the US District Court (Massachusetts) against Evolv Technologies Holdings, Inc on allegations that Evolv Technologies made misleading claims about the capabilities and performance of its products, specifically in the context of weapon detection and the differentiation between weapons and harmless personal items. This action seeks a permanent injunction and other equitable relief to prevent future deceptive practices in the marketing and sale of AI-developed products.
