Cybersecurity
[22 November 2024] US Justice Department seeks to unwind Google’s partnership with Anthropic:
It has been reported that the US Department of Justice (DOJ) has filed a proposal to the US federal court to bar Google from acquiring, investing in or collaborating with any company that controls where consumers search for information, including query-based AI products. In particular, the DOJ has requested the court to unwind Google’s partnership with AI company Anthropic as well as order Google to divest its web browser product Chrome. The DOJ's proposal comes as part of a broader anti-trust proceeding to curb Google’s alleged monopoly over online search.

Generative AI
[14 November 2024] DHS releases framework for the safe and secure deployment of AI in critical infrastructure:
The Department of Homeland Security (DHS) has released a set of recommendations for the safe and secure development and deployment of AI in critical infrastructure, the "Roles and Responsibilities Framework for Artificial Intelligence in Critical Infrastructure" (Framework). This Framework was developed by and for entities at each layer of the AI supply chain: cloud and compute providers, AI developers, and critical infrastructure owners and operators – as well as the civil society and public sector entities that protect and advocate for consumers.

Data Privacy & Protection
[13 November 2024] Register of Copyrights testifies before the Senate Committee:
The Register of Copyrights of the US Copyright Office Shira Perlmutter has testified before the Senate Committee on Oversight, stating the Copyright Office is still working to get parts 2 and 3 of its promised report on Copyright and Artificial Intelligence out by the end of 2024. Register Perlmutter has not yet revealed the Copyright Office's position on the question whether training AI models with copyrighted works without licenses from the copyright owners is "fair use". However, the Copyright Office will be providing in their upcoming report "a framework for analysis to explain how the fair use doctrine and the various factors the courts must consider should be approached in the context of different fact patterns".

Copyright & IP
Generative AI
[13 November 2024] FinCEN issues alert on fraud schemes involving deepfake media targeting financial institutions:
The US Treasury's Financial Crimes Enforcement Network (FinCEN) has issued an alert to help financial institutions detect and report fraud schemes involving deepfake media created with generative AI. The alert (1) identifies typologies and red flag indicators of such fraud and outlines reporting requirements under the Bank Secrecy Act (BSA); (2) emphasises the risks associated with generative AI, such as identity-related fraud schemes and cybercrimes, which impact anti-money laundering and counter-terrorism efforts; (3) encourages financial institutions to use image and metadata analysis, reverse image searches, and specialised detection software to detect deepfake media; and (4) suggests the implementation of multifactor authentication and live verification to improve identity checks, though criminals may attempt to circumvent these by exploiting technological glitches or switching communication methods.

[12 November 2024] US state attorneys generals adopt letter to FCC on enhanced robocall mitigation database:
47 State Attorneys General across the US have adopted the comment letter to the Federal Communications Commission's (FCC) proposals on enhancing the robocall mitigation database. The letter (1) supports the proposed measures aimed at increasing accountability among voice service providers, especially those handling cross-border call traffic; (2) recommends mandatory multi-factor authentication, regular updates of provider details, and penalties for false filings to curb robocall abuse; and (3) argues in favour of procedural improvements such as data validation tools and filing fees to deter non-compliance.

[12 November 2024] US state attorney generals adopt letter to FCC on robocall mitigations:
47 State Attorneys General across the United States have adopted the comment letter to the Federal Communications Commission's (FCC) proposals on enhancing the robocall mitigation database. The letter (1) supports the proposed measures aimed at increasing accountability among voice service providers, especially those handling cross-border call traffic; (2) recommends mandatory multi-factor authentication, regular updates of provider details, and penalties for false filings to curb robocall abuse; and (3) argues in favour of procedural improvements such as data validation tools and filing fees to deter non-compliance.

Data Privacy & Protection
[30 October 2024] DOC and DOE sign MOU to advance safe, secure, and trustworthy development and use of AI:
The US Department of Commerce (DOC), as represented by the National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST), and the US Department of Energy (DOE), announced a memorandum of understanding (MOU) signed earlier this year to collaborate on safety research, testing, and evaluation of advanced AI models and systems. Through this MOU, the DOC and DOE intend to evaluate the impact of AI models on public safety, including risks to critical infrastructure, energy security, and national security. Key focus areas include developing classified evaluations of advanced AI models’ chemical and biological risks, as well as developing and evaluating evaluate privacy enhancing technologies that aim to protect personal and commercial proprietary data.

Defense & National Security
Data Privacy & Protection
Cybersecurity
[25 October 2024] Copyright Office rejects good-faith AI trustworthiness research as an exemption under DMCA section 1201:
The Librarian of Congress, upon the recommendation of the Register of Copyrights of the US Copyright Office, issued a final rule adopting temporary exemptions to the statutory prohibition on circumvention of technological measures that control access to copyrighted works under section 1201 of the Digital Millennium Copyright Act ("DMCA"). For background, DMCA section 1201 generally makes it unlawful to circumvent technological measures used to prevent unauthorized access to copyrighted works. Every three years, the Copyright Office considers exemptions to section 1201. For this year, among other things, there was a proposed exemption of good-faith AI trustworthiness research which intends to cover the circumvention of safeguards and contract terms on online platforms hosting AI models for the purpose of researching biased and other undesirable outputs. However, the Register concluded that such an exemption was not necessary to allow socially important research and therefore recommended denying the petition. The rule became effective on 28 October 2024.

Copyright & IP
Generative AI
[22 October 2024] Government Accountability Office warns of privacy, transparency issues in commercial generative AI development:
Government Accountability Office (GAO) has published a technology assessment report to US lawmakers on generative AI training, development, and deployment cautions. The report notes (1) that despite the efforts of commercial developers of generative AI technologies to continuously monitor their AI models after deployment, developers are finding that "their models may be susceptible to attacks or may produce outputs that are factually incorrect or exhibit bias"; and (2) developers collect data from a variety of sources to train their generative AI models, but specifics of the training data used by commercial developers are not entirely available to the public.

[21 October 2024] SEC announces 2025 priorities, including AI:
The SEC's Division of Examinations has announced its examination priorities for fiscal year 2025, emphasizing the importance of AI (among other areas) due to its potential risks and impact on market integrity. The Division encourages registrants to assess and improve their compliance programs, particularly concerning emerging technologies like AI, to safeguard investor interests and maintain orderly capital markets - "If advisers integrate AI into advisory operations, including portfolio management, trading, marketing, and compliance, an examination may look in-depth at compliance policies and procedures as well as disclosures to investors related to these areas" (SEC).

Generative AI
[16 October 2024] Department of Labor issues guidance on AI and worker well-being best practices:
The Department of Labor has issued a set of best practices to help employers and AI developers implement ethical standards in AI systems to ensure workers benefit from the new opportunities and are shielded from potential harms of AI. The guidance calls for: (1) centering worker empowerment; (2) ethically developing AI; (3) establishing AI governance and human oversight; (4) ensuring transparency in AI use; (5) protecting labor and employment rights; (6) using AI to enable workers; (7) supporting workers impacted by AI; and (8) ensuring responsible use of worker data.

Data Privacy & Protection
[15 October 2024] FDA publishes paper on its perspective to AI regulation:
The Food and Drug Administration (FDA) has released its perspective on regulating AI in healthcare and biomedicine, stating that oversight needs to be coordinated across all regulated industries, international organizations and the US government. The agency has highlighted that it is coleading an AI working group of the International Medical Device Regulators Forum that both promotes AI best practices globally and leads a working group within the International Council for Harmonisation that works to accommodate AI in clinical trials.

Health & Life Sciences
[3 October 2024] OMB issues guidance to advance the responsible acquisition of AI in government:
The Office of Management and Budget (OMB) has released the "Advancing the Responsible Acquisition of Artificial Intelligence in Government" memo, which builds upon an earlier memo that established the first binding requirements for US agencies to strengthen governance, innovation, and risk management for the use of AI. The new memo establishes acquisition-related practices that agencies must implement to ensure effective deployment of required risk management practices for rights-impacting and safety-impacting AI. The memo calls for agencies to (1) address privacy risks throughout the acquisition lifecycle; (2) ensure that AI-based biometrics protect the public's rights, safety, and privacy; (3) comply with civil rights laws to avoid unlawful bias, unlawful discrimination, and harmful outcomes; (4) identify when solicitations require compliance for rights-impacting and safety-impacting AI; (5) incorporate transparency requirements into contractual terms and solicitations to obtain necessary information and access; (6) delineate responsibilities for ongoing testing and monitoring and build evaluations into vendor contract performance; and (7) require AI incident reporting.

[26 September 2024] FTC fines $6m on a robocall case:
The Federal Communications Commission (FCC) has adopted a $6 million fine against political consultant Steve Kramer for illegal robocalls that used deepfake AI-generated voice cloning technology and caller ID spoofing to spread election misinformation to potential New Hampshire voters prior to the state's January presidential primary election.

[9 September 2024] US Commerce Department proposes requiring reporting for advanced AI, cloud providers:
The US Commerce Department's Bureau of Industry and Security has announced it is proposing to require "frontier AI" model developers and cloud computing providers to report to the federal government about their development activities, cybersecurity measures as well as outcomes from "red-teaming" efforts (e.g. testing for dangerous capabilities including the ability to assist in cyberattacks or lowering barriers to entry for non-experts to develop chemical, biological, radiological, or nuclear weapons). The regulatory push comes as legislative action in the US Congress on AI has stalled.

Defense & National Security
[5 September 2024] UK, US and Canadian nuclear regulators release principles for deploying AI in the nuclear sector:
The UK, US, and Canadian nuclear regulators (The UK Office for Nuclear Regulation, United States Nuclear Regulatory Commission, and Canadian Nuclear Safety Commission) have outlined principles for deploying AI in the nuclear sector. The trilateral paper includes (1) common areas of focus for regulators when approaching AI; (2) understanding how to manage systems based on the consequences of AI failure and the level of AI autonomy; (3) the importance of human and organisational factors in the use of AI; (4) integrating AI into existing nuclear systems; (5) managing the AI lifecycle from design to deployment; and (6) considerations for safety cases for AI in nuclear applications.

Cybersecurity
[29 August 2024] US AI Safety Institute signs MoUs regarding AI safety research, testing and evaluation With Anthropic and OpenAI:
The US AI Safety Institute has announced Memorandums of Understanding (MoU) that will enable formal collaboration on AI safety research with both Anthropic and OpenAI. Each company’s MoU establishes the framework for the US AI Safety Institute to receive access to major new models from each company prior to and following their public release. The agreements will enable collaborative research on how to evaluate capabilities and safety risks, as well as methods to mitigate those risks.

[14 August 2024] The FTC finalizes its rules clamping down on fake online reviews, including bans on fake and AI-generated reviews and testimonials:
The Federal Trade Commission (FTC) has voted unanimously to ban marketers from using fake reviews, such as those generated with AI technology, and other misleading advertising practices. The ban also forbids marketers from exaggerating their own influence by, for example, paying for bots to inflate their follower count. The final rule which will go into effect 60 days after it is published in the Federal Register.

Online Safety & Child Protection
[12 August 2024] CFPB wants to set the rules for how banks use AI on top of existing customer protection laws:
In a letter to the US Treasury Secretary, the Consumer Financial Protection Bureau (CFPB) has outlined its approach to regulating AI and other emerging technologies in the financial sector, emphasising that these technologies must still comply with existing customer protection laws. The CFPB has also mentioned other ideas/initiatives such as (1) providing guidance to make it clear that lenders must provide accurate reasons for credit denials, regardless of the complexity of their models; (2) proposing rules to prevent financial institutions from hoarding personal data and requiring them to share it with other companies at the consumer’s direction; (3) monitoring and testing algorithms used in lending decisions to ensure compliance with anti-discrimination laws; and (4) proposing new federal oversight for large technology companies offering digital wallets and payment apps.

Data Privacy & Protection
Antitrust & Competition
[31 July 2024] US Copyright Office releases report on copyright and AI:
The US Copyright Office has released Part 1 of the Report on Copyright and Artificial Intelligence, examining copyright law and policy issues raised by AI. This Part 1, which will be complemented by additional publications, addresses the topic of digital replicas or deepfakes, including the protection of artistic style. Key points in the report include: (1) calls for new federal legislation to protect against unauthorized digital replicas, advocating for a new federal right that should, among others, be licensable, subject to guardrails, but not assignable, with effective remedies including monetary damages and injunctive relief; and (2) while there are existing laws that might protect against copying artistic style, the report does not recommend including style as protected subject matter under a new federal digital replica law at this time. However, this could change if existing protections are prove inadequate.

Copyright & IP
Generative AI
[30 July 2024] NTIA releases report on dual use foundation models with open weights:
The National Telecommunications and Information Administration (NTIA) has released a report titled "Dual-Use Foundation Models with Widely Available Model Weights". "Open-weight" models allow developers to build upon and adapt previous work, broadening AI tools’ availability to small companies, researchers, nonprofits, and individuals. The report considers the public safety, geopolitical, societal, competition, innovation and research aspects of open-weight models. The report then recommends the US government to develop new capabilities to monitor for potential risks, but refrain from immediately restricting the wide availability of open model weights in the largest AI systems.

Generative AI
Defense & National Security
Antitrust & Competition
[26 July 2024] NIST releases draft guidance on managing misuse risk for dual use foundation models:
The Department of Commerce, through the National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST), has released draft guidance titled "Managing Misuse Risk for Dual-Use Foundation Models (NIST AI 800-1)" to help developers mitigate the risks stemming from generative AI and dual use foundation models. The guidance includes 7 objectives and practices to manage misuse risks: (1) Anticipate potential misuse risk, (2) Establish plans for managing misuse risk, (3) Manage the risks of model theft, (4) Measure the risk of misuse, (5) Ensure that misuse risk is managed before deploying foundation models, (6) Collect and respond to information about misuse after deployment, and (7) Provide appropriate transparency about misuse risk. Other key points from the guidance include (1) identifying and categorizing different types of adversarial attacks, (2) providing metrics for assessing the impact of these attacks on AI performance, (3) offering best practices for mitigating vulnerabilities, and (4) establishing a standardized framework for testing and improving AI system resilience. The guidance is open to public comments until 9 September 2024.

Generative AI
Cybersecurity
[26 July 2024] NIST releases AI testing platform Dioptra:
The Department of Commerce, through the National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST), has released a testing platform called Dioptra designed to help AI system users and developers measure how certain types of attacks can degrade the performance of an AI system. Dioptra supports the Measure function of the NIST AI Risk Management Framework by providing functionality to assess, analyse, and track identified AI risks.

Sandbox
Cybersecurity
[25 July 2024] FCC moves forward with proposal to regulate AI-generated political ads:
Following a 3-2 vote, the Federal Communications Commission (FCC) has advanced a proposal that would require political advertisers to disclose their use of AI in broadcast television and radio ads. The proposal will move into a 30-day public comment period, followed by a 15-day reply period. For noting, dissenting opinions to the proposal included: (1) concerns about the potential chaos and confusion it could cause during an election cycle, (2) arguments that the FCC’s intervention might infringe on free speech protection, and (3) fears that the new regulations could overlap and conflict with the FCC’s jurisdiction.

Generative AI
[23 July 2024] Joint statement on competition in generative AI foundation models and AI products:
The European Commission, UK Competition Markets Authority, US Department of Justice and the US Federal Trade Commission have signed a joint statement on competition in generative AI foundation models and AI products. The statement outlines the competition risks associated with emerging AI business models (i.e. concentrated control of key inputs, entrenching or extending market power in AI related markets, and arrangements involving key players). The statement then sets out principles for protecting competition in the AI ecosystem, namely (1) fair dealing (i.e. identifying exclusionary tactics that undermine competition), (2) interoperability (i.e. emphasizing the importance of interoperability among AI products and services to enhance competition and innovation), and (3) choice (i.e. scrutinising lock-in methods that restrict choice, or investments/partnerships that sidestep merger enforcement).

Antitrust & Competition
Generative AI
[23 July 2024] FTC issues orders to eight companies seeking information on surveillance pricing:
The Federal Trade Commission (FTC) has initiated an inquiry into the practices of eight companies (Mastercard, Revionics, Bloomreach, JPMorgan Chase, Task Software, PROS, Accenture, and McKinsey & Co) involved in offering surveillance pricing products and services. Key points include (1) the potential impact on privacy, competition, and consumer protection, (2) the use of advanced algorithms, AI, and personal information to set targeted prices, (3) the FTC's use of its 6(b) authority to conduct wide-ranging studies, and (4) the aim to shed light on the opaque market of pricing intermediaries and their effects on consumers.

[23 July 2024] House Financial Services Committee holds hearing into AI in financial services and housing:
The House Financial Services Committee, led by Chairman Patrick McHenry (NC-10), has held a hearing on AI applications in financial services and housing. Key points of the hearing include (1) the importance of explainability and transparency in AI systems, (2) the need for standardized descriptions for vendor-provided AI systems, (3) the potential for AI to reduce bias in financial services, and (4) the necessity of enforcing existing anti-discrimination laws as AI adoption increases.

Data Privacy & Protection
[17 July 2024] USPTO adopts guidance update on patent subject matter eligibility, addressing AI-generated innovations:
The United States Patent and Trademark Office (USPTO) has adopted a guidance update on patent subject matter eligibility, specifically addressing innovations in AI and other critical and emerging technologies. The guidance update notes: (1) the necessity of evaluating whether a claim recites an abstract idea or other judicial exception, (2) the importance of integrating the judicial exception into a practical application, (3) the introduction of new examples to assist in applying the guidance, and (4) the focus on AI-assisted inventions and the level of human contribution required for patent eligibility.

Copyright & IP
[16 July 2024] FCC chair proposes new tactics to crack down on AI-generated robocalls:
Federal Communications Commission (FCC) Chair Jessica Rosenworcel has proposed a rule that would require callers to disclose the use of AI on robocalls. The proposal would require callers to obtain prior express consent to disclose that the caller intends to use AI-generated calls, and to disclose to consumers on each call when they receive an AI-generated call. The proposal will be considered by the full commission during an August meeting.

This observation was based on the SEC's updated regulatory agenda for Spring 2024, which indicated that "Conflicts of Interest Associated With the Use of Predictive Data Analytics by Broker-Dealers and Investment Advisers" remained in the "proposed rule stage", suggesting that the SEC intends to gather more feedback on the above rule.

Generative AI
[24 June 2024] CFPB approves rule to ensure accuracy and accountability in the use of AI and algorithms in home appraisals:
The Consumer Financial Protection Bureau (CFPB) has adopted the "Quality Control Standards for Automated Valuation Models" to enhance the accuracy and fairness of home value estimates generated by automated appraisal tools. Companies utilizing these tools must implement safeguards to ensure reliable estimates, prevent data manipulation, avoid conflicts of interest, and adhere to relevant nondiscrimination laws. These standards will become effective one year after their official publication in the Federal Register.

Cybersecurity
[11 June 2024] SEC charges founder of AI recruitment startup Joonko with fraud:
The SEC has charged Joonko (AI recruitment startup), alleging that (1) the company falsely claimed to use AI to help clients find diverse and underrepresented job candidates; and (2) Raz, CEO and founder of Joonko, misled investors by claiming the company had earned over $1 million in revenue and had more than 100,000 active job candidates. In a related action, the US Attorney's Office for the Southern District of New York announced criminal charges against Raz with violating the antifraud provisions of the federal securities laws.

Finance
[10 June 2024] 5th Circuit scraps plans to adopt AI rule:
The 5th US Circuit Court of Appeals (in New Orleans) has decided not to adopt a proposed rule at the appellate level regulating the use of generative AI by lawyers appearing before it. The proposed rule would have required lawyers to certify that, to the extent an AI program was used to generate a filing, citations and legal analysis were reviewed for accuracy. Lawyers who misrepresented their compliance with the rule could face sanctions and the prospect of their filings being stricken. However, this proposed rule was opposed by members of the bar in public comments submitted to the 5th Circuit, arguing that rules already on the books were sufficient to deal with any issues with the technology, including ensuring the accuracy of court filings.

[6 June 2024] FTC investigates Microsoft x Inflection AI deal:
It's been reported that the Federal Trade Commission is investigating Microsoft's recent deal with AI startup Inflection AI to examine if Microsoft deliberately structured it in a manner that would avoid an antitrust review.

Antitrust & Competition
[6 June 2024] US Department of Treasury issues RFI on AI in financial services sector:
The US Department of the Treasury has released a request for information on the uses, opportunities, and risks of Artificial Intelligence (AI) in the financial services sector. This builds on Treasury’s recent work on cybersecurity and fraud in AI and initiatives by other federal agencies. Treasury seeks public comment on AI applications in financial services and the associated opportunities and risks within 60 days.

It's been reported that the US Justice Department and the Federal Trade Commission have reached a deal that allows them to proceed with antitrust investigations into the dominant roles that Microsoft, OpenAI and Nvidia, play in the AI industry.

Generative AI
[30 May 2024] NIST reports on results from age estimation software evaluation:
The National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) concluded its first evaluation of software algorithms designed for estimating a person's age from photographs. This inquiry aimed to assess the performance of six voluntarily submitted algorithms in the context of age verification requirements for AI development sectors. The report found that none of them emerged as a clear leader, but highlighted improvements in age estimation accuracy compared to a decade ago, alongside a commitment to ongoing evaluation and methodological updates to reflect rapid advancements in the field.

Online Safety & Child Protection
[28 May 2024] NIST launched a new program to advance sociotechnical testing and evaluation for AI:
The National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) has launched a new testing, evaluation, validation and verification (TEVV) program intended to help improve understanding of AI’s capabilities and impacts. The program called "Assessing Risks and Impacts of AI" (ARIA) aims to help organizations and individuals determine whether a given AI technology will be valid, reliable, safe, secure, private and fair once deployed. The program comes shortly after several recent announcements by NIST around the 180-day mark of the Executive Order on trustworthy AI and the US AI Safety Institute’s unveiling of its strategic vision and international safety network.

Data Privacy & Protection
Cybersecurity
[24 May 2024] FCC Proposes $6m fine For N.H. Robocalls:
The Federal Communications Commission (FCC) has proposed a $6 million fine for the robocalls spoofing President Joe Biden’s voice earlier this year. If adopted, a new proposal would review whether the FCC should require candidates and issue advertisements to disclose whenever AI-generated content appears in TV and radio ads. But it would not apply to political ads shared on social media.

Generative AI
[22 May 2024] FCC proposes new rules requiring disclosure of AI-generated content in political ads:
US Federal Communications Commission (FCC) Chairperson Jessica Rosenworcel has released a circular proposing new rules related to the use of AI in political advertising. If adopted, the rules would require TV and radio broadcasters to disclose if AI-generated content was used during an advertisement. This proposal aims to (1) seek comment on whether to require an on-air disclosure and written disclosure in broadcasters’ political files when there is AI-generated content in political ads, (2) apply the disclosure rules to both candidate and issue advertisements, (3) request comment on a specific definition of AI-generated content, and (4) apply the disclosure requirements to broadcasters and entities that engage in origination programming, including cable operators, satellite TV and radio providers and section 325(c) permittees.

Generative AI
[21 May 2024] US Secretary of Commerce releases stategic vision on AI Safety:
The US Secretary of Commerce has adopted a strategic vision for the US AI Safety Institute (AISI), which sets out three key goals: (1) advance the science of AI safety; (2) articulate, demonstrate, and disseminate the practices of AI safety; and (3) support institutions, communities, and coordination around AI safety. Under this strategy, the AISI will focus on testing advanced models and systems to identify and evaluate new risks, developing guidelines for assessments and risk mitigation, and conducting and coordinating technical research.

Sandbox
[16 May 2024] US Department of Labor's releases AI principles for employers and developers:
The Department of Labor issued the "Artificial Intelligence and Worker Well-being: Principles for Developers and Employers". The guidelines outline a set of guiding principles aimed at the development and deployment of AI systems across all sectors in the workplace. These principles emphasise worker empowerment, ethical development of AI, clear governance and human oversight, transparency in AI use, protection of labour and employment rights, enabling workers through AI, support for workers impacted by AI, and responsible handling of worker data. The Principles are not intended to be an exhaustive list but instead a guiding framework for businesses. AI developers and employers should review and customize the best practices based on their own context and with input from workers.

Data Privacy & Protection
[30 April 2024] DHS advances efforts to reduce risks at the intersection of AI and chemical, biological, radiological and nuclear threats:
The Countering Weapons of Mass Destruction Office (CWMD) of the Department of Homeland Security (DHS) has issued a report focused on the reduction of risks associated with the misuse of AI in the development or use of chemical, biological, radiological, and nuclear (CBRN) threats. The report notes that (1) AI model developers have implemented internal evaluation and red teaming systems, but varied approaches and the dual-use nature of the science involved lead to inconsistencies; and (2) the limited access to CBRN expertise and above inconsistencies highlight the need for ongoing collaboration among industry, government, and academia to manage AI-related risks.

Defense & National Security
Cybersecurity
[30 April 2024] USPTO inquiry into the impact of AI on certain patentability determinations:
The United States Patent and Trademark Office (USPTO or Office) seeks public comments regarding the impact of the proliferation of AI on prior art, the knowledge of a person having ordinary skill in the art (PHOSITA), and determinations of patentability made in view of the foregoing.

Copyright & IP
[29 April 2024] Department of Energy announces new actions on AI:
The US Department of Energy (DOE) has released a report on the opportunities and challenges in AI with respect to the nation's clean energy economy. DOE has also announced various R&D actions including, among others: (1) a new "VoltAIc" Initiative to use AI to help streamline siting and permitting at the Federal, state, and local level; (2) an initial assessment on the safe, secure, and trustworthy deployment of AI and convening energy stakeholders and technical experts to collaboratively assess potential opportunities and risks of AI to grid resilience; and (3) establishing a working group on powering AI and data center infrastructure.

Cybersecurity
[29 April 2024] NIST release four draft publications on AI, including new guidance for generative AI:
The National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) has released four draft publications, seeking comment by 2 June 2024: (1) the AI RMF Generative AI Profile (NIST AI 600-1); (2) Secure Software Development Practices for Generative AI (NIST SP 800-218A); (3) Reducing Risks Posed by Synthetic Content (NIST AI 100-4); and (4) A Plan for Global Engagement on AI Standards (NIST AI 100-5). These publications are intended to provide guidance for safely harnessing the potential of AI while minimizing associated risks.

Cybersecurity
[10 April 2024] USPTO reaffirms existing rules apply to AI-crafted submissions:
The US Patent and Trademark Office (USPTO) has published guidance outlining existing rules and regulations for entrepreneurs, legal professionals, and other stakeholders who use AI in their submissions. The guidance covers scenarios such as using AI software for document drafting, disclosure duties when using AI tools, and filing documents with the USPTO. Violations of USPTO rules through improper use of AI systems could lead to penalties such as revocation of a user's USPTO.gov account, as well as criminal, civil, or administrative liabilities. The USPTO is also collaborating with Commerce Secretary Gina Raimondo and other federal agencies to shape AI and intellectual property policy.

Copyright & IP
[27 March 2024] NTIA calls for independent audits of AI systems in new accountability report:
The National Telecommunications and Information Administration (NTIA) has called for independent audits of high-risk AI systems, as part of a series of recommendations in the "AI Accountability Policy Report". The Report makes 8 set of policy recommendations across 3 categories: Guidance, Support and Regulations. Notably, the Report calls for (1) audit guidelines; (2) disclosure information standards (e.g. model cards or 'nutrition label' style disclosures); (3) liability standards; (4) investment into US AI Safety Institute and National AI Research Resource; (5) more research into AI assessment tools; (6) independent audits and regulatory inspections of high risk AI models and systems; (7) boost government capacity across sectors; (8) requirement for government suppliers/contractors/grantees to adopt AI governance and assurance practices.

National Strategy
[26 March 2024] US Copyright Office plans AI-related amendments to copyright rules:
The Copyright Office has initiated a comprehensive examination of the impact of generative AI on copyright law and policy. A section on this topic will be published later in Spring 2024, with later sections focusing on training AI models on copyrighted works, licensing considerations, and liability issues.

Generative AI
[18 March 2024] SEC charges two investment advisers with making false and misleading statements about their use of AI:
The Securities and Exchange Commission has announced that it has settled charges against Delphia (USA) Inc. and Global Predictions Inc., two investment advisers, for making false and misleading statements about their use of AI. The SEC emphasized that investment advisers should not mislead the public by claiming to use AI when they are not. Delphia agreed to pay a civil penalty of $225,000, and Global Predictions agreed to pay a civil penalty of $175,000.

Generative AI
[15 March 2024] FTC inquiry into Reddit's AI-related deals ahead of IPO:
A few days ahead of its IPO, Reddit has been notified by the US Federal Trade Commission that they are investigating the company's AI training deals. In its filing to the SEC, Reddit disclosed that FTC is conducting a non-public inquiry focused on Reddit's sale, licensing, or sharing of user-generated content with third parties to train AI models.

Generative AI
[1 March 2024] FTC opens consultation into proposed amendments to Trade Regulation Rule on Impersonation of Government:
The Federal Trade Commission (FTC) has opened the public consultation on its notice of proposed rulemaking on amendments to the Trade Regulation Rule. The proposed amendment aims to (1) extend protections of the Trade Regulation Rule on Impersonation of Government and Businesses to individuals in order to address the increased use of technologies, such as AI, which harm consumers, and (2) extend liability to entities supplying goods and services, such as providers of AI tools, if they have knowledge or reasonable awareness that these goods or services will be used in unlawful impersonations. The public consultation ends on 30 April 2024.

[15 February 2024] FTC seeks to ban AI deepfakes-enabled fraud:
The Federal Trade Commission has finalised a rule that would enable it to directly seek monetary relief in federal court from scammers engage in certain business and government impersonation scams. The FTC is now seeking to extend that rule to prohibit the impersonation of individuals (including via AI-generated deepfakes). The FTC is also seeking public comment on whether the revised rule should declare it unlawful for a firm, such as an AI platform that creates images, video, or text, to provide goods or services that they know or have reason to know is being used to harm consumers through impersonation.

[13 February 2024] US Patent and Trademark Office clarify patentability of inventions assisted by AI:
The US Patent and Trademark Office (USPTO) has released guidance clarifying that AI-assisted inventions are "not categorically unpatentable", and may be patented provided that a "natural person provided a significant contribution to the invention". This guidance is subject to public comment.

[13 February 2024] FTC says it will go after companies that 'quietly' change privacy policies to mine user data for AI:
The Federal Trade Commission (FTC) warned in its blog post that it will strictly enforce how AI firms and other companies treat their terms of service and will pursue those who “quietly” change them to exploit data to enhance their AI tools.

Generative AI
[8 February 2024] FCC makes AI-generated voices in robocalls illegal:
The Federal Communications Commission (FCC) announced the unanimous adoption of a Declaratory Ruling that recognizes calls made with AI-generated voices are "artificial" under the Telephone Consumer Protection Act (TCPA). The ruling, which takes effect immediately, makes voice cloning technology used in common robocall scams targeting consumers illegal. This would give State Attorneys General across the country new tools to go after bad actors behind these nefarious robocalls.

[6 February 2024] New Senate bill aims to kill proposed SEC rule on AI conflicts of interest:
Senators Bill Hagerty and Ted Cruz introduced the Protecting Innovation in Investment Act which aims to bar the Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC)'s new proposed rules requiring broker-dealers and investment advisers to identify and eliminate conflict of interests arising from their use of AI tools (e.g. predictive data analytics). Senator Hagerty said in his press release that "American consumers will ultimately bear the cost of yet another SEC attempt to overregulate financial markets", and that this Senate bill is to "protect Americans' affordable access to financial markets".

The CEOs of the biggest social media companies - Meta, Tiktok, X, Snap and Discord - were questioned by the US Senate Judiciary Committee over issues of child online safety. Part of the hearing focused on the impact of AI-based content recommendation algorithms on child users.

[29 January 2024] US Department of Commerce issues proposed rule impacting AI and IaaS providers to counter foreign malicious actors:
The Secretary of Commerce (Secretary) has issued a notice proposing regulations (1) requiring US Infrastructure as a Service (IaaS) providers to verify the identity of their foreign customers, along with procedures for the Secretary to grant exemptions; and authorize special measures to deter foreign malicious cyber actors' use of US IaaS products; and (2) requiring providers of certain IaaS products to submit a report to the Secretary when a foreign person transacts with that provider or reseller to train a large AI model with potential capabilities that could be used in malicious cyber-enabled activity.

[19 December 2023] FTC bans Rite Aid from using facial recognition:
FTC has banned Rite Aid's facial recognition technology which falsely tagged consumers, particularly women and people of color, as shoplifters (and without reasonable safeguards). The ban will last five years.

Data Privacy & Protection
[13 December 2023] HHS Finalizes Rule to Advance Health IT Interoperability and Algorithm Transparency:
The US Department of Health and Human Services (HHS) through the Office of the National Coordinator for Health Information Technology (ONC) finalised its 'Health Data, Technology, and Interoperability: Certification Program Updates, Algorithm Transparency, and Information Sharing' (HTI-1) rule. This follows the release of the HTI-1 proposed rule in April 2023. Among other things, the HTI-1 final rule imposes transparency requirements for AI and other predictive algorithms that are part of certified health IT.

[27 November 2023] UK and US develop new global guidelines for AI security:
The UK National Cyber Security Centre (NCSC) and the US Cybersecurity and Infrastructure Security Agency (CISA) (in cooperation with industry experts and 21 other international agencies and ministries) launched the 'Guidelines for Secure AI System Development' that will help developers of any systems that use AI make informed cyber security decisions at every stage of the development process. The guidelines focus on 4 key areas: (1) secure design, (2) secure development, (3) secure deployment, and (4) secure operation and maintenance.

[21 November 2023] FTC Authorizes Compulsory Process for AI-related Products and Services:
The Federal Trade Commission has approved an omnibus resolution authorizing the use of compulsory process in nonpublic investigations involving products and services that use or claim to be produced using AI or claim to detect its use. Compulsory process in investigations at the FTC refers to the authority of the FTC to compel individuals, organizations, or entities to provide information, documents, and testimony relevant to an ongoing investigation.

[31 August 2023] US Copyright Office seeks public opunion on copyright and AI-generated works:
The US Copyright Office is undertaking a study of the copyright law and policy issues raised by AI systems. The Office seeks comment on issues around generative AI, including how AI models use copyrighted material in their training data, whether AI-generated works can be copyrighted without human involvement, the potential liability for infringing work generated by AI, and how to deal with AI-generated work that imitates the style of a human artist.

[7 May 2026] US and China to pursue guardrails to prevent AI rivalry crisis at upcoming presidential summit:
It is reported that Washington and Beijing are considering launching official discussions on AI, with potential inclusion on the agenda for an upcoming US-China summit between President Donald Trump and President Xi Jinping, as reported by the Wall Street Journal. The discussions will focus on the risks associated with erratic AI models, autonomous military systems, and AI-driven attacks by non-state actors. Treasury Secretary Scott Bessent will lead the American side, while China has yet to appoint its representative. This initiative follows increasing concerns regarding AI's role in autonomous weapons and large-scale cyberattacks, highlighted by AI startup Anthropic's decision to withhold its advanced model, Mythos, due to its potential to enable widespread cyberattacks.

Cybersecurity
[1 May 2026] US, Australia, Canada, New Zealand and UK release joint guidance on careful adoption of agentic AI services:
The U.S. Cybersecurity and Infrastructure Security Agency, the National Security Agency, the Australian Signals Directorate’s Australian Cyber Security Centre, the Canadian Centre for Cyber Security, New Zealand’s National Cyber Security Centre and the United Kingdom’s National Cyber Security Centre have jointly released a comprehensive roadmap outlining a strategic approach to AI adoption, focusing on five key areas: responsibly utilizing AI to enhance its mission, ensuring the security of AI systems, protecting critical infrastructure from malicious AI use, fostering collaboration with interagency and international partners, and expanding AI expertise within its workforce. This initiative aligns with Executive Order 14110, emphasizing the safe and trustworthy development and use of AI, and underscores CISA's commitment to integrating AI technologies while mitigating associated risks to national cybersecurity and critical infrastructure.

Agentic AI
[17 March 2026] Japan and US eye joint development of AI shipbuilding robots:
It is reported that the US and Japan have initiated discussions to jointly develop AI technologies for shipbuilding robots, aiming to enhance efficiency and address labor shortages in the shipbuilding industry. This collaboration reflects a broader trend of international partnerships leveraging AI and robotics to modernize industrial processes. For instance, in May 2025, HD Hyundai Robotics and Persona AI signed an agreement to develop humanoid welding robots for shipbuilding automation, with prototype humanoids expected by the end of 2026 and full commercial deployment in 2027. Additionally, in 2018, TSUNEISHI SHIPBUILDING Co., Ltd. and Carnegie Mellon University presented results from their joint research on integrating IoT and robotics into shipbuilding, focusing on areas such as automatic hull cleaning systems and welding robots for double bottom blocks. These initiatives underscore a global movement towards integrating advanced technologies into shipbuilding to improve productivity and safety.

Defense & Security
Robotics
[6 March 2026] US mulls new rules for AI chip exports, including requiring US investments by foreign firms:
It is reported that the US Commerce Department has drafted regulations that would require companies to obtain US approval for exporting AI chips globally. This proposed framework would mandate that firms like Nvidia and AMD seek permission for nearly all AI accelerator exports, expanding current restrictions from approximately 40 countries to a worldwide scope. The regulations introduce a tiered approval process: shipments of up to 1,000 units of Nvidia's latest GB300 GPUs would undergo a relatively straightforward review, while larger deployments would necessitate more stringent scrutiny, including potential conditions such as foreign governments investing in US AI infrastructure or providing security assurances. For deployments exceeding 200,000 units in a single country, the host nation's government would need to be involved, with approvals granted only to allies making significant security commitments and matching investments in American AI. These measures aim to control the proliferation of advanced AI capabilities and maintain U.S. leadership in the sector.

Chips & Data Centres
Trade & Investment
[5 March 2026] US, Japan, New Zealand, South Korea, Singapore, UK and Canada join Australia's guidance on supply chain risks and mitigations for AI:
The Canadian Centre for Cyber Security, Japan’s National Cybersecurity Office, New Zealand National Cyber Security Centre, South Korea's National Intelligence Service, Singapore's Cyber Security Agency, UK's National Cyber Security Centre, US’ National Security Agency have joined the Australian Cyber Security Centre's guidance on the supply chain risks and mitigations associated with AI and machine learning (ML) systems, emphasizing the importance of secure management to protect against cyber threats that can arise from third-party datasets and pre-trained models. This guidance targets organizations involved in AI and ML development, highlighting the need for comprehensive risk assessments throughout the lifecycle of AI products, including supplier evaluations, data integrity checks, and the establishment of clear communication channels regarding cybersecurity responsibilities. It outlines specific risks such as data poisoning, model serialisation attacks, and vulnerabilities in AI software, while recommending mitigations like using trusted data sources, implementing secure file formats, and conducting ongoing performance testing. The guidance aims to enhance the resilience of AI and ML supply chains by integrating cybersecurity best practices tailored to the unique challenges posed by these technologies.

Cybersecurity
[6 February 2026] US, China opt out of joint declaration on AI use in military:
Thirty-five countries have signed a declaration at the Responsible AI in the Military Domain (REAIM) summit in A Coruña, Spain, establishing 20 principles for the governed deployment of AI in warfare. While major signatories such as Canada, France, Britain, and South Korea affirmed human responsibility over AI weapons and the necessity of clear command chains, China and the US opted out of the non-binding agreement. The declaration, which includes guidelines on risk assessments, national oversight sharing, and personnel training, saw a decrease in endorsement compared to previous summits in The Hague and Seoul, reflecting growing hesitation amid geopolitical uncertainty and the challenge of balancing innovation with the prevention of unintended military escalation.

Defense & Security
[4 February 2026] Nvidia AI chip sales to China stalled by US security review:
It is reported that Nvidia has encountered a regulatory delay as sales of its H200 AI chips to China remain in limbo nearly two months after initial US presidential approval, primarily due to an ongoing national security review involving the US Departments of State, Defense, and Energy. While the Commerce Department eased export curbs in January 2026 and completed its specific analysis, the State Department is reportedly advocating for stricter conditions to prevent the technology from being used in ways that could undermine US interests. Consequently, Chinese customers are withholding orders until licensing terms and conditions are finalized, even though China recently approved its first batch of these chips for import to balance domestic AI development with technological needs. Although Nvidia CEO Jensen Huang expressed optimism that the licensing process is nearing completion, the conflicting interests between US security departments and the specific export requirements continue to stall the transition of these high-powered processors into the Chinese market.

[16 January 2026] Israel and US sign joint statement on AI:
Israel and the US have signed a Joint Statement in the field of Artificial Intelligence. This follows Israel's joining the Pax Silica initiative in December 2025, which unites leading nations in the field of AI. Out of the nine leading nations in this sector, Israel was selected to be the first country to sign a joint statement with the US. Under the joint statment, the countries will expand bilateral cooperation beyond AI into critical sectors such as semiconductors, quantum computing, space exploration, and energy storage. This alliance is designed to secure global supply chains and protect sensitive technologies through joint research, investment, and commercialization efforts.

National Strategy
[15 January 2026] US and Taiwan sign deal on reshoring of semiconductors to the US:
The American Institute in Taiwan has signed a historic trade agreement with the Taipei Economic and Cultural Representative Office to drive a massive reshoring of the US semiconductor sector and strengthen domestic economic resilience. This strategic partnership mandates at least $250 billion in direct investments from Taiwanese technology enterprises into U.S. production facilities for semiconductors, energy, and artificial intelligence, supplemented by an additional $250 billion in credit guarantees to establish a robust industrial ecosystem. The deal includes the creation of world-class industrial parks within the United States and facilitates American investment in Taiwan’s defense, telecommunications, and biotechnology sectors to deepen technological collaboration. To ensure balanced trade, the agreement implements a predictable tariff framework where U.S. reciprocal rates on Taiwanese goods are capped at 15 percent, while providing zero percent tariffs for aircraft components and generic pharmaceuticals. Furthermore, the pact incentivizes domestic manufacturing by allowing Taiwanese companies to import specific quantities of semiconductors duty-free based on their progress in building and completing new production capacity on American soil. This initiative aims to reverse the long-term decline of the US share of global wafer fabrication and secure the foundational components necessary for modern telecommunications, automobiles, and military hardware.

Trade & Investment
Chips & Data Centres
[14 January 2026] US approves Nvidia H200 chip exports to China, with conditions:
The US government through the Department of Commerce has published a regulation approving the export of Nvidia's H200 AI chips to China under the conditions that (1) the chips will be reviewed by a third-party testing lab to confirm their technical AI capabilities before they can be shipped to China, which cannot receive more than 50% of the total amount of chips sold to US customers; and (2) Nvidia will need to certify that (a) there are enough H200s in the US, and (b) Chinese customers has demonstrated "sufficient security procedures" and cannot use the chips for military purposes. Those conditions had not been established previously. This decision marks a significant shift from previous restrictions aimed at limiting China's access to advanced AI hardware. The approval process involved an inter-agency review, and the final decision was made by President Trump. Chinese regulators have yet to formally approve the imports, and there is speculation that they may impose conditions, such as requiring a proportion of domestic chips to be purchased alongside the H200.

The meeting focused on fostering joint initiatives with high economic impact, specifically targeting the development of digital capabilities, the empowerment of national talent, and the strengthening of the technology-innovation and entrepreneurship ecosystem.

Generative AI
[14 January 2026] EMA and FDA set common principles for AI in medicine development:
The European Medicines Agency (EMA) and the US Food and Drug Administration (FDA) have jointly established ten principles for the responsible use of AI throughout the medicines lifecycle. These principles provide broad guidance on AI applications in evidence generation and monitoring, spanning from early research and clinical trials to manufacturing and safety surveillance. Aimed at medicine developers and marketing authorization holders, the principles are intended to underpin future AI guidance within their respective jurisdictions and foster enhanced international collaboration among regulators, technical standard organizations, and other stakeholders. This initiative builds upon the EMA's AI reflection paper published in 2024 and aligns with the European Commission's Biotech Act proposal, which highlights AI's potential to expedite the development of safe and effective medicines.

[12 January 2026] Qatar and UAE to join US Pax Silica to bolster technology supply chain:
It is reported that, according to Undersecretary of State for Economic Affairs Jacob Helberg, Qatar and the United Arab Emirates will soon join Pax Silica, a U.S.-led initiative to secure AI and semiconductor supply chains. Qatar is expected to sign the Pax Silica declaration on 12 January, followed by the UAE on 15 January. The move comes against the backdrop of The Future Minerals Forum, a government‑led global minerals and supply chain conference hosted by Saudi Arabia that will bring together senior officials, industry leaders and investors in Riyadh from 13-15 January. Helberg said the Pax Silica group will focus this year on expanding membership, building strategic projects to secure supply chains and coordinating policies to protect critical infrastructure and technology. Discussions are under way on projects that could modernize trade and logistics routes, including the India-Middle East-Europe Corridor, using advanced US technology to boost regional integration and expand America’s economic footprint.

[10 January 2026] Vice President JD Vance backs UK over ‘unacceptable’ sexualised AI images on X:
It is reported that US Vice President JD Vance considers the sexualized manipulation of images of women and children by the Grok AI chatbot to be "entirely unacceptable," as stated by UK Deputy Prime Minister David Lammy following their recent discussions. This issue has sparked significant controversy, with Elon Musk, owner of X and developer of Grok, accusing the UK government of attempting to suppress free speech after ministers threatened actions that could potentially block the platform. The UK government, supported by regulator Ofcom, is considering measures against X due to Grok's generation of explicit images, including those involving minors. Ofcom is conducting an expedited assessment of the companies' responses to these concerns.

[19 December 2025] US launches review of advanced Nvidia AI chip sales to China:
It is reported that, according to inside sources, the Trump administration has initiated an inter-agency review to authorize the export of Nvidia’s H200 AI chips to China, a move that reverses long-standing restrictions on high-end semiconductor sales. Under this proposal, the U.S. government would collect a 25% fee on the shipments, with President Trump arguing that providing American hardware will maintain U.S. technological dominance by reducing Chinese reliance on domestic chipmakers. The Department of Commerce has referred license applications to the State, Energy, and Defense Departments for a 30-day evaluation period; however, while officials emphasize the review will be rigorous, the final decision-making authority rests with the President. This shift marks a significant pivot from the previous administration’s policy of strictly limiting Chinese access to advanced technology to mitigate national security risks.

Defense & National Security
[16 December 2025] US suspends technology deal with UK:
It is reported that the US has suspended a technology deal it struck with Britain earlier this year which was intended to boost ties in AI, quantum computing and civil nuclear energy. According to inside sources, US President Donald Trump's administration had been pushing for Britain's concessions in areas of trade outside the tech partnership but were becoming increasingly frustrated with UK's lack of willingness to address so-called non-tariff barriers, including rules and regulations governing food and industrial goods. Official details have yet to be announced.

Generative AI
[11 December 2025] US introduces Pax Silicia Initiative (with coalition of other countries):
The US Department of State has launched the Pax Silica Initiative, being a coalition of countries to build a "secure, prosperous, and innovation driven silicon supply chain—from critical minerals and energy inputs to advanced manufacturing, semiconductors, AI infrastructure, and logistics". The initiative aims to reduce coercive dependencies, protect the materials and capabilities foundational to AI, and ensure aligned nations can develop and deploy transformative technologies at scale. The inaugural Pax Silica Summit convenes counterparts from: Japan, Republic of Korea, Singapore, the Netherlands, The United Kingdom, Israel, United Arab Emirates, and Australia. Countries will partner on securing strategic stacks of the global technology supply chain, including, but not limited to: software applications and platforms, frontier foundation models, information connectivity and network infrastructure, compute and semiconductors, advanced manufacturing, transportation logistics, minerals refining and processing, and energy. Countries affirmed a shared commitment to: (1) pursue projects to jointly address AI supply chain opportunities and vulnerabilities in: priority critical minerals. semiconductor design, fabrication, and packaging, logistics and transportation, compute, and energy grids and power generation; (2) pursue new joint ventures and strategic co-investment opportunities; (3) protect sensitive technologies and critical infrastructure from undue access or control by countries of concern; and (4) build trusted technology ecosystems, including ICT systems, fiber-optic cables, data centers, foundational models and applications.

[9 December 2025] International Network of AI Safety Institutes rebrand away from "safety" to focus on scientific measurements:
It is reported that the International Network of AI Safety Institutes, comprising countries such as Australia, Canada, the EU, France, Japan, Kenya, South Korea, Singapore, the UK, and the US, is rebranding to the International Network for Advanced AI Measurement Evaluation and Science to emphasize its commitment to the scientific measurement and evaluation of AI models (following UK-led calls to move away from the 'safety' label). The UK will assume the role of network coordinator, aiming to lead efforts in developing rigorous methods for testing advanced AI systems.

[3 December 2025] CISA and International Partners issue joint guidance on securely integrating AI into operational technology:
The US Cybersecurity and Infrastructure Security Agency (CISA), along with partners including Australia, released joint guidance to help critical infrastructure owners and operators securely integrate AI into Operational Technology (OT) systems, recommending the establishment of AI governance frameworks, continuous model testing, and embedding security throughout the AI lifecycle to balance efficiency gains with unique risks to safety and security.

Sources say that the Commerce Department is reviewing a change to its policy of barring sales of such chips to China. The White House nor the Commerce Department have made an official comment.

Defense & National Security
[19 November 2025] US approves sale of 70,000 AI chips to UAE and Saudi Arabia:
The US Commerce Department has announced the approval of the sale of up to 70,000 advanced AI chips to companies in the UAE and Saudi Arabia. Under the deal, US companies will be permitted to sell up to 35,000 of NVIDIA Corporation’s GB300 servers or equivalent products to G42, a state-run AI company based in Abu Dhabi, and Humain, a Saudi government-backed AI venture. The GB300 server contains Nvidia’s Blackwell B300 processor, an advanced chip. The approvals come following discussions between President Trump and leaders of both countries, with agreements including security provisions designed to prevent the chips from benefiting China and tech company Huawei. This approval represents a policy shift from earlier in 2025 when some Trump administration officials had rejected exporting directly to state-backed companies due to security concerns.

Defense & National Security
[19 November 2025] US and Saudi Arabia sign strategic AI partnership:
President Donald J. Trump and Crown Prince Mohammed bin Salman of Saudi Arabia have finalised landmark agreements to deepen the U.S.-Saudi strategic partnership, including increasing Saudi investment commitments in the US to nearly $1 trillion, and signing agreements on civil nuclear energy cooperation, critical minerals collaboration, and AI, all aimed at enhancing economic ties. Relevantly, the US and Saudi Arabia have signed a Memorandum of Understanding that encompasses the supply of advanced semiconductors, the development of AI applications, building and developing advanced AI infrastructure, building national capabilities, and expanding high-value investments between the two countries.

Generative AI
[6 November 2025] US to block Nvidia's sale of scaled-down AI chips to China:
It is reported based on inside sources that the US White House has informed other federal agencies that it will not permit Nvidia to sell its latest scaled-down AI chips to China. The chip, known as the B30A, can be utilized to train large language models when efficiently arranged in large clusters, a capability many Chinese companies require. It is reported that Nvidia has provided samples of the B30A chip to several of its Chinese customers.

Defense & National Security
[4 November 2025] US approves Microsoft licence to export AI chips to UAE:
It is announced through Microsoft’s official press release that the US government has granted Microsoft a license to export AI chips to the United Arab Emirates. Microsoft is one of the few companies to secure export licenses from the US Commerce Department to ship GPUs to the UAE. These licenses enable Microsoft to ship the equivalent of 60,400 additional A100 chips, in this instance involving Nvidia’s even more advanced GB300 GPUs.

Chips & Data Centres
[3 November 2025] Trump says China, other countries can’t have Nvidia’s top AI chips:
It is reported that, in a CBS interview and remarks aboard Air Force One, US President Donald Trump has declared that Nvidia's advanced Blackwell AI chips will be exclusively available to US companies, barring China and other nations from access. President Trump emphasised that only the US should possess these top-tier semiconductors. While the President did not rule out the possibility of China obtaining a less advanced version, he stated that the most sophisticated Blackwell chips would not be shared internationally.

[29 October 2025] US signs Technology Prosperity Deals with Japan and South Korea:
The US has signed Technology Prosperity Deals (TPD) with Japan and South Korea, aiming to enhance collaboration in science and technology sectors such as AI, civil nuclear energy, and quantum computing. Each TPD agreement will establish joint initiatives between the nations' premier research institutions (i.e. US Center for AI Safety Institute, Korea AI Safety Institute, and Japan AI Institute) as well as coordinate US-Korean and US-Japan AI exports.

National Strategy
[8 October 2025] UK MHRA and US DFA to forge new collaboration on medical technologies and AI:
UK's Medicines and Healthcare products Regulatory Agency (MHRA) and the US Food and Drug Administration (FDA) will enhance collaboration to accelerate innovation, strengthen patient safety, and reduce transatlantic barriers in medical technology and AI. This includes the launch of the MHRA's National AI Commission, featuring experts from both countries, to guide the safe and transparent use of AI in healthcare. Additionally, new international reliance routes will facilitate faster UK market access for medical devices approved by trusted regulators, such as the FDA. These initiatives aim to harmonize regulations and expedite patient access to cutting-edge medical technologies.

Generative AI
[24 September 2025] US rejects international AI governance at UN Security meeting:
The US, represented by Michael Kratsios (Assistant to the President and OSTP Director), addressed the United Nations Security Council's open debate on AI, stating that the US "totally reject all efforts by international bodies to assert centralized control and global governance of AI", and that "the path to this world is found not in bureaucratic management, but in the freedom and duty of citizens, the prudence and cooperation of statesmen, and the independence and sovereignty of nations". Kratsios further stated that the US believes "broad overregulation incentivizes centralization, stifles innovation, and increases the danger that these tools will be used for tyranny and conquest. Ideological fixations on social equity, climate catastrophism, and so-called existential risk are dangers to progress and obstacles to responsibly harnessing this technology as an extension of human ingenuity and capacities".

Antitrust & Competition
[18 September 2025] US and UK signed memorandum of understanding on Technology Prosperity Deal, covering AI:
The governments of the United States and the United Kingdom have signed a memorandum of understanding (MoU) on the Technology Prosperity Deal. The MoU applies to private sector actors and research institutions in AI, civil nuclear, fusion, quantum technologies, 6G, and advanced telecommunications. It sets a framework for joint research, shared infrastructure, standards development, AI policy alignment, commercial partnerships, workforce development, secure supply chains, and export promotion. The MoU also provides that Ministerial-Level Working Group will be established within six months, and annual discussions will assess progress.

Cybersecurity
[14 August 2025] US embeds trackers in AI chip shipments to catch diversions to China, sources say:
It is reported according to anonymous sources that US authorities have secretly placed location tracking devices in targeted shipments of advanced chips they see as being at high risk of illegal diversion to China. Sources say that the trackers aim to detect AI chips being diverted to destinations which are under US export restrictions, and help build cases against people and companies who profit from violating US export controls.

Defense & National Security
[8 August 2025] President Trump reveals plans to levy 100% tariff on semiconductors, unless companies are building in the US:
President Trump has announced that US will impose a 100% tariff on imports of semiconductors subject to an exemption that it will not apply to companies that are manufacturing in the US or have committed to do so. It is hinted that this exemption will apply to companies like Apple, Nvidia, GlobalFoundries and others who have committed funds towards or pledged to manufacture semiconductor products in the US. President Trump's announcement was, however, not a formal tariff announcement, and much remains unclear about how companies and countries around the world will be impacted.

[4 August 2025] 2025 APEC Digital and AI Ministerial Statement:
At the APEC summit in Incheon, South Korea, the Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation adopted the 2025 Digital and AI Ministerial Statement, highlighting the role of AI in driving innovation and addressing socio-economic challenges. The statement emphasises secure and responsible adoption of AI and other digital technologies to enhance productivity, efficiency, resilience, and economic development. It encourages member economies to integrate these technologies with balanced, human-centred approaches to workforce development, education, and lifelong learning. It also promotes cooperation and information-sharing on digital policies to strengthen regional collaboration, cross-border trade, and investment, while fostering greater understanding of the benefits of emerging technologies.

[4 July 2025] US reportedly plans to curb sales of AI GPUs to Malaysia and Thailand to prevent smuggling to China:

Exemptions are expected for firms based in the US or allied nations to reduce disruption, especially for manufacturing processes like chip packaging. [15 May 2025] US and UAE secure $200 billion in deals, including an AI acceleration partnership:

During the visit, Trump and Sheikh Mohamed also attended the unveiling of a new 5GW AI campus, which would be the largest outside the US.

Defense & National Security
[13 May 2025] Saudi Arabia commits $600 billion investment in US, covering AI:
As part of its tour to the Gulf states, the US White House has announced Saudi Arabia’s $600-billion commitment to invest in the US, building economic ties that will endure for generations to come. The first deals under the announcement will aim to strengthen US energy security, defense industry, technology leadership, and access to global infrastructure and critical minerals. Notably, under this deal, (1) Saudi Arabian firm DataVolt will invest $20bn in AI data centers and energy infrastructure in the US; (2) Alphabet’s Google, DataVolt, Oracle, Salesforce, Advanced Micro Devices and Uber will invest $80bn in transformative technologies in both countries; and (3) Nvidia will sell AI chips in Saudi Arabia, with a first tranche of 18,000 of its newest “Blackwell” chips going to Humain, Saudi Arabia’s sovereign-wealth-fund-owned AI startup.

Chips & Data Centres
Logistics & Infrastructure
[13 May 2025] BIS issues policy statement clarifying export controls on AI related integrated circuits:
The US Bureau of Industry and Security (BIS) has issued a policy statement clarifying that certain activities involving advanced computing integrated circuits (ICs) and related commodities used to train AI models may require an export authorisation under the Export Administration Regulations. These activities are: (1) exports, reexports, or transfers (in-country) of advanced computing ICs and commodities subject to the EAR to any party, such as foreign Infrastructure as a Service (IaaS) providers (e.g., data center providers), when the exporter, reexporter, or transferor has “knowledge” that the IaaS provider will use these items to conduct training of AI models for or on behalf of parties headquartered in D:5 countries (including China) or Macau; (2) transfers (in-country), defined as a change in end use or end user, of advanced computing ICs and commodities subject to the EAR already in the possession of parties such as IaaS providers, if there is “knowledge” that the items will be used by the transferee to train AI models for or on behalf of parties headquartered in D:5 countries (including China) or Macau; and (3) a “U.S. person” provides any ‘support’ or performs any contract, service, or employment, when there is “knowledge” such activity will be used for or may assist the training of AI models for or on behalf of parties headquartered in D:5 countries (including China) or Macau.

Defense & National Security
[30 April 2025] Trump officials plan changes to Biden's AI chip export rule:
It is reported that according to internal sources, the Trump administration is working on changes to a Biden-era 'Framework for Artificial Intelligence Diffusion' rule which is set to go into effect on 15 May 2025 to limit global access to AI chips under a three-tiered system. The sources suggest that the administrarion is planning to remove the tiered system, and replacing it with a global licensing regime with government-to-government agreements to regulate access to US AI chips (potentially as a negotiating tool in trade talks). The plans are still under discussion and subject to change.

Defense & National Security
[29 April 2025] US government requests EU to rewrite code of practice for AI models:
It is reported that the US administration has sent an official démarche document that formally requests the European Commission to address the flaws in the Code of Practice for general purpose AI models. The US critique highlights (1) the need for substantial amendments to enhance flexibility, reduce prescriptiveness, strengthen trade secret protections, better align with the AI Act itself, and clarify its relationship with EU copyright law; (2) several practical implementation challenges, particularly for open-weights models, including monitoring, incident reporting and staging requirements; (3) concerns about regulatory discrimination against predominantly US-based large AI developers through disproportionate regulatory burdens that could discourage growth; and (4) additional concerns on elements exceeding the AI Act's provisions, unclear application to downstream players who modify models, and terminology misaligned with international scientific consensus.

Antitrust & Competition
[11 April 2025] US Customs issues updated guidance on reciprocal tariff exclusion for specificed products, including semiconductors and ICs:
The US Customs and Border Protection has issued updated guidance which sets out a list of specified products which will be exempt from the reciprocal tariffs imposed by President Trump under Executive Order 14257. The exemptions broadly cover semiconductors, integrated circuits and smartphones - meaning that Chinese products in those categories will likely be spared from Trump's 125% tariffs.

National Strategy
[26 March 2025] BIS expands export controls to cover additional 80 entities, notably to further restrict China's AI and advanced computing capabilities:
The US Department of Commerce’s Bureau of Industry and Security (BIS) has amended the Export Administration Regulations (EAR), expanding 'Entity List' to cover 80 additional entities (notably from China, the United Arab Emirates (UAE), South Africa, Iran, Taiwan) so that they will be subject to export restrictions and additional licensing requirements on certain sensitive US-made technologies. The update, issued under the Export Control Reform Act, applies to entities involved in advanced computing, AI, quantum technologies, and military-related research across multiple target jurisdictions and who may engage in activities deemed contrary to US national security and foreign policy interests. The stated objectives of this update include: (1) "Restrict the Chinese Communist Party’s (CCP) ability to acquire and develop high-performance and exascale computing capabilities, as well as quantum technologies, for military applications"; (2) "Impede China’s development of its hypersonic weapons program"; (3) "Prevent entities associated with the Test Flying Academy of South Africa (TFASA) from using U.S. items to train Chinese military forces"; (4) "Disrupt Iran’s procurement of unmanned aerial vehicles (UAVs) and related defense items"; and (5) "Impair the development of unsafeguarded nuclear activities and ballistic missile program".

The deal follows a recent meeting between top UAE officials and US President Donald Trump. Under this deal, the UAE will substantially increase its existing investments in the US economy in AI infrastructure, semiconductors, energy, and manufacturing.
