[11 February 2025] US and UK abstain from signing the Statement on Inclusive and Sustainable Artificial Intelligence for People and the Planet:
The UK and UK have abstained from signing a joint statement on Inclusive and Sustainable Artificial Intelligence for People and the Planet at the AI Action Summit in Paris. The statement sets out priorities including "ensuring AI is open, inclusive, transparent, ethical, safe, secure and trustworthy, taking into account international frameworks for all" and "making AI sustainable for people and the planet". The statement has been signed by 60 countries, including India, China, Japan, Canada, Brazil, France and Australia.

[11 February 2025] JD Vance warns against "excessive regulation" of AI at AI Action Summit in Paris:
At the AI Action Summit in Paris, US Vice President JD Vance delivered a keynote address advocating for a pro-innovation, deregulatory approach to AI and rejecting European-style "excessive regulations". Key quotes include: (1) "excessive regulation of the AI sector could kill a transformative industry just as it's taking off, and we'll make every effort to encourage pro-growth AI policies, and I'd like to see that deregulatory flavour making its way into a lot of the conversations at this conference."; and (2) "we feel very strongly that AI must remain free from ideological bias, and that American AI will not be co-opted into a tool for authoritarian censorship."

[29 January 2025] Decoupling America’s Artificial Intelligence Capabilities from China Act introduced:
US Senator Hawley has introduced legislation titled "Decoupling America’s Artificial Intelligence Capabilities from China Act " which aims to (1) prohibit the import from or export to China of artificial intelligence technology; (2) prohibit US companies from conducting AI research in China or in cooperation with Chinese companies; and (3) prohibit US companies from investing money in Chinese AI development.

Defense & National Security
[28 January 2025] Trump to tariff chips made In Taiwan, targeting TSMC:
In his conference speech to the Republican Party in Florida, President Trump has stated, among other matters, that he is preparing to place tariffs beyond Chinese assembled electronics to computer chips made in Taiwan, warning the tariffs could reach as high as 100%. President Trump made specific reference to TSMC, expressing intentions to move TSMC's chip production back to the US (which used to be its base before it had moved to Taiwan). Chips & Data Centres
[13 January 2025] US White House issues Interim Final Rule on AI diffusion export including controls on sales of AI chips:
The White House issued an Interim Final Rule on Artificial Intelligence Diffusion Export, including controls on sales and export of AI chips. The rule (1) prohibits access to chip exports for stated adversaries, including China, Russia, Iran, and North Korea, and caps exports to approximately 120 countries; (2) exempts 18 allied nations from these restrictions, including Australia, Canada, the United Kingdom, France, South Korea, and Japan; (3) include streamlined licensing that exempts low-risk chip orders with up to 1’700 GPUs from requiring export licenses and expediting shipments for research and healthcare uses; (4) allows trusted entities to obtain "Universal Verified End User" status to be able to deploy up to 7% of their global AI capacity internationally, or "National Verified End User (VEU)" status to be able to purchase up to 320’000 GPUs over two years; (5) limits Non-VEU entities in non-allied nations to a cap of 50’000 GPUs per country, though government-to-government agreements with aligned nations can double their chip quotas; and (6) establishes stringent security measures to protect sensitive AI model weights from being diverted for adversarial use.

Defense & National Security
[2 December 2024] US announce sweeping set of export controls on China relating to chip-manufacturing equipment, memory, and software:
The US Department of Commerce’s Bureau of Industry and Security (BIS) has announced a package of rules designed to further restrict China's capability to produce advanced-node semiconductors that can be used in the next generation advanced weapon systems and in AI and advanced computing, which have significant military applications. The new regulations prevent China from accessing 24 types of chip-manufacturing equipment and three software programs, and place restrictions on the sale to China of high-bandwidth memory (HBM), an advanced class of 3D-stacked computer memory component that is often used in customized AI chips.

It was not clear whether the statement would lead to further talks or action on the issue.

Agentic AI
[10 November 2024] US ordered TSMC to halt shipments to China of chips used in AI applications:
It has been reported that the US Department of Commerce has sent a letter to Taiwan Semiconductor Manufacturing Co (TSMC) imposing export restrictions on certain sophisticated chips, of 7 nanometer or more advanced designs, destined for China that power AI accelerator and graphics processing units (GPU). Defense & National Security
[28 October 2024] US Treasury issues final rules restricting investments in key tech sectors (including semiconductor and AI) in "countries of concern" (e.g. China):
The US Department of the Treasury has issued final rules, implementing Executive Order 14105. From 2 January 2025, the final rules will prohibit anyone based from engaging in business dealings with persons of a "country of concern" (e.g. China) involving certain technologies that may contribute to the threat to US national security. Semiconductors and microelectronics, quantum information technologies, and AI systems of a certain threshold (e.g. computing power of greater than 10^24 computational operations) are covered under this rule. The final rules will also require US investors to notify the Treasury of investments in less advanced technologies that could still pose national security risks (e.g. AI systems under the prohibited threshold but trained with computing power greater than 10^23 computational operations).

It emphasizes collaboration on digital economy frameworks, inclusivity in AI development, and the importance of cybersecurity and human rights. The commitments also include efforts to close digital divides and empower vulnerable communities, ensuring that the benefits of AI are accessible to all.

Defense & National Security
[30 September 2024] US sets new rule that could spur AI chip shipments to the Middle East:
It has been reported that the US Commerce Department has unveiled a rule that could ease shipments of AI chips to data centers in the Middle East. For background, since October 2023, US exporters have been required to obtain licenses before shipping advanced chips to parts of the Middle East and Central Asia. Under the new rule, data centers will be able to apply for Validated End User status that will allow them to receive chips under a general authorization, rather than requiring their US suppliers to obtain individual licenses to ship to them.

Chips & Data Centres
[30 September 2024] US expands Validated End User program to cover data centres:
The US Bureau of Industry and Security (BIS) of the Department of Commerce has adopted a new order expanding the Validated End User (VEU) program to encompass data centers. Under this program, US exporters can now ship designated items to pre-approved entities under a general authorisation, streamlining the process and reducing the need for multiple individual export licenses. The program's vetting process ensures that only data centers committed to the highest security standards gain facilitated access to advanced US. technological innovation. According to the regulator, this action aims to bolster US national security and promote export control compliance within the realms of AI development, as well as the semiconductor industry.

The US and United Arab Emirates have released a statement reaffirming their shared intention to promote cooperation in AI and related technologies. The US and UAE intend to closely collaborate to: (1) advance safe, secure and trustworthy AI; (2) align regulatory frameworks to strengthen innovation ecosystems; (3) promote ethical AI research and development; (4) broaden and deepen cooperation in AI protection and cybersecurity; (5) facilitate opportunities for trusted trade and investment; (6) talent development and exchange; (7) promote clean energy for the AI future; and (8) support AI for sustainable development in developing countries. The US and UAE will develop a government-to-government memorandum of understanding to build upon the above goals.

Inaugural members will include Australia, Canada, the European Union, France, Japan, Kenya, the Republic of Korea, Singapore, the United Kingdom, and the United States. The meeting will include technical experts from each member’s AI safety institute, or equivalent government-backed scientific office, to discuss priority work areas, and advance global collaboration and knowledge sharing on AI safety.

Generative AI
Data Privacy & Protection
[1 August 2024] New US rule on foreign chip equipment exports to China to exempt some allies:
It has been reported that US President Joe Biden's administration plans to unveil a new rule that will expand US powers under the Foreign Direct Product Rule (FDPR) to stop exports of semiconductor manufacturing equipment from some foreign countries to Chinese chipmakers. For noting, under the FDPR, if a product was made using American technology, the US government has the power to stop it from being sold - including products made in a foreign country. Places whose exports would be affected by the proposed new rule would include Israel, Taiwan, Singapore and Malaysia. But shipments from allies that export key chipmaking equipment - including Japan, the Netherlands and South Korea - will be excluded.

Defense & National Security
[1 August 2024] US and Singapore deepen collaboration on critical technologies:
As part of the 2nd US-Singapore CET Dialogue, the US and Singapore have met again to deepen collaboration in various critical technology areas, including AI. Key points include (1) expanding National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) and Singapore Infocomm Media Development Authority (IMDA)'s governance and risk management frameworks to include generative AI; (2) collaborating on testing and evaluation, including aligning red-teaming guidelines and benchmarks; (3) supporting international standards, frameworks, and best practices for AI at bodies like ISO; (4) advancing AI safety through cooperation between US and Singapore AI Safety Institutes, with a meeting in September 2024; (5) exploring research collaboration between National Science Foundation (NSF) and AI Singapore (AISG) on responsible AI; (6) supporting inclusive AI development through a capacity-building program for Southeast Asian officials; (7) convening an NSF-funded workshop in Singapore to enhance collaboration in responsible AI research.

Cybersecurity
[16 July 2024] Singapore and US strengthen defence ties with new AI agreement:
Singapore and the US have signed the "Statement of Intent (SOI) on Data, Analytics, and Artificial Intelligence (AI) Cooperation" which focuses on collaboration in responsible AI use, quality data management and talent development in the context of military defence.

Defense & National Security
[22 June 2024] US closer to curbing investments in China's AI, tech sector:
It has been reported that the US Treasury Department has issued draft rules which aim to restrict and monitor US investments in China for AI, computer chips and quantum computing that could "threaten" US national security. The US previously proposed similar rules in August 2023 that put an onus on US individuals and companies to determine which transactions will be restricted or banned. Now the current draft rules would ban transactions in AI for certain end uses, and involving systems trained in using a specified quantity of computing power but would also require notification of transactions related to the development of AI systems or semiconductors not otherwise prohibited. Some exceptions would apply to publicly traded securities (e.g. index funds or mutual funds); certain limited partnership investments; buyouts of country-of-concern ownership; transactions between a US parent company and a majority-controlled subsidiary; binding commitments that pre-date the order; and certain syndicated debt financings. The US is on track to implement these rules by the end of 2024. Public comments on the proposed rules will be accepted until 4 August 2024.

Defense & National Security
[11 June 2024] US weights more limits on China's access to chips needed for AI:
It has been reported that the US government is considering additional restrictions on China's access to advanced chip technology used in AI. The potential measures aim to limit China’s ability to utilise a cutting-edge chip architecture known as gate all-around (GAA) which enhances chip performance and reduces power consumption. The specifics of the proposed rules are still under discussion, and it is unclear when a final decision will be made.

Defense & National Security
[5 June 2024] US and Singapore share principles and collaboration on AI:
US Secretary of Commerce Raimondo and Singapore Minister for Communications and Information Josephine Teo co-led a Roundtable on AI with US and Singapore companies and government officials. The Roundtable underscored the importance of the close and long-standing relationship between the US and Singapore, which has grown to include close economic cooperation on digital issues. Key points include: (1) NIST and IMBA to continue to co-operate through the exchange of best practices and other information concerning AI governance frameworks, including NIST AI Risk Management Framework and IMDA's AI Verify; (2) the US AI Safety Institute and Singapore Digital Trust Center to plan important collaborations on advancing the science of AI safety; (3) Commerce and MCI to collaborate the support the responsible design, development, deployment, and evaluation of AI technologies; and (4) Commerce and IMDA to launch a new AI talent bridge program.

Generative AI
Cybersecurity
[23 May 2024] United States-Kenya Joint Leaders’ Statement:
The White House has issued the US-Kenya Joint Leader's Statement, which includes commitments on cooperation in digital technology. Under this statement, both nations commit to strengthening cooperation on technology policy to support Kenya's digital economy, including establishing a strategic dialogue on AI to deepen collaboration in developing safe and secure AI systems. The statement also states that the US recognises Kenya as a crucial partner in strengthening semiconductor supply chains.

Generative AI
Cybersecurity
[21 May 2024] World leaders sign up to Seoul Declaration and Statement of Intent toward International Cooperation on AI Safety Science:
Australia, Canada, the European Union, France, Germany, Italy, Japan, the Republic of Korea, the Republic of Singapore, the United States of America and the United Kingdom signed the (1) Seoul Declaration for safe, innovative and inclusive AI; and (2) Seoul Statement of Intent toward International Cooperation on AI Safety Science. Together, these documents build upon the Bletchley Declaration, and aim to (a) promote safe, secure, and trustworthy AI development, (b) address global challenges and the protection of human rights, and (c) commit nations to create AI safety institutes and work together on AI safety science, sharing information about AI models, risks, and safety incidents.

Cybersecurity
Defense & National Security
[16 May 2024] Top US and Chinese officials begin talks on AI in Geneva:
Top envoys from the US and China met in Geneva, Switzerland to initiate talks surrounding the regulation of AI. This meeting is the first under an intergovernmental dialogue on AI agreed upon during a meeting between President Xi and President Biden in San Francisco in November 2023. Outcomes of the meeting have yet to be revealed.

Generative AI
Data Privacy & Protection
Defense & National Security
[9 May 2024] ENFORCE Act introduced:
The "Enhancing National Frameworks for Overseas Restriction of Critical Exports Act" (ENFORCE Act/HR 8315) was introduced in the US House of Representatives. The ENFORCE Act amends the Export Control Reform Act of 2018 to prevent foreign adversaries from exploiting US artificial intelligence (AI) and other enabling technologies. In particular, it would establish a licensing requirement for US persons to export, re-export, or in-country transfer of certain items. Other activities that may support these items regarding the design, development, production, use, and operation are subject to the licensing requirement as well.

Defense & National Security
[5 April 2024] US-EU Trade and Technology Council joint statement including commitment to a risk-based approach to AI:
The US and the EU, following the sixth ministerial meeting of the TTC (Transatlantic Technology and Trade Council), issued a joint statement including a commitment to a risk-based approach to AI to ensure its safe, secure, and trustworthy development. Key points include (1) continued bilateral and joint participation in international organisations such as G7, OECD, and UN processes; (2) endorsed the Hiroshima Process International Code of Conduct for AI developers; (3) the EU AI Office and US AI Safety Institute to exchange information on their regulatory approaches and agree to establish a dialogue to expand their collaboration further; (4) implementing the Joint Roadmap on Evaluation and Measurement Tools for Trustworthy AI and Risk Management, aiming to establish interoperable international standards.

Generative AI
Cybersecurity
Data Privacy & Protection
[1 April 2024] US and UK announce partnership on science of AI safety:
The US and UK AI Safety Institutes have signed a Memorandum of Understanding to collaborate on research, safety evaluations, and guidance for AI safety. They aim to develop shared capabilities through information-sharing, close cooperation, and expert personnel exchanges. The partnership will focus on developing tests for advanced AI models and building a common approach to AI safety testing.

Sandbox
Generative AI
[13 March 2024] US introduces draft UN resolution on AI:
The US has introduced a draft resolution at the United Nations promoting "safe, secure and trustworthy" AI systems. It calls for "effective safeguards for the use of AI, including physical and security systems and risk management. The draft also "encourages the private sector to adhere to applicable international and domestic laws". The resolution, which is co-sponsored by more than 50 nations, would be nonbinding.

[25 February 2024] US and China agree to map out framework for developing AI responsibly:
US and China have finally agreed to meet in the next few months to work on a framework for the responsible development of AI.

[31 May 2023] Fourth Ministerial meeting of the Trade and Technology Council (TTC):
Among other matters, the EU and US at the TTC have reaffirmed their committment to strengthening their transatlantic co-operation on emerging technologies, including AI. On AI, the EU and US are aligned on a risk-based approach to AI to advance trustworthy and responsible AI technologies.

Workforce Transparency Act:
A bill to provide for voluntary disclosure by developers and users of AI regarding workforce data and for reporting by the Secretary of Labor regarding the workforce data, and for other purposes.

Public Sector & Governance
Children's Health, Advancement, Trust, Boundaries, and Oversight in Technology Act (CHATBOT Act):
A bill to require the creation of family accounts for children to be able to use AI chatbots, to require verifiable parental consent for teens using AI chatbots, and for other purposes.

Youth AI Privacy Act:
A bill to require entities that make artificial intelligence chatbots available to minors to implement certain safe design features, and for other purposes.

AI Data Center Moratorium Act:
A bill to impose a moratorium on the construction of new data centers until legislation is enacted that safeguards the public from the dangers of AI.

Chips & Data Centres
Guaranteeing and Upholding Americans’ Right to Decide Responsible AI Laws and Standards (GUARDRAILS) Act:
A bill to repeal the Executive Order entitled "Ensuring a National Policy Framework for Artificial Intelligence" that was issued on 11 December 2025.

Federal v State
Artificial Intelligence Ready Data Act:
A bill to establish standards and guidelines to make open Government data assets AI-ready, and for other purposes.

Public Sector & Governance
Growing University AI Research for Defense Act (GUARD) Act:
A bill to authorize the Secretary of Defense to establish a National Security and Defense Artificial Intelligence Institute. The proposed institute would facilitate collaboration between academia, government, and industry, focusing on defense-related AI data management and operational readiness to maintain the US' strategic advantage over foreign adversaries.

Defense & National Security
States' Right to Regulate Artificial Intelligence (AI) Act:
This Act aims to prohibit the use of federal funds to implement, administer, or enforce the Executive Order Ensuring a National Policy Framework for AI, issued on 11 December 2025. That order seeks to establish a unified national AI policy framework designed to minimise regulatory burdens, preempt conflicting State laws, and balance innovation with protections for children, copyrights, free expression, and public safety. It directs federal agencies to challenge restrictive State AI laws, condition certain federal funding on State compliance, and implement federal standards for AI disclosure, reporting, and preemption.

Online Safety & Child Protection
Data Privacy & Protection
Copyright & IP
The Republic Unifying Meritocratic Performance Advancing Machine intelligence by Eliminating Regulatory Interstate Chaos Across American Industry (TRUMP AMERICA AI Act):
This legislative framework would codify President Trump’s executive order to create one rulebook for AI that protects children, creators, conservatives, and communities from potential harms associated with AI, while promoting innovation to ensure the nation's leadership in the global AI race. Key provisions include imposing a duty of care on AI developers to prevent foreseeable harm, reforming Section 230 to enhance parental control over children's online access, safeguarding minors on online platforms, and protecting creators' rights by requiring explicit consent for the use of their data in AI training. Additionally, the act addresses concerns about bias against conservative viewpoints in AI systems and mandates transparency regarding AI's impact on employment.

Online Safety & Child Protection
Data Privacy & Protection
Copyright & IP
Restoring Export and Security Trade Restrictions for Integrated Circuit Technologies (RESTRICT) Act:
This bill would prohibit the sale of the most advanced US AI chips to China and other countries of concern, while strengthening US competitiveness by creating a secure, license-free export pathway for trusted American companies operating data centres abroad. In particular, the bill would: (1) prohibit the sale of H200 and other advanced AI chips to China by directing the Under Secretary of Commerce to deny export licenses for advanced integrated circuits to countries of concern; (2) codify existing restrictions on exports of US advanced integrated circuits and related products to China without imposing new controls; (3) apply these prohibitions to all nations under a US arms embargo as of 1 January 2025; (4) safeguard national security while allowing export controls to adapt by permitting the Under Secretary of Commerce to revise the definition of “advanced integrated circuit or product” after two years with congressional certification; and (5) facilitate secure global operations for US firms by requiring regulations on physical, cybersecurity, and remote access security for license-free transfers to US-owned facilities outside countries of concern.

Defense & National Security
Cybersecurity
Digital Trade Promotion Act:
A bill to empower the president to negotiate and conclude digital trade agreements with other countries to regulate electronic commerce and cross-border data flows (broadly including AI). Key provisions include authorising the US Trade Representative to enter into comprehensive digital trade agreements, ensuring nondiscrimination for digital goods and services, prohibiting discriminatory digital taxes and data localization, and promoting cooperation in areas like AI and cybersecurity.

Data Privacy & Protection
Cybersecurity
Generative AI
AI Talent Act:
A bill to enhance federal agencies' ability to recruit and retain top AI and technical talent. The proposed legislation aims to modernize federal hiring practices by establishing specialized talent teams, enabling skills-based hiring, and providing shared tools to expedite the identification and onboarding of qualified candidates. Key provisions include: (1) to establish Agency Tech & AI Talent Teams to improve recruiting, assessments, job announcements, and candidate evaluation; (2) to authorize OPM to create a central AI and tech talent team to lead pooled hiring, provide training and support to agency hiring teams, and develop shared resources; (3) to allow subject-matter experts to develop and administer skills-based assessments to ensure candidates demonstrate real technical proficiency; (4) to enable agencies to share qualified candidate pools (“shared certificates”), reducing duplicate hiring cycles and speeding placement; (5) to create a shared online platform to reuse and customize validated technical assessments across government; (6) to phase out automated self-assessments over five years, with limited, publicly posted waivers; (7) to allow agencies to stand up additional talent teams in other high-need areas (e.g., cybersecurity, data science, health care, IT); and (8) to authorize OPM to establish additional government-wide talent teams for high-need hiring priorities beyond AI and tech.

Cybersecurity
Secure and Feasible Exports (SAFE) Chips Act:
A bill to codify existing restrictions on the sale of advanced AI chips to countries like China, North Korea, Russia, and Iran. The bipartisan legislation seeks to maintain the United States' leadership in AI by preventing adversaries from accessing critical technologies, thereby safeguarding national security and economic interests. The bill would (1) direct the Secretary of Commerce to deny export license applications for advanced chips to foreign adversary countries for a period not less than 30 months; (2) after 30 months, the Executive Branch has discretion to update technical parameters as it sees fit; (3) define Democratic People’s Republic of Korea, Russia, Iran, and the People’s Republic of China, including Hong Kong and Macau, as Foreign Adversary Countries; (4) define advanced integrated circuits as any chips more powerful than those currently licensed for export to foreign adversary countries; and (5) direct the Department of Commerce to publish any proposed updates in the Federal Register that have been approved by a majority vote of the End-User Review Committee and to brief Congress 30 days before any proposed changes.

Defense & National Security
AI Civil Rights Act (2025):
US Senator Edward J. Markey (D-Mass.) and Representative Yvette Clarke (NY-09) have reintroduced the AI Civil Rights Act, aiming to prevent the use of biased and discriminatory AI algorithms in critical decision-making processes affecting American individuals. It has three key provisions: (1) to prohibit companies from offering, licensing, or using algorithms that discriminate on the basis of protected characteristics, like race or sex; (2) to require AI companies to conduct independent audits to identify and mitigate algorithmic discrimination; and (3) to give individuals the right to appeal an AI-based decision to a human, and empower the Federal Trade Commission, state attorneys general, and private individuals to enforce this part of the law. The bill was previously introduced in the US Senate in September 2024 but stalled in the 118th Congress session and expired thereafter.

Generative AI
Data Privacy & Protection
Advanced Artificial Intelligence (AI) Security Readiness Act:
A bill to direct the NSA’s AI Security Center to develop and disseminate security guidance that identifies potential vulnerabilities and threats and establishes security strategies and contingency plans for America’s advanced AI systems.

Cybersecurity
Defense & National Security
AI-Related Job Impacts Clarity Act:
A bill aimed at increasing transparency regarding the impact of AI on employment. The proposed legislation would require major companies and federal agencies to submit quarterly reports to the Department of Labor detailing AI-related job effects, including layoffs and job displacement. The Department of Labor would then compile this data into a publicly available report for Congress and the public.

National Strategy
Guaranteeing Access and Innovation for National Artificial Intelligence (GAIN AI) Act:
A bill to require entities seeking a license to export advanced AI chips to countries of concern to certify that US persons have priority in acquiring those chips. For background, the GAIN AI Act was previously introduced as part of the National Defense Authorization Act, as a more direct successor to the recently rescinded Biden-era AI Diffusion Rule to address ongoing national security and supply chain concerns regarding advanced AI chips. The GAIN AI Act is now being introduced as standalone legislation rather than as an amendment to the National Defense Authorization Act.

Defense & National Security
Learning Innovation and Family Empowerment (LIFE) with AI Act:
This bill aims to create a parent-centered framework that safeguards student data privacy, enhances transparency, and promotes the responsible and optional use of AI in K-12 personalized learning. The bill seeks to empower parents to protect their children from potential harm as AI becomes increasingly integrated into education. The bill has received support from organizations like Parents Defending Education Action, which emphasizes the importance of protecting students' privacy and reinforcing parental rights under existing laws.

Data Privacy & Protection
Online Safety & Child Protection
Guidelines for User Age-verification and Responsible Dialogue (GUARD) Act:
A bill aimed at protecting minors from the potential dangers of AI chatbots. The legislation seeks to ban AI companions for minors, require AI chatbots to disclose their non-human status, and establish new criminal offenses for companies that develop AI targeting minors with solicitations or production of sexual content.

Online Safety & Child Protection
Generative AI
AI for Main Street Act:
A bill to amend the Small Business Act to require small business development centers to assist small business concerns with the use of artificial intelligence, and for other purposes.

Generative AI
Aligning Incentives for Leadership, Excellence, and Advancement in Development (AI LEAD) Act:
A bill which proposes to: (1) classify AI systems as products, allowing for product liability claims to be brought against companies if their AI system causes harm; (2) incentivize AI companies to design their systems safely rather than rushing AI systems to market; and (3) hold AI companies accountable without stifling innovation by allowing for the continued development of beneficial AI systems.

Children Harmed by AI Technology Act (CHAT Act):
A bill to require artificial intelligence chatbots to implement age verification measures and establish certain protections for minor users, and for other purposes.

Strengthening Artificial intelligence Normalization and Diffusion By Oversight and EXperimentation Act (SANDBOX Act):
A bill to require the Director of the Office of Science and Technology Policy to establish a Federal regulatory sandbox program for artificial intelligence, and for other purposes.

Sandbox
The No Advanced Chips for the Chinese Communist Party (CCP) Act:
This bill prohibits exports of advanced AI semiconductors to China unless both the US Department of Commerce and the United States Congress approve. It also provides that semiconductors are covered if they exceed thresholds for processing power, dynamic random-access memory (DRAM) bandwidth, or interconnect capacity. The bill requires the Secretary of Commerce to conduct an interagency review with the Secretary of Defence, the Secretary of Energy, the Secretary of State, and the Director of National Intelligence. The bill requires assessment of risks to US national security, technological leadership, military applications, human rights, and economic impacts following the enactment of a joint resolution by Congress approving each export. The bill provides exemptions for humanitarian purposes, US diplomatic operations, and chip repairs.

Defense & National Security
Validation and Evaluation for Trustworthy Artificial Intelligence (VET AI) Act:
This bill is reintroduced since its passage out of the Senate Commerce, Science, and Transportation Committee in 2024 before the end of the 118th Congress. The bill would require National Institute of Standards and Technology to lead the development of “detailed specifications, guidelines, and recommendations for third-party evaluators to work with AI companies to provide robust independent external assurance and verification” of AI systems. The bill also includes provisions to develop voluntary, consensus-based guidelines for internal and external assurance of AI systems. The bill applies to developers, deployers, and independent evaluators of AI, aiming to enhance trust, accountability, and risk management without mandating specific technologies. It establishes an advisory committee to recommend qualifications for AI assurance professionals and requires the Secretary of Commerce to study the sector’s capabilities and report to Congress.

Cybersecurity
Data Privacy & Protection
H.R.4873 (bill to codify Executive Order 14319 relating to preventing woke AI in the Federal Government):
A bill to give Executive Order 14319 the effect of the law. The order requires the Director of the Office of Management and Budget (OMB), in conjunction with the Administrator for Federal Procurement Policy, the Administrator of General Services, and the Director of the Office of Science and Technology Policy, to issue guidance ensuring that agency heads procure only those large language models (LLMs) developed in accordance with the principles of truth-seeking and ideological neutrality. It also requires each agency head to include section terms in government contracts with LLMs requiring that the procured LLM comply with the principles of truth-seeking and ideological neutrality. This must be done for each contract entered into following the date of publication of the OMB guidance. It must also be done for existing contracts to the greatest extent possible. Additionally, within 90 days of the issuance of OMB guidance, agency heads must adopt procedures to ensure that procured LLMs comply with the principles. Executive Order 14319 includes a standard disclaimer stating that it does not create any legally enforceable rights or benefits against the US government, its agencies, employees, or other individuals. The bill would make Executive Order 14319 legally enforceable if adopted.

Generative AI
Data Privacy & Protection
Transparency and Responsibility for Artificial Intelligence Networks (TRAIN) Act:
The bill establishes a subpoena mechanism allowing copyright holders to determine whether their works were used to train generative AI models. The bill applies to developers, including entities and government agencies who design, substantially modify, or train such models, excluding non-commercial end users. It permits copyright owners to request subpoenas from district courts to compel developers to disclose records or copies of training material, provided there is a good faith belief that their copyrighted content was used. Developers must comply promptly and maintain confidentiality, while noncompliance creates a rebuttable presumption of infringement.

Copyright & IP
Generative AI
Unleashing AI Innovation in Financial Services Act:
This bill would promote AI in financial services through regulatory sandboxes for AI test projects at federal financial regulatory agencies.

Sandbox
Artificial Intelligence Accountability and Personal Data Protection Act:
This bill (Bill No. S.2367) seeks to establish a federal tort against the appropriation, collection, processing, sale, or other exploitation of individuals’ data without express, prior consent. The bill applies to entities, including those deploying generative AI systems, that misuse personal or inferred data, and provides individuals with a private right of action to claim damages, injunctive relief, and attorney’s fees. It bans predispute arbitration agreements and class action waivers, mandates explicit consent with clear third-party disclosure, and sets a federal minimum standard without pre-empting stronger state protections.

Data Privacy & Protection
Generative AI
No Adversarial AI Act:
The bill would (1) create a permanent framework for barring the use of all Chinese AI models from U.S. executive agencies, as well as those from Russia, Iran and North Korea; (2) require the Federal Acquisition Security Council to create a list of AI models developed in those countries and regularly update it; (3) restrict US federal agencies from buying or using those AI technologies without an exemption, such as for carrying out research, from the US Congress or the Office of Management and Budget; and (4) contain a provision that can be used to get technologies off the list with proof that they are not controlled or influenced by a foreign adversary of the US.

H. R. 3961:
A bill to prohibit the Secretary of Defense from entering into software source code contracts with entities with certain relationships with China, and for other purposes.

Defense & National Security
Cybersecurity
Preventing Deep Fake Scams Act:
This bill would establish a task force to assess how financial institutions can use AI to protect against fraud and identify potential risks associated with abusing AI technology, particularly deepfakes. It would also establish best practices to safeguard consumers from these types of financial crimes. The task force would produce a detailed report of its findings to Congress within one year of the bill’s enactment.

Cybersecurity
Deepfakes
Responsible Innovation and Safe Expertise (RISE) Act:
A bill to establish immunity from civil liability for certain AI developers. It clarifies that when professionals—such as physicians, attorneys, engineers, and financial advisors—use AI systems in their practice, they retain the legal duty to exercise due diligence, verify the system’s outputs, and stand behind the advice they deliver. This is the first targeted liability reform legislation for professional-grade AI. Developers may claim safe-harbor immunity only if they publicly release a model card and key design specifications so that physicians, attorneys, engineers, and other professionals can understand what the AI can and cannot do before relying on it for decisions that affect end users.

Generative AI
Testing and Evaluation Systems for Trusted Artificial Intelligence Act (TEST AI Act):
A bill to enhance national capacity for the testing and evaluation of AI systems. It outlines a collaborative initiative between the National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) and the Department of Energy (DOE) to establish a pilot programme for AI testbeds. These testbeds are intended to develop and refine evaluation standards addressing aspects such as performance, security, privacy, and bias, contributing to the foundation of broader AI measurement standards.

Cybersecurity
Data Privacy & Protection
Chip Security Act:
A bill to require the Secretary of Commerce to issue standards with respect to chip security mechanisms for integrated circuit products, and for other purposes. The legislation seeks to enhance oversight of advanced chips and directs the Commerce Department and Department of Defense to explore chip security mechanisms.

Cybersecurity
Defense & National Security
Clean Cloud Act:
A bill to amend the Clean Air Act to establish requirements on the collection of electricity consumption data and emissions standards for servers and other computing equipment used for cryptocurrency mining, and for other purposes.

Energy & Environment
Health Tech Investment Act:
A bill aimed at improving health outcomes for Medicare patients by encouraging the use of cutting-edge, AI-enabled medical devices. The bill will assign all US Food and Drug Administration (FDA) approved AI-enabled medical devices to a New Technology Ambulatory Payment Classification (APC) in the Hospital Outpatient Prospective Payment System (OPPS) a minimum of 5 years so that adequate data regarding delivery and service costs is acquired before assignment of a permanent payment code. Specifically, the bill would: (1) develop a formalized payment pathway for ABHS FDA-cleared medical devices; (2) provide patients with access to innovative, AI-enabled clinical technology; (3) provide manufacturers and providers with the certainty they need to invest in developing next-generation healthcare technologies and bringing them to market, and (4) improve patient outcomes, providing resources for providers to meet ABHS standards of care.

Health & Life Sciences
TAME Extreme Weather and Wildfires Act:
A bill to enhance the use by the National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration of artificial intelligence for weather forecasting, and for other purposes.

Generative AI
Leveraging Artificial Intelligence to Streamline the Code of Federal Regulations Act of 2025:
A bill to require the use of artificial intelligence to review agency regulations, and for other purposes.

National Strategy
Decoupling America’s Artificial Intelligence Capabilities from China Act:
This bill aims to (1) prohibit the import from or export to China of artificial intelligence technology; (2) prohibit US companies from conducting AI research in China or in cooperation with Chinese companies; and (3) prohibit US companies from investing money in Chinese AI development.

Defense & National Security
Responsible AI Disclosure Act of 2024:
This bill would require the heads of financial agencies to carry out a study that would help establish recommended definitions and standards for categorizing AI data and methodologies used to train AI models. These heads, among other responsibilities delineated in the bill, would assess current and recommended standards for the delineation and ratios of synthetic versus genuine data in the training of AI models (and the sources for that data). They would issue a report to specific House committees detailing their findings and recommendations.

Data Privacy & Protection
Generative AI
AI Leadership Training Act:
The bill requires the director of the Office of Personnel Management (OPM) to establish or otherwise ensure the existence of a training program on artificial intelligence (AI) for federal management officials and supervisors. The training should enable federal employees to understand the trade-offs associated with AI and its use by the federal government.

Training & Workforce
Artificial Intelligence Literacy Act of 2023:
The bill amends the Digital Equity Act of 2021 to promote artificial intelligence (AI) literacy within schools as part of the Digital Equity Competitive Grant Program.

Education
Workforce of the Future Act of 2024:
The bill would attempt to promote 21st century artificial intelligence (AI) workforce development by authorizing the secretary of Education to carry out K–12 education programs.

Education
Next Generation Military Education Act:
The bill would provide personnel of the Department of Defense (DOD) with increased access to training and education in artificial intelligence (AI) and machine learning.

Technology Workforce Framework Act of 2024:
he bill would expand the functions of the National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) to include workforce frameworks for critical and emerging technologies, including artificial intelligence (AI).

Mathematical and Statistical Modeling Education Act:
This bill requires the National Science Foundation (NSF) to take certain actions to increase mathematical and statistical modeling education in elementary and secondary schools.

Education
AI Training Expansion Act of 2023:
The bill attempts to expand artificial intelligence (AI) training within the executive branch by amending the Artificial Intelligence Training for the Acquisition Workforce Act.

Training & Workforce
Managing Active and Reserve Tech Talent Effectively (MARTTE) Act of 2023:
The bill seeks to ensure the hiring and presence of individuals with programming, coding, and artificial intelligence (AI) capabilities within the armed forces.

Defense & National Security
Workforce for AI Trust Act:
The bill would direct the National Science Foundation (NSF) and the National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) to direct more research and education to the development and training of safe and trustworthy artificial intelligence (AI) systems.

Training & Workforce
Jobs of the Future Act of 2023:
The bill seeks to study the impact of artificial intelligence (AI) on workforce opportunities in the United States and how to best prepare workers for future opportunities and avoid sustained job displacement.

National Strategy
NSF AI Education Act of 2024:
The bill would create scholarships to enable the study of artificial intelligence (AI) development and quantum computing, create professional development fellowships at the National Science Foundation (NSF), and create an award program for research on AI development.

Training & Workforce
AI LEAD Act:
The bill establishes a chief artificial intelligence officer in each federal agency and creates a council for officers to collaborate on issues related to artificial intelligence (AI) within the federal government.

National Strategy
PREVAIL Act:
By amending title 35, the bill attempts to strengthen patent rights, particularly for small businesses, limit repetitive challenges within the Patent Trial and Appeal Board, and reform Inter Partes review with the goal of assisting small business patent holders.

Copyright & IP
Next Generation Pipelines Research and Development Act:
The bill establishes programs to encourage research and development (R&D) and commercialization of technologies related to pipelines and power generation. The bill amends portions of the Infrastructure Investment and Jobs Act, as well as creates and funds new initiatives.

Logistics & Infrastructure
DOE and USDA Interagency Research Act:
The bill directs the secretary of the Department of Energy (DOE) and the secretary of the Department of Agriculture (DOA) to collaborate on research and development (R&D) activities focused on advancing the missions of DOE and DOA.

National Strategy
Ensuring Safe and Ethical AI Development Through SAFE AI Research Grants:
The bill would require the National Academy of Sciences (NAS) to establish a grant program to develop safe artificial intelligence (AI) models and safe AI research.

Generative AI
United States-Israel Future of Warfare Act of 2023:
This bill requires the Department of Defense (DOD) to establish the United States-Israel Future of Warfare Research and Development Fund to conduct collaborative defense projects between the United States and Israel in areas of emerging technologies (e.g., artificial intelligence (AI)).

The bill would establish internation artificial intelligence (AI) research partnerships.

Global Investment in American Jobs Act of 2023:
The bill directs the secretary of the Department of Commerce and other agency heads to review the global competitiveness of the United States in attracting foreign direct investment (FDI) and ways to address foreign trade barriers for firms working on advanced technology.

National Strategy
FAA Research and Development Act of 2023:
The legislation directs the Federal Aviation Administration (FAA) to conduct research and development (R&D) on a variety of topics, including artificial intelligence (AI) and machine learning (ML). The section focused on AI calls for examination of various applications of AI that can improve airport efficiency and safety.

National Strategy
AI Advancement and Reliability Act of 2024:
The bill would create a center on artificial intelligence (AI) in the Department of Commerce that would advance measurement science for AI reliability, robustness, resilience, security, and safety. The center would also support ongoing research and collaborate with the private sector.

Cybersecurity
AI Grand Challenges Act of 2024:
The bill would authorize the director of the National Science Foundation to identify grand challenges and award competitive prizes for artificial intelligence research and development.

National Strategy
Land Grant Research Prioritization Act of 2023:
The bill would amend the Food, Agriculture, Conservation, and Trade Act of 1990 by making research grants available to projects evaluating using artificial intelligence in an agricultural context, with specific interest in improving specialty crop production.

National Strategy
Water Quality and Environmental Innovation Act:
This bill establishes and funds the Water Quality and Environmental Innovation Fund to fund research and projects using artificial intelligence (AI) and other emerging technologies to address threats to water quality.

Generative AI
DOE and NASA Interagency Research Coordination Act:
This bill provides statutory authority for a research and development partnership between the Department of Energy (DOE) and the National Aeronautics and Space Administration (NASA). Specifically, the bill authorizes DOE and NASA to enter into a memorandum of understanding to support cross-cutting and collaborative research and development that furthers the missions of both agencies. Through the partnership, DOE and NASA may conduct research in a variety of focus areas (e.g., dark matter), develop ways to support large voluntary data sets on space and aeronautical information, promote multi-agency data sharing, and support NASA's access to DOE research infrastructure.

Energy
Expanding AI Voices through Capacity Building Act:
The bill would support a broad and diverse interdisciplinary research community for the advancement of artificial intelligence (AI) and AI-powered innovation through partnerships and capacity building at institutions of higher education to expand AI capacity in populations historically underrepresented in STEM.

Training & Workforce
NSF AI Education Act of 2024:
The bill would support the National Science Foundation in education and professional development relating to artificial intelligence (AI).

Education
DOE and NSF Interagency Research Act:
The bill provides statutory authority for a research and development (R&D) partnership between the Department of Energy (DOE) and the National Science Foundation (NSF). Specifically, the bill requires DOE and NSF to enter into a memorandum of understanding to support cross-cutting and collaborative research and development that furthers the missions of both agencies in areas such as artificial intelligence (AI), promotes multi-agency and cross-sector data sharing, supports research infrastructure, and organizes education and training initiatives.

Preventing Algorithmic Collusion Act of 2024:
The bill restricts the use of algorithmic pricing to prevent collusion by firms that utilize artificial intelligence (AI) / machine learning (ML) models to predict and set prices. It also would create a task force to advance efforts by the U.S. government to combat national security threats posed by the technology.

Generative AI
Executive Orders

Filter Categories...
Ensuring a National Policy Framework for Artificial Intelligence (Executive Order 14365, 2025):
The Order establishes a unified national policy framework for AI, aiming to eliminate state-level regulations that hinder innovation and create compliance challenges for AI companies. The order directs the creation of an AI Litigation Task Force to challenge state laws deemed unconstitutional or obstructive, and requires the Commerce Department to evaluate state AI laws, identifying those that compel false outputs or violate constitutional rights. States with onerous AI laws risk losing federal funding under programs like BEAD, while agencies may condition grants on states refraining from enforcing such laws. The FCC is tasked with considering a federal reporting and disclosure standard, and the FTC must issue guidance clarifying that state laws mandating deceptive AI outputs are preempted. Finally, the order calls for legislative recommendations to establish a uniform federal AI framework, while preserving state authority in areas such as child safety, infrastructure, and procurement.

Data Privacy & Protection
Online Safety & Child Protection
Preventing Woke AI in the Federal Government (Executive Order 14319, 2025):
The Order (1) directs agency heads to procure only large language models (LLMs) that adhere to “Unbiased AI Principles” defined in the Order: truth-seeking and ideological neutrality; (2) instructs the Director of the Office of Management and Budget, in consultation with other Federal leaders, to issue guidance for agencies to implement these principles in AI procurement; and (3) mandates that Federal contracts for LLMs include terms ensuring compliance with the Unbiased AI Principles, including terms holding vendors accountable for certain costs if contracts are terminated due to noncompliance.

Generative AI
Promoting the Export of the American AI Technology Stack (Executive Order 14320, 2025):
The Order (1) directs the Secretary of Commerce to establish and implement the American AI Exports Program to support the development and deployment of U.S. full-stack AI export packages. These full-stack, end-to-end packages include hardware, data systems, AI models, cybersecurity measures, applications for sectors like healthcare, education, agriculture, and transportation, and more. The packages must comply with export controls and other relevant requirements; and (2) directs the Secretary of Commerce to review and select proposals that will receive export support from the Economic Diplomacy Action Group, such as loans, guarantees, and technical assistance.

Cybersecurity
Accelerating Federal Permitting of Data Centre Infrastructure (Executive Order 14318, 2025):
The Order (1) directs the Secretary of Commerce to launch an initiative to provide financial support, such as loans, grants, and tax incentives, for Qualifying Projects (i.e. including data centers that require greater than 100 megawatts of new load, infrastructure projects related to data center energy needs, semiconductor facilities, networking equipment, or other data center or related infrastructure projects selected by the Secretary of Defense, Secretary of the Interior, Secretary of Commerce, or Secretary of Energy); (2) revokes a Biden-era Executive Order that would have saddled AI data center development on Federal lands with pages of DEI and climate requirements; (3) instructs agencies to streamline environmental reviews and permitting for data centers and related infrastructure by leveraging existing exemptions and creating new ones to expedite the construction of Qualifying Projects; (4) enhances transparency and efficiency by designating Qualified Projects for expedited permitting under the FAST-41 framework; (5) promotes the use of Brownfield and Superfund sites for data center development, repurposing these lands for productive use; and (6) directs the Department of the Interior, the Department of Energy and the Department of Defense to authorize data center construction on appropriate Federal lands.

Logistics & Infrastructure
Removing Barriers to American Leadership in Artificial Intelligence (Executive Order 14179, 2025):
This order calls for "removing barriers to American leadership in Artificial Intelligence". In particular, the order (1) sets out the new national policy "to sustain and enhance America’s global AI dominance in order to promote human flourishing, economic competitiveness, and national security"; (2) requires the Director of the Office of Management and Budget (OMB) along with other executives to develop and submit an action plan to achieve the above policy within 180 days; (3) requires all agencies to review, revise, suspend or rescind any existing policies, directives, regulations, orders and other actions that were taken under the now-revoked Executive Order 14110 that are now inconsistent with the above policy; and (4) requires the OMB to revise its OMB Memoranda M-24-10 and M-24-18 as necessary to make them consistent with the above policy.

Defense & National Security
Generative AI
Advancing U.S. Leadership in Artificial Intelligence Infrastructure (Executive Order 14141, 2025):
This order directs the US Department of Defense (DOD) and US Department of Energy (DOE) to lease federal sites to the private sector (via a competitive bid process) for building, owning and operating gigawatt-scale AI data centres and power generation facilities, and "to facilitate this infrastructure’s interconnection to the electric grid, fulfill permitting obligations expeditiously, and advance transmission development around federal sites."

Defense & National Security
[REPEALED] Safe, Secure, and Trustworthy Artificial Intelligence (Executive Order 14110, 2023):
This Order establish various regulatory, economic and strategic initiatives that are aimed at driving safe, secure and trustworthy AI. For example, on the regulatory front, the Order: (1) requires developers of foundation models that pose serious risk to national/economic security, public health/safety, etc to notify the federal government; (2) calls for AI safety guidance/standards to be established by the NIST (on red-team testing), Dept of Energy & Dept of Homeland Security (on critical infrastructure sectors), and Dept of Commerce (on AI-generated content and content authentication); (3) calls for data privacy legislation to regulate federal government use of AI; and (4) reaffirms the AI ethic principles in the Blueprint for AI Bill of Rights + additional guidelines on algorithmic discrimination. On the economic/strategic piece, the Order proposes a new cybersecurity program, labour market study, continued R&D support, training programs, and international cooperation plans.

Cybersecurity
Data Privacy & Protection
Generative AI
Promoting the Use of Trustworthy Artificial Intelligence in the Federal Government (Executive Order 13960, 2020):
This Order requires agencies to prepare an inventory of non-classified and non-sensitive current and planned AI use cases. Agencies must share their inventories with the public and other agencies, to the extent practicable.

Data Privacy & Protection
Maintaining American Leadership in Artificial Intelligence (Executive Order 13859, 2019):
This Order establishes federal principles and strategies to strengthen the nation's capabilities in AI to promote scientific discovery, economic competitiveness, and national security.

Defense & National Security
Guidelines, Frameworks & Standards

Filter Categories...
A National Policy Framework for Artificial Intelligence (2026):
The Trump Administration has issued a comprehensive national legislative framework aimed at winning the AI race to enhance human flourishing, economic competitiveness, and national security for Americans, while addressing public concerns about the technology's impact on issues such as children's wellbeing and energy costs, outlining 7 key objectives: (1) protecting children in AI services, (2) strengthening communities and small businesses through AI development, (3) safeguarding American creators from AI-generated content infringement, (4) defending free speech and First Amendment protections against AI censorship, (5) leading global AI innovation by removing barriers and ensuring access to testing environments, (6) ensuring American workers benefit from AI-driven growth through skills training and job creation, and (7) establishing a federal AI policy framework to protect rights and support innovation while preventing a fragmented state regulation landscape.

Public Sector & Governance
Framework
Strategy
US AI Action Plan (2025):
The US White Office has unveiled the US AI Action Plan in accordance with President Trump’s January executive order on Removing Barriers to American Leadership in AI. The Plan identifies over 90 Federal policy actions across three pillars – Accelerating Innovation, Building American AI Infrastructure, and Leading in International Diplomacy and Security – that the Trump Administration will take in the coming weeks and months. Key policies in the AI Action Plan include: (1) Exporting American AI: The Commerce and State Departments will partner with industry to deliver secure, full-stack AI export packages – including hardware, models, software, applications, and standards – to America’s friends and allies around the world; (2) Promoting Rapid Buildout of Data Centers: Expediting and modernizing permits for data centers and semiconductor fabs, as well as creating new national initiatives to increase high-demand occupations like electricians and HVAC technicians; (3) Enabling Innovation and Adoption: Removing onerous Federal regulations that hinder AI development and deployment, and seek private sector input on rules to remove; and (4) Upholding Free Speech in Frontier Models: Updating Federal procurement guidelines to ensure that the government only contracts with frontier large language model developers who ensure that their systems are objective and free from top-down ideological bias.

National Strategy
NIST Guidelines on Adversarial Machine Learning - A Taxonomy and Terminology of Attacks and Mitigations (NIST AI 100-2 E2025):
This NIST Trustworthy and Responsible AI report provides a taxonomy of concepts and defines terminology in the field of adversarial machine learning (AML). The taxonomy is arranged in a conceptual hierarchy that includes key types of ML methods, life cycle stages of attack, and attacker goals, objectives, capabilities, and knowledge. This report also identifies current challenges in the life cycle of AI systems and describes corresponding methods for mitigating and managing the consequences of those attacks. The terminology used in this report is consistent with the literature on AML and is complemented by a glossary of key terms associated with the security of AI systems. Taken together, the taxonomy and terminology are meant to inform other standards and future practice guides for assessing and managing the security of AI systems by establishing a common language for the rapidly developing AML landscape.

Cybersecurity
NIST Guidelines for Evaluating Differential Privacy Guarantees (NIST SP 800-226):
The US National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) has published its finalised Guidelines for Evaluating ‘Differential Privacy’ Guarantees to De-Identify Data (NIST Special Publication 800-226). Differential privacy works by adding random "noise" to the data in a way that obscures the identity of the individuals but keeps the database useful overall as a source of statistical information. However, noise applied in the wrong way can jeopardise privacy or render the data less useful. These guidelines aim to help practitioners of all backgrounds better understand how to think about differentially private software solutions. Multiple factors for consideration are identified in a differential privacy pyramid along with several privacy hazards, which are common pitfalls that arise as the mathematical framework of differential privacy is realised in practice.

Data Privacy & Protection
[TOOLKIT] Dioptra:
Dioptra is a software test platform (developed by the NIST) for assessing the trustworthy characteristics of artificial intelligence (AI). Trustworthy AI is: valid and reliable, safe, secure and resilient, accountable and transparent, explainable and interpretable, privacy-enhanced, and fair - with harmful bias managed. Dioptra supports the Measure function of the NIST AI Risk Management Framework by providing functionality to assess, analyze, and track identified AI risks. Dioptra provides a REST API, which can be controlled via an intuitive web interface, a Python client, or any REST client library of the user's choice for designing, managing, executing, and tracking experiments.

Sandbox
Data Privacy & Protection
Cybersecurity
NIST Guidelines on Managing Misuse Risk for Dual-Use Foundation Models (NIST AI 800-1):
This guidance helps developers mitigate the risks stemming from generative AI and dual use foundation models. The guidance includes 7 objectives and practices to manage misuse risks: (1) Anticipate potential misuse risk, (2) Establish plans for managing misuse risk, (3) Manage the risks of model theft, (4) Measure the risk of misuse, (5) Ensure that misuse risk is managed before deploying foundation models, (6) Collect and respond to information about misuse after deployment, and (7) Provide appropriate transparency about misuse risk. Other key points from the guidance include (1) identifying and categorizing different types of adversarial attacks, (2) providing metrics for assessing the impact of these attacks on AI performance, (3) offering best practices for mitigating vulnerabilities, and (4) establishing a standardized framework for testing and improving AI system resilience.

Generative AI
Cybersecurity
Copyright & IP
NIST AI Risk Management Framework - Generative AI Profile (NIST AI 600-1):
This document focuses on generative AI and builds upon the NIST's existing AI Risk Management Framework (AI RMF). The document details 12 risks and 400 actions for mitigation. The document uses the concept of "profiles" to allow organizations to tailor their specific use cases, sectors, or applications to their unique requirements, risk tolerances, and resources.

Cybersecurity
Data Privacy & Protection
Advancing Governance, Innovation, and Risk Management for Agency Use of Artificial Intelligence (2024):
This is a government wide policy issued by the White House Office of Management and Budget (OMB) which directs federal agencies: (1) to implement concrete safeguards around AI; (2) to improve public transparency in their use of AI; and (3) to designate Chief AI Officers, establish AI governance boards. The OMB will also remove unnecessary barriers to responsible AI innovation; issue a request for information on responsible procurement of AI in government; and direct agencies to expand and upskill their AI talent (including a commitment from the Biden Administration to hire 100 AI professionals by summer 2024).

Generative AI
Data Privacy & Protection
Bipartisan Framework on AI Legislation (2023):
Introduced by Senators Richard Blumenthal and Josh Hawley, this framework provides a blueprint for an 'US AI Act'. It proposes (1) a licensing regime for companies developing sophisticated general-purpose or models used in high-risk situations; (2) an independent oversight body to oversee the licensing regime and monitor compliance; (3) section 230 of the Communications Decency Act, which provides legal protections to tech firms for third party content, does not extend to AI applications, (4) various transparency obligations (especially around training data and model accuracy); and (5) other controls and protections on AI in the context of consumer and child safety, and national safety.

[REPEALED] Ensuring Safe, Secure and Trustworthy AI (2023):
This document sets out 8 voluntary committments by participating tech companies to the White House. These voluntary commitments are only a first step in developing and enforcing binding obligations to ensure safety, security, and trust in AI.

Cybersecurity
SAFE Innovation Framework for AI (2023):
Introduced by Senator Chuck Schumer, this framework proposes a framework for AI innovation based on the following principles: (1) Security, (2) Accountability, (3) Foundations and (4) Explainability.

Cybersecurity
Data Privacy & Protection
NIST AI Risk Management Framework (NIST AI 100-1):
The National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) (under the US Department of Commerce) has developed a framework to better manage risks to individuals, organizations, and society associated with AI. The NIST AI Risk Management Framework (AI RMF) is intended for voluntary use and to improve the ability to incorporate trustworthiness considerations into the design, development, use, and evaluation of AI products, services, and systems.

Generative AI
Data Privacy & Protection
Cybersecurity
[REPEALED] Blueprint for an AI Bill of Rights (2022):
The blueprint identifies 5 voluntary principles to guide the design and use of 'automated systems': (1) protection from unsafe and ineffective systemns, (2) protection from algorithmic discrimination, (3) data privacy protection, (4) provisions for notice and explanation, and (5) provisions for human alternatives. While the blueprint is not hard law, it has potential to influence legislation and regulation.

Further Reading
US state-by-state AI legislation snapshot (BCLP):
An interactive map that actively tracks the proposed, failed and enacted AI regulatory bills from across the United States. This tracker includes laws addressing automated decision-making (noting that not all automated decision-making systems involve AI) but omits biometric data, facial recognition, and sector-specific administrative laws.

Data Privacy & Protection
Compute in America: Building the Next Generation of AI Infrastructure at Home (10 June 2024):
A comprehensive 3-part series exploring the policy changes needed to ensure that AGI is invented in the USA and deployed through American data centres. It covers (1) how to build an AI data centre; (2) how to build the future of AI in the US; and (3) a policy playbook for 5 GW clusters in 5 years.

Infrastructure & Hardware
US AI Regulation simplified (30 March 2024):
A quick overview of the US AI regulatory landscape and structural factors behind its fragmented state.

Public Sector & Governance
Digital Replica Bill May Leave Performers Worse Off (2 January 2024):
A comprehensive critique of the NO FAKES Bill, arguing that the bill may undermine performers' control over their intellectual property rights.
